1201 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sitka


Nos. 4215, 4677


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 342; 527 A.2d 265; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 983


February 10, 1987, Argued  
June 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in the first case charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number sixteen, and tried to the jury before Doyle, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Information in the second case charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, and presented on a plea of guilty to the court, O'Connor, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review, based on an contention of unconstitutionality, of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a (Rev. to 1983), as amended by 1983 Conn. Pub. Acts No. 83-534, pursuant to a conditional guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a (Rev. to 1983), as amended by 1983 Conn. Pub. Acts No. 83-534. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Act under which the statute was derived. Defendant entered a conditional guilty plea to the charge, reserving the right to challenge the trial court's subject matter jurisdiction. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that there was no constitutional restriction affecting how 1983 Conn. Pub. Acts No. 83-534 was passed by the legislature; thus, the law was constitutional. Courts were not authorized to pass upon the regularity of legislative proceedings. Pursuant to Conn. Const. art. III, § 13 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-1a, each house was authorized to determine the rules of its own proceedings and no constitutional restrictions were involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor.

 

1202 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cristofaro v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 4725


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 260; 527 A.2d 255; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 973


March 11, 1987, Argued  
June 16, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the defendant denying the plaintiff's subdivision application, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought to subdivide certain property. Defendant planning and zoning commission denied the application because the proposed lots were not at least one acre as required by subdivision regulations. The landowner appealed to the Superior Court (Connecticut), where the commission's action was upheld and the appeal dismissed. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought to subdivide certain property. The applicable zoning ordinance required each proposed lot to contain at least 30,000 square feet. Although the lots met this requirement, they did not have access to public sewer and water. The subdivision regulations required such lots to contain a minimum of one acre. The landowner argued that the planning and zoning commission, acting in its capacity as a planning commission, had no authority to enact and apply a subdivision regulation that required a larger minimum lot size than that set by the applicable zoning regulations. Affirming the rejection of the landowner's application, the court held that the landowner could not challenge the validity of the regulations in an action in which he had sought to take advantage of them. Rather, he was required to challenge them in a declaratory judgment action. The court applied the same rule applicable to zoning ordinances, although this was a subdivision ordinance, because like zoning regulations, the subdivision regulations were applied generally to the entire municipality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court affirming the rejection of the landowner's subdivision application.

 

1203 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sullivan


No. 3013


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 80; 525 A.2d 1353; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 938


January 8, 1987, Argued  
May 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the fourth degree and risk of injury to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before A. Aronson, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a minor, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him after a jury trial of risk of injury to a minor, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Three witnesses testified that they saw defendant encouraging a four-year-old child to touch his penis. The court upheld defendant's conviction. Although the trial court erred in failing to observe a sequestration order, defendant had not shown prejudice because a witness testified at a pretrial motion to dismiss. Thus, defendant could have exposed any fashioning of the witness' testimony to correspond to that of another witness. However, the inconsistencies were wholly explainable by reference to factors other than the order of their testimony. An amendment to the information was not substantive but merely charged two methods of committing the same crime and was thus properly permitted. The information, fairly read, charged defendant with conduct that was likely to impair the victim's morals, not with actually impairing the victim's morals, which was not within the proscription of § 53-21. Although the trial court gave the jury an erroneous burden of proof for the process of drawing inferences from circumstantial evidence, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by it because the jury did not actually draw the critical inference from circumstantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

1204 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKenna


No. 3728


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 122; 525 A.2d 1374; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 940


December 4, 1986, Argued  
May 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Jackaway, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area No. 12, which convicted him after a jury trial of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle while intoxicated, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56b(a). Defendant's motion for reargument was denied. Considerable direct evidence was offered at trial regarding defendant's intoxication at the accident scene.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to find that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56b was void for vagueness; in charging the jury on "intoxication;" (3) in admitting results of an intoximeter test; and (4) in admitting certain photographs of the victim. Defendant claimed that the statute failed to adequately define the prohibited conduct as it did not define "intoxication." The court held that § 53a-56b was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, whose conduct was clearly proscribed under any interpretation of the term. Nor was defendant denied due process by the jury instruction on intoxication. The instruction given, despite its similarity to instructions allegedly defining "under the influence," was substantially similar to the definition approved by the Connecticut Supreme Court. While the trial court erred in instructing the jury regarding inferences to be drawn from the evidence, the error did not warrant reversal as the direct evidence on the issue of intoxication was substantial. Defendant failed to preserve the admissibility of the intoximeter test. Finally, the court found no abuse of discretion in the ruling admitting the challenged photographs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the crime of manslaughter in the second degree.

 

1205 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wylie


No. 4235


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 683; 525 A.2d 528; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 931


December 2, 1986, Argued  
May 12, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and possession of a pistol, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six and tried to the jury before McDonald, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of carrying a pistol without a permit, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), defendant was found guilty of guilty of carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant appealed the conviction on the ground that the trial court erred in denying his motions to suppress evidence and a statement he made at the time he was detained.


OVERVIEW: A market clerk saw that defendant was carrying a gun. The clerk told a police officer who was in the market about the gun. The officer immediately left the market, and saw defendant walking quickly across the street. When defendant turned and saw the officer, he began to run. The officer stopped defendant and held him at gunpoint. A backup officer searched defendant, found live rounds in his pants pocket, and found the gun 20 feet from where defendant was stopped. At the time he was apprehended, defendant stated that he thought carrying a gun was alright as long as it was not loaded. Defendant argued that the officer lacked an articulable suspicion to support the initial detention, and that his statement was inadmissible because he was in custody and the officers failed to give him Miranda warnings. The conviction was affirmed. The court held that defendant's initial detention and the search were justified. The circumstances surrounding the stop and frisk constituted specific and articulable facts which, taken together with rational inferences from those facts, reasonably warranted the intrusion. The court also found that defendant's statement was spontaneous and voluntary.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for carrying a pistol without a permit was affirmed.

 

1206 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simmons


No. 5165


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 561; 524 A.2d 669; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 913


February 11, 1987, Argued  
April 28, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation, possession of narcotics by a person who is not drug dependent, and possession of less than four ounces of a controlled substance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was presented on a plea of nolo contendere to the court, which rendered judgment of guilty of possession of narcotics and of violation of probation, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Fourteen (Connecticut) that convicted him of various drug possession charges after he entered a plea of no contest. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motions to suppress and for a hearing to challenge the truthfulness of a warrant.


OVERVIEW: The police obtained a search warrant for defendant's home, person and car to search for drugs and contraband. The police executed the warrant and found drugs in defendant's home. Defendant initially pled not guilty and filed a motion to suppress the evidence and then moved for a Franks hearing to challenge the veracity of the affidavits supporting the warrant application. The trial court denied the hearing. On review, defendant argued that he was entitled to the hearing and that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-33f he had a right to present evidence on the issue of probable cause. The court rejected the arguments, finding that defendant merely made allegations and had not made the requisite showing of deliberate falsehood or of reckless disregard for the truth, and an offer of proof. The court refused to adopt the probable cause standard of § 54-33f because it would create a new rule of law that would mandate a hearing every time a defendant made an allegation of untruthfulness in an affidavit. The court found that such a rule would be contrary to the sensible threshold test.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

1207 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williamson


No. 4763


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 532; 524 A.2d 655; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 910


December 4, 1986, Argued  
April 21, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, possession of cocaine with intent to sell, possession of marihuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, carrying a dangerous weapon, carrying a pistol without a permit and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Murray, J., granted the defendant's motions to suppress and to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, and the state, with the permission of the trial court appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted the motion of defendant charged with drug and weapons offenses in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-277(a), 21a-279c, 53-206, 29-35, 53a-167a to suppress and dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The state claimed that the trial court erred in concluding that the state had violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights when defendant was stopped and arrested after running into a restaurant while an police officer called for him to stop. Before defendant ran, there was nothing to indicate that he and his companions were engaging in any illegal behavior. The court set aside and remanded, holding that (1) the trial court erroneously concluded that the investigatory operation was illegal in design; (2) while the police had no more than a generalized suspicion of illegal conduct when they approached the restaurant, that suspicion became specific and focused on defendant when he ran into the restaurant in response to warnings that police had arrived; (3) the facts available to the police officer at the time of the pursuit were sufficient to justify a Terry investigative stop; and (4) the facts found by the trial court fully supported the conclusion, as a matter of law, that probable cause existed to believe that defendant illegally possessed narcotics and that he carried a pistol.


OUTCOME: The court set aside and remanded the judgment granting defendant's motion to suppress and dismiss with directions to deny defendant's motion, where defendant was convicted of drug and weapons offenses.

 

1208 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dullivan


No. 4878


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 474; 523 A.2d 1353; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 902


January 6, 1987, Argued  
April 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence was insufficient to uphold the verdict. The court found that the jury could have reasonably concluded that defendant's display of a gun while accompanied by another man, coupled with defendant's request to "see" the lone victim's radio, was sufficient to conclude that through the use or threat of force defendant committed a robbery rather than a larceny. The court, however, found error in the trial court's instruction on circumstantial evidence because it unconstitutionally diluted the State's burden of proving every element of the crime charged beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that the instruction allowed the jury to infer that defendant intended to communicate a threat by an erroneous "more probable than not" standard. While the court found that the evidence tending to prove that defendant threatened the victim with the use of force by displaying a gun was sufficient, the court concluded that the evidence was not so overwhelming that it rendered the instruction error harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's jury instruction. The court set aside the judgment and remanded the action for a new trial.

 

1209 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


In re Carl O.


Nos. 4578, 4579


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 428; 523 A.2d 1339; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 896


January 15, 1987, Argued  
April 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and youth services alleging a certain minor child to be neglected and uncared for, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters at New Haven, and tried to the court, Brenneman, J.; judgment committing the child to the custody of the commissioner for a period not to exceed eighteen months, from which the respondents filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a mother and father, appealed from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered a judgment committing their child to the custody of petitioner, the commissioner of the department of children and youth services (DCYS) for a period not to exceed eighteen months pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 46b-129(a).


OVERVIEW: Respondents appealed from a judgment of the trial court committing their child to the commissioner of the department of children and youth services (DCYS) for a period not to exceed eighteen months. DCYS filed a petition pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 46b-129 (a) alleging the child to be neglected and uncared for. On appeal, respondents claimed that the trial court erred (1) in granting and confirming the order of temporary custody, (2) in holding that the child was "homeless," (3) in holding that the child had "special needs," (4) in denying the mother's motion to enforce rights, (5) in granting DCYS's motion to amend, (6) in interpreting §§ 46b-129 and 46b-120 in a manner that was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, (7) in refusing to find that § 46b-129 was in violation of the due process clauses of the United States and Connecticut constitutions, and (8) in rendering a judgment of commitment where such decision was not supported by the evidence. The court rejected all of the arguments on appeal and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which committed petitioners' child to the custody of the commissioner.

 

1210 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hyslop


No. 3627


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 457; 523 A.2d 1350; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 899


February 5, 1987, Argued  
April 14, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: The victim was attacked one evening while she was walking along the highway. Her description of her assailant resulted in a composite picture that proved to be a remarkable likeness of defendant. The victim identified defendant from the third photo array that she was shown. His picture was not in the first two arrays. The police took the victim to the parking lot of defendant's employer, where she identified him exiting a van. Defendant challenged her out-of-court identification as impressively suggestive. The trial court denied his motion to suppress the identification. Because the testimony was conflicting as to whether the officers stopped talking when defendant's van arrived, the issue of credibility was for the trial court to determine. Finding no clear error, the court held that the evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that the identification procedure, while suggestive, was not impermissibly so. The court also found no error in the trial court's admitting evidence of defendant's flight. The State was not required to show that he had actual knowledge that he was wanted by the police to introduce evidence that he ran from his home when officers arrived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sexual assault in the first degree.

 

1211 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Floyd


No. 4115


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 361; 523 A.2d 1323; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 887


December 10, 1986, Argued  
April 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the first degree and arson in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Norcott, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of using a motor vehicle without permission and arson in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted defendant of arson in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-113(a) and of using a motor vehicle without the owner's permission in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119b(a)(1). Defendant appealed the convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of setting fire to a car that belonged to his live-in companion's brother. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motions for a mistrial based on an improper summation by the prosecutor. Holding that the prosecutor's comments did not deny defendant a fair trial, the court affirmed the conviction. The prosecutor's references in closing argument to her personal ethics were improper when viewed in isolation, but were invited by defense counsel's accusation that the prosecutor was unethical. Further, the prosecutor's mention of the Fifth Amendment in closing was clearly a reference to the burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt and was not an improper comment on defendant's failure to testify. Finally, the complainant's testimony that she believed that the car was equipped with an anti-theft device, and thus could not be used without a key, was admissible even though it was based solely on the fact that her brother told her it was so equipped. The testimony was not hearsay because it was not offered to establish the truth of the matters contained therein.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error in defendant's conviction.

 

1212 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perez


No. 4548


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 279; 523 A.2d 508; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 880


December 11, 1986, Argued  
March 31, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of burglary in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdict and jugment of guilty; thereafter, the state filed a supplemental information charging the defendant with the crime of being a persistent serious felony offender and, following a plea of guilty, the court rendered judgment of guilty, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted of burglary in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-103 and sentenced defendant as a persistent serious felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-40(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-103 and with being a persistent serious felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-40 (b). On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court violated his state and federal rights to due process when it improperly charged the jury on circumstantial evidence, inferences and burden of proof, thereby impermissibly diluting the state's burden of proof. The central issue on appeal involved the trial court's instruction to the jurors that they could draw inferences from circumstantial evidence. The court concluded that the instructions given in the case diluted the state's burden of proving guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and were therefore erroneous. However, the court affirmed the conviction finding that the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1213 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Dubno v. Falsey


Nos. 3394, 3395


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 95; 521 A.2d 1044; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 862


January 13, 1987, Argued  
March 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in the first case, by the plaintiff commissioner from an order of the Probate Court for the District of New Haven directing, inter alia, that the department of revenue services recompute the succession tax on a marital trust established by the defendants' decedent, and appeal, in the second case, by the plaintiff executors from the determination in the same probate order that the assets of the marital trust were taxable in the estate of the plaintiffs' decedent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and referred to Hon. Raymond J. Devlin, state trial referee; judgment sustaining, in part, the commissioner's appeal in the first case, and judgment dismissing the executors' appeal in the second case, from which the defendant executors in the first case and the plaintiff executors in the second case appealed to this court.

The defendants in the first case and the plaintiffs in the second case filed motions for reargument which were denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the executors of the estates of a husband and wife, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which found that the marital trust assets were includible in the estate of the husband and affirmed a probate court's finding that the assets of the marital trust were taxable in the estate of the wife, the donee of the power of appointment.


OVERVIEW: The husband died and was survived by his wife and their two children. The husband's will established a marital trust for the wife's benefit, and gave her a general power of appointment exercisable by her will over the residue of the trust assets. If the power were not exercised, his will provided that the assets would go to their children. The wife exercised the power in favor of the children in her will. The wife subsequently died. The husband's estate paid the succession tax on the entire value of the trust assets. Upon the death of the wife, the husband's executor's sought a recomputation of the succession tax. The tax was recomputed, based on the then certain fact that the assets had passed to the husband's children. The probate court found that the assets of the marital trust were taxable in the estate of the wife, the donee of the power of appointment. The trial court affirmed that finding and also found that the marital trust assets were includible in the estate of the husband, and that interest was due on the overpayment at the rate of four percent per annum. The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal because the transfer of such assets was taxable in both estates.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1214 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Douglas


Nos. 3989, 4182


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 103; 522 A.2d 302; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 863


December 10, 1986, Argued  
March 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging each defendant with the crimes of attempted robbery in the first degree, and aiding in assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of judgments of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted them of attempted robbery in the first degree and aiding in an assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendants and two others were charged with the same crimes. One of the other men was acquitted and all of the State's witnesses in his trial testified at defendants' trial. Defendants claimed that the trial court erred in failing to order the State to produce the transcripts of the witnesses' testimony in the trial that ended in acquittal. The court held that defendants' constitutional rights of confrontation were violated by the trial court's refusal to conduct an in camera examination to determine if the transcripts in the trial that ended in acquittal contained material inconsistent statements of the witnesses sufficient to have affected the outcome of defendants' trials. Defendants' rights of confrontation outweighed the statute that required erasure of records after acquittal. The court remanded the case for an inspection to determine what, if any, of the prior testimony should be made available to defendants to preserve their constitutional rights. Also, there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's failure to sever defendants' trials because there was no showing of manifest prejudice or substantial injustice.


OUTCOME: The court set aside defendants' judgments of conviction and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1215 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Addessi v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


No. 4664


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 86; 521 A.2d 605; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 847


January 7, 1987, Argued  
March 3, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Stodolink, J., granted the named defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) that granted defendant power company's motion for summary judgment, in the injured party's action for damages for personal injury sustained on the power company's property. The trial court's grant of summary judgment was premised upon its finding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557g was not unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The injured party argued that § 52-557g, which provided that land owners that made their property available to the public free of charge for recreational purposes owed no duty of care to the public, was unconstitutionally vague because it did not require the land owner to post on the property a notice that it was shielded from liability. The court rejected this argument because it did not attack the language of the statute. Specifically, the court noted that the injured party did not claim that the language would not permit a reasonable person of ordinary intelligence to know what was permitted or prohibited under the statute. The court concluded that, while the legislature could have required the type of posting suggested by the injured party, its failure to do so did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague, where the language was clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the power company's motion for summary judgment.

 

1216 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hanson v. Department of Income Maintenance


No. 4662


Appellate Court of Connecticut


10 Conn. App. 14; 521 A.2d 208; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 836


December 2, 1986, Argued  
February 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant determining that the plaintiff was ineligible for continued income assistance benefits, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Gaffney, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which dismissed her administrative appeal of a determination by defendant department of income maintenance that she was ineligible for income assistance because the claimant failed to comply with the time limitations under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(b).


OVERVIEW: On the 31st day after the department mailed the notice of its decision, the claimant initiated her appeal by mailing a copy of her petition to the department by certified mail. The department filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal because it was served more than 30 days after the notice was sent. The claimant argued that because the last day for service fell on a Sunday, when the United States postal service was not open to accept certified or registered mail, her service by certified mail on the next day was sufficient to satisfy the requirements of § 4-183(b). The court disagreed, noting that the right to appeal from an administrative decision was purely statutory and was accorded only if the conditions fixed by the statute were met. The time limitations under § 4-183(b) were not merely procedural limitations, but were essential parts of the remedy and were mandatory. Because the claimant did not strictly comply with § 4-183(b), the trial court lacked jurisdiction and her appeal was properly dismissed. The court declined to consider the claimant's equal protection challenge because it was not raised at the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the claimant's administrative appeal.

 

1217 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. McDonough


No. 4293


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 631; 521 A.2d 160; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 823


November 4, 1986, Argued  
February 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the third degree, sexual assault in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Licari, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of assault in the third degree, sexual assault in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: One night the victim met defendant, whom she had previously met while out dancing. Defendant invited the victim back to his apartment ostensibly to check on his pets and have a nightcap. After they spent a short time in the apartment defendant physically and sexually assaulted the victim. The victim suffered blows to her face and body, which caused bleeding and bruises. Defendant knocked the victim to the floor, straddled her legs, pinned her arms down, punched her in the face, and attempted to undress her. He refused to let her leave the apartment and threatened her life. The victim ultimately escaped. Defendant was convicted of assault in the third degree, sexual assault in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree. Defendant's major assertion on appeal was that the lower court erred in its charge to the jury on the use of circumstantial evidence in making inferences. The court found error in part, set aside the judgment, and remanded for a new trial. The court held that it was reasonably possible that the jury was misled by the lower court's explanations regarding the use of circumstantial evidence about the ultimate burden of proof borne by the State.


OUTCOME: The court found error in part, set aside the judgment, and remanded for a new trial.

 

1218 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kluttz


Nos. 3208, 3209


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 686; 521 A.2d 178; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 831


October 14, 1986, Argued  
February 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with seven counts of the crime of misconduct with a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Bingham, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of seven counts of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle, from which the state, on the granting of permission, and the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error, further proceedings on the state's appeal; no error on the defendant's appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) that convicted him of seven counts of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-222a, and the State appealed from the imposition of only one sentence on the guilty verdicts of seven counts of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on seven counts of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-222a. The lower court imposed only one sentence on the guilty verdicts of the seven counts. Defendant appealed his conviction on the ground that the lower court erred in submitting to the jury negligent homicide with a motor vehicle as a lesser included offense of misconduct with a motor vehicle. The state appealed the imposition of only one sentence on the seven counts. The court reversed on the sentence. The court held that where the charge of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle was required to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt, and where the four traditional requirements of the lesser included offense doctrine were met, the court properly designated negligent homicide with a motor vehicle as a lesser included offense of misconduct with a motor vehicle. Additionally, the court held that a vehicular homicide resulting in multiple deaths yielded multiple sentences.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing.

 

1219 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cubano


No. 4294


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 548; 520 A.2d 250; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 805


November 7, 1986, Argued  
February 3, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Barall, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), for robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred (1) in failing to grant a motion to suppress identification testimony, (2) in refusing to grant a request for an in-court lineup, and (3) in failing to dismiss the charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by failing to suppress all identification testimony that resulted from the roadside identification of him in a police car by a store customer who had observed defendant from the parking lot as he exited a building that had just been robbed. Although the customer's view of defendant was brief, his degree of attention was manifest in light of the fact that defendant was removing a stocking mask as he exited. The time interval between the view and the roadside identification was minimal and the certainty of the identification was positive. It was not error for the trial court to hold that the customer's identification was sufficiently reliable to warrant its admission into evidence. Also, because the in-court identification was not the product of an out-of-court confrontation "conducive to irreparable misidentification," due process did not mandate an in-court lineup as a matter of right. Finally, there was no merit in the claim that the charges should have been dropped because the warrantless arrest was illegal. The court pointed out that an illegal arrest affected evidentiary rulings but imposed no jurisdictional barrier to prosecution.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

St. John v. State


No. 4049


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 514; 520 A.2d 612; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 797


November 5, 1986, Argued  
January 27, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for specific performance of a contract for the sale of certain real property owned by the defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and referred to Julius B. Kuriansky, attorney state trial referee, who recommended that judgment be rendered in favor of the defendant; thereafter, the court, Lewis, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the referee's recommendation, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bidder appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), in favor of defendant state department of transportation for specific performance of an alleged contract made to buy property and for a declaratory judgment arising out of the solicitation of bids for the sale of that property.


OVERVIEW: The bidder had submitted a bid and a deposit to purchase the subject property. The department notified the bidder that his bid was the highest and that it would recommend to the State Properties Review Board that the sale of the property to the bidder be approved as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-80. The trial court specifically accepted a referee's conclusion that the failure of the Board to approve the sale was fatal to the bidder's case. On appeal, the court rejected the contention that the Board's alleged unreasonable delay in rejecting the sale of the property required a finding that the department had waived the requirement of approval by the Board. Because the Board rejected the sale of the property to the bidder for appropriate reasons, the court rejected the contention that the department failed to act in good faith in rejecting the bid. The court refused to review the claim that the department was estopped from not selling the property, which claim relied upon the affirmative actions of the department and the prior course of conduct between the parties. The estoppel claim had not been properly preserved.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the department and against the bidder, the court found no error.

 

1221 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Grievance Committee, Hartford-New Britain Judicial Dist. v. Goldfarb


No. 4421


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 464; 519 A.2d 624; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 785


October 8, 1986, Argued  
January 20, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment of the defendant on allegations of attorney misconduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, N. O'Neill, J.; judgment in favor of the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grievance committee sought review after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) denied its motion for leave to amend and held that the committee had failed to prove that defendant attorney had violated certain sections of the Code of Professional Responsibility in a proceeding that was initiated by presentment of the attorney pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 31.


OVERVIEW: The committee initiated a proceeding against the attorney by presentment of the attorney. The committee alleged improprieties with respect to the attorney's handling of a client's affairs. An assistant state's attorney, pursuant to § 31, represented the committee. On the day the trial was to begin, the committee sought to amend the complaint. The trial court denied the motion, apparently having concluded that the state's attorney could only prosecute the committee's complaint rather than present an attorney in its own right. The court set aside the judgment. Grievance committees performed a necessary and valuable function by providing the courts with able and competent experts to investigate and evaluate claims of attorney misconduct. That delegation of power, however, was not a deprivation of power. The Superior Court retained inherent and plenary power to regulate and discipline its officers. It was error for the trial court to have concluded that the grievance committee could diminish that power. The rules of court did not provide exclusive methods for conducting attorney discipline proceedings in the Superior Court.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1222 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Atherton


No. 4408


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 340; 518 A.2d 962; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1157


October 8, 1986, Submitted  
December 23, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical are a number three, and tried to the jury before Moraghan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury, Geographical Area Number Three (Connecticut), for two counts of sexual assault in the first degree. Among other claims, it was argued that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence the victim's out-of-court identification, and abused its discretion when it allowed direct examination of the victim in regard to prior sexual experience.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, defendant unsuccessfully moved to suppress evidence of a photographic array on the grounds that it was not reliable and that defendant's due process rights had been violated. On appeal, the court examined the State's exhibit A, which was the color photographic array at issue. The court found that the physiognomy of the seven persons photographed was remarkably similar. Even if the array was impermissibly suggestive, the victim's identification was sufficiently reliable to withstand challenge. The victim was able to closely observe defendant for over a minute while he walked with her along a lit sidewalk, and the victim was reasonably certain about her identification. It was error for the trial court to allow the introduction of the inherently prejudicial evidence of the victim's lack of prior sexual experience. However, defendant presented an alibi defense. Evidence of the victim's prior sexual relations could not have had any influence on the alibi defense. In the context of the overwhelming evidence of repeated sexual assaults, the court concluded that the one erroneous ruling was not sufficiently prejudicial to render it likely to affect the outcome of the case.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

State v. Walker


No. 4069


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 373; 519 A.2d 83; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1163


November 5, 1986, Argued  
December 23, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-143(a)(4) in connection with a bank robbery. Witnesses in the bank identified the robber's attire, and witnesses outside the bank also confirmed that defendant was wearing almost identical clothing to the robbery suspect immediately after the robbery. A jail witness testified that defendant disclosed that he could not be identified because he was completely covered. Defendant was convicted and appealed. Defendant challenged the trial court's jury instructions. The court held that the trial court's jury instruction on identity of defendant, and the use of circumstantial evidence in drawing inferences as to identity, was properly given in the charges concerning circumstantial evidence and were not given in relation to elements of the crime charged. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the trial court's failure to instruct on the definition of intent was not reversible error because defendant did not claim he did not have the requisite intent, but that he was not the perpetrator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

State v. Smith


No. 3727


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 330; 518 A.2d 956; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1156


September 16, 1986, Argued  
December 23, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, and with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and having a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Ford, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), where he was found guilty of two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, and with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and having a weapon in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a vehicle driven by another person. They got into a near collision with a taxi cab and an altercation ensured that involved defendant firing gunshots that caused injury to the taxi driver and passenger. Defendant and the driver were later apprehended by police and a firearm was found underneath the front seat of the car where defendant had been sitting. Defendant was tried and found guilty of two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59 (a)(1) and with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and having a weapon in a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35. Defendant appealed. On review, the court determined that a showing was required that no one in the vehicle had a proper permit to possess or carry such a weapon. Therefore, if the driver had a proper permit to carry a pistol, defendant could not have been properly convicted. The State failed to establish that the driver lacked a valid permit, and therefore failed to prove an essential element of the crime alleged against defendant. For this reason, that conviction on this count was set aside.


OUTCOME: The court found error in part, and the judgment was remanded and set aside as to the weapon in a motor vehicle count only but otherwise affirmed.

State v. Wright


No. 4186


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 275; 518 A.2d 658; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1175


October 17, 1986, Argued  
December 9, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Falsey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury, Connecticut, which convicted him of robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery in the first degree in a trial in which he alleged that the State's burden of proof was diluted and that the jury should have been instructed as to the reliability of identification testimony. The court affirmed the conviction by finding that special instructions on the reliability of identification testimony was not needed due to the consistency of the eyewitness' testimony. The charge as to the duty to prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt was proper. The court concluded that precedent showed that the "near certitude" language that defendant contended was needed as to the charge on the burden of proof was not required and that the charge did not encourage the jury to quantify the element finding process. The court also held that there was no need for defendant's requested charge on identification testimony because that testimony was not uncertain, unclear, or inconsistent. The court further found that defendant's claim of inconsistency as to his facial hair at the time of the robbery did not require more detailed instructions because the eyewitnesses were extensively cross-examined as to their ability to identify the robber.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree.

State v. Allen


No. 4100


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 169; 517 A.2d 1043; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1153


September 16, 1986, Argued  
November 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted murder, assault in the first degree, assault on a peace officer and having a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Curran, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of attempted murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a(a), 53a-49, of assault in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), of assault on a peace officer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c(a)(1), and of having a weapon in a motor vehicle under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the offenses with which he was charged in a substituted information in a trial in which he alleged that there had been prosecutorial misconduct and that the State should not have been allowed to reopen its case on the charge of having a weapon in a motor vehicle. The court affirmed those convictions, finding that allowing the State to reopen its case to fill the evidentiary deficiency as to the weapons charge after defendant's motion for an acquittal was denied was not an abuse of discretion because the proffered evidence related to the essential element of if defendant's pistol met § 29-38's definition of a weapon. The court also held that the prosecutorial misconduct as to the comments on the evidence during the State's closing arguments did not entitle defendant to any relief because there was evidence that the jury naturally and necessarily interpreted that argument as a comment on his failure to testify. The court further determined that defendant endorsed the curative instructions and that the record showed that the State only commented on the strength of its case and defendant's corresponding inability to cast doubt on that strength.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for attempted murder, for assault in the first degree, for assault on a peace officer, and for having a weapon in a motor vehicle.

State v. Augustine


No. 4036


Appellate Court of Connecticut


9 Conn. App. 74; 515 A.2d 1079; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1126


September 15, 1986, Argued  
October 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of injury or risk of injury to a minor and cruelty to persons, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Smith, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the risk of injury to her six-year old daughter in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut), conditioned defendant's release from pretrial custody upon her written promise to appear and the prohibition of contact between her and her daughter. Defendant was convicted and appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague, and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her conviction. The court rejected both arguments and held that there was sufficient evidence from which a jury could conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant hit her daughter with a shoe and caused extensive, serious, and severe bruising. Defendant also argued that her conviction could be set aside because the trial court abused its discretion when it set the particular conditions for her pretrial release. The court held that appellate review of a constitutional claim to pretrial release was not available after a conviction because the accused had no legal cognizable interest in the outcome of the appeal on that basis, absent the reasonable expectation or demonstrated probability that the same controversy involving the same defendant would recur. The court held that there was no such expectation or probability in the present case and that the issue was moot.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

State v. Nims

Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 631; 513 A.2d 1280; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1116


June 4, 1986, Argued  
August 26, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of burglary in the first degree, three counts of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, and one count of theft of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Mulvey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of burglary in the first degree, two counts of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, and one count of theft of a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), where he was found guilty of one count of burglary in the first degree, two counts of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, and one count of theft of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant were observed entering a attached garage carrying pillow cases. Defendant accosted people inside the house and fled, firing shots. Several people, including police officers, identified defendant after seeing him flee the scene. The co-defendant also testified against defendant, who was charged and found guilty on counts of burglary, attempted assault, reckless endangerment, and theft of a firearm. The jury charge, as a whole, fairly and correctly presented the case to the jury.

1230 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ames v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 3425


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 642; 514 A.2d 352; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1117; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,346


June 11, 1986, Argued  
August 26, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant retailer sought review of an order from the Superior Court, New London (Connecticut), which awarded damages to plaintiff in a product liability action. Plaintiff challenged an order refusing to charge the jury on her claim for punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a 14-year-old girl, filed a product liability action against the retailer after she was injured by a riding mower that had been sold by the retailer. The jury awarded damages to plaintiff. The retailer appealed and plaintiff filed a cross-appeal. Plaintiff contended that the trial court erred by failing to charge the jury on her claim for punitive damages. The court found that the retailer's failure to install a deadman's control on the lawnmower, when such devices were not universally accepted by the industry and were not required under applicable safety standards at the time the retailer's machine was distributed, and its reliance on the product manufacturer for safety testing did not rise to the level of reckless conduct. Without the required showing of recklessness, there was no basis for the jury to consider an award of punitive damages against the retailer. However, the court found that the retailer had a duty to adequately warn plaintiff of its failure to install a deadman's control on the lawnmower.


OUTCOME: The order awarding damages to plaintiff was affirmed. The order refusing to charge the jury on plaintiff's claim for punitive damages was affirmed.

State v. Newton


No. 3244


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 528; 513 A.2d 1261; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1106


May 2, 1986, Argued  
August 19, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a minor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Foti, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of both crimes, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) judgment that convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70 and risk of injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, arguing that the superior court erred in instructing the jury on the two types of conduct proscribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. §53-21 where he was charged with only one type.


OVERVIEW: Defendant committed a sexual act upon his girlfriend's nine-year old daughter and was charged with sexual assault in the first and risk of injury to a minor. Defendant was convicted of both charged offenses. He appealed, challenging the superior court's jury instructions. In setting aside defendant's conviction for the offense of risk of injury to a minor, the court concluded that because defendant was only charged with one of the two types of behavior proscribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, the superior court erred in instructing the jury on both types of proscribed conduct. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 proscribed (1) deliberate indifference to or the creation of situations that could harm a minor's moral or physical welfare and (2) acts directly perpetrated on the minor and injurious to her moral or physical well-being. Defendant was only charged with committing the latter, but from the very beginning of trial, the superior court invited the jury to consider both the charged and the uncharged portions of the statute. This created a reasonable possibility that the jury was misled by the superior court's instructions and mandated a new trial on this charge.


OUTCOME: There was error as to the risk of injury count only. The judgment finding the defendant guilty of risk of injury to a minor was set aside, and the case remanded for a new trial on that count.

State v. Elliott


No. 3219


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 566; 513 A.2d 1285; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1110


June 6, 1986, Argued  
August 19, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of burglary in the first degree and two counts of unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) finding him guilty of two counts of burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4) and two counts of unlawful restraint in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95(a). Points of error included issues surrounding defendant's identification and the increase of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: During investigation of a burglary in which two victims were tied up, the victims viewed photographic arrays. About four months later, one victim picked out defendant's photo and identified him in court. The other victim was unable to identify defendant from photos but identified him in court. The identification procedures were not unnecessarily suggestive or unreliable based on a totality of the circumstances. An expert's testimony about the dangers of misidentification was properly excluded. Reliability of eyewitness identification was common knowledge and the testimony would not have assisted the jury in resolving the issue. Three days after sentencing defendant, the trial court recalled and resentenced him. Because the original sentence was legal, the trial court could not correct it under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 935. After the sentence began, the trial court had no authority to modify it. Denial of defendant's motion for mistrial was not an abuse of discretion where defendant was presented with possibly exculpatory information at trial. He declined the trial court's offer of a continuance, effectively precluding inquiry into whether the information was exculpatory or not.


OUTCOME: The court found error in part. The judgment was set aside and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment as on file except that the original sentence imposed was to be reinstated.

 

1233 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 3764


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 578; 513 A.2d 758; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1111


June 11, 1986, Argued  
August 19, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor vehicle infraction complaint charging the defendant with violation of the department of motor vehicles regulation prohibiting the installation of the use of radar detecting devices, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the court, Barry, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Twelve (Connecticut), which found him guilty of violating Conn. Agencies Regs. § 14-137-1 by having a radar detector installed in his automobile.


OVERVIEW: A police officer testified that he observed a radar detector mounted on the dashboard of defendant's automobile, but that he did not know if there was a cord hanging from the device or how it was mounted on the dashboard. Defendant admitted to the officer that the device was a radar detector. Defendant moved to dismiss at the close of the State's case on the ground that there was no evidence that the device was installed or that he was the person who had installed it. The court held that the trial court's findings that the device was located on the dashboard in front of defendant, that he was aware of its presence, and that it was positioned in such a way that its purpose could be fulfilled encompassed each aspect of the offense of installation of a radar detector. The court noted that an administrative ruling had clarified the meaning of the term "installed" as used in Conn. Agencies Regs. § 14-137-1 by providing that the term referred to a device that was so affixed or situated that it was capable of being activated by the operator of a vehicle while driving. The court also held that the State was not required to show that defendant had personally installed the device.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

1234 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kitt


No. 2190


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 478; 513 A.2d 731; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1100


March 20, 1986, Argued  
August 12, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Upon Motion to Reargue Granted, Modified November 11, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Amended information charging the defendant with burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, larceny in the third degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Coppeto, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of each crime, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, larceny in the third degree, and conspiracy to commit larceny in the third degree. Defendant sought appellate review of his convictions.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err in denying his motion for a mistrial and in failing to give the jury a cautionary instruction after the State questioned a witness called by defendant to verify that he was validly asserting his Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The court held that the trial court erred in permitting an amendment of the information charging defendant with second-degree larceny to be superseded by a charge of third-degree larceny. The court held that the trial court's decision permitting the jury to be instructed as to third-degree larceny was an error that unconstitutionally deprived defendant of his rights to a fair trial and to adequate notice of the charges against him. The court therefore vacated defendant's conviction of third-degree larceny. The court further held, under the plain error rule, that defendant was improperly convicted of two counts of conspiracy arising out of a single agreement. The court set aside both conspiracy convictions, and remanded the case for the application of the trial court's discretion in determining which conspiracy was proved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary in the third degree. His conviction of and sentence for larceny in the third degree was vacated. The court remanded the case to the trial court for its discretionary decision as to which conspiracy conviction should be sustained and for the entry of a not guilty judgment as to the other conspiracy count.

 

1235 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wright


No. 3975


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 399; 513 A.2d 176; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1091


May 1, 1986, Argued  
August 5, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Kline, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of both crimes, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), for sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree. From the denial of his motion to set aside the verdict, defendant raised claims of error that addressed, among other areas, an out-of-court identification, and the failure to give an adverse inference jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the circumstances justified an immediate one-on-one viewing of defendant by the victim because the victim's family had appeared at defendant's residence to confront him. The situation was potentially volatile and the police were obliged to defuse it. Even if it had been found that the process was overly suggestive, the identifications were still admissible because they were reliable. The victim had a good and sufficient opportunity to view defendant at the time of the assault at close range and with adequate lighting. Defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction to the effect that an unfavorable inference could be drawn against the State for its failure to furnish the testimony of the boyfriend of the victim's daughter. The boyfriend was not shown to be a person the State would have naturally produced as one possessing superior or unique knowledge material to the case. As to the sufficiency of evidence challenge, the victim's testimony, which was believed by the jury, was sufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant compelled her to engage in sexual intercourse by use of force, and also that he robbed her of money and jewelry.


OUTCOME: No error was found.
