Zimny v. Cooper-Jarrett, Inc.


No. 3784


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 407; 513 A.2d 1235; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1092


April 2, 1986, Argued  
August 5, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries and the resulting death of the plaintiff's decedent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the action was withdrawn as against the named defendant et al.; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Aspell, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff against the defendant Thomas W. Hogan, Jr., only, from which the defendant Thomas W. Hogan, Jr., appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator brought an action to recover damages for personal injuries and the resulting death of decedent. Following a jury trial, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) entered judgment for the administrator. Defendant driver appealed.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was involved in a complicated multi-vehicle accident that occurred on an icy area of the interstate. While helping her mother exit her damaged car, decedent was struck by the driver's vehicle and received injuries that resulted in her death 45 days later. After the administrator settled with other defendants, the negligence case proceeded against the driver. Finding the driver negligent, the jury rendered a verdict for the administrator in an amount that reflected decedent's comparative negligence of 20 percent. Finding credible evidence from which the jury could reasonably have found that the driver was negligent and the proximate cause of the accident resulting in decedent's injuries and death, the court upheld the verdict. Because the rescue doctrine applied under Connecticut's comparative negligence statute, the administrator's recovery was not barred, but merely reduced, by decedent's negligence in attempting to rescue her mother. Moreover, the testimony of the administrator's expert was admissible. The amount of damages did not shock the court's sense of justice so as to compel the conclusion the jury was influenced by ignorance, partiality, prejudice, or corruption.


OUTCOME: Finding no error, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Crowther v. Gerber Garment Technology, Inc.

Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 254; 513 A.2d 144; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1073

July 29, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover sales commissions allegedly due from the defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Pickett, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff employee in an action brought by the employee to recover sales commissions, and the employee filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: After the termination of his employment, an employee brought an action against his employer for unpaid commissions. The trial court awarded double wages and attorney's fees to the employee, and the employer sought review. The court affirmed, holding that double wages were available to the employee under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-72, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by awarding double wages. Also, attorney's fees were available to the employee under § 31-72 within the discretion of the trial court. Further, the award of statutory attorney's fees under § 31-72 was properly taken into account when calculating the amount of recovery to be measured against the amount of the employee's pretrial offer of judgment. Finally, the court denied the employee's cross-appeal for attorney's fees incurred on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the employee.

Moll v. Gianetti


No. 3586


Appellate Court of Connecticut


8 Conn. App. 50; 510 A.2d 1009; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 1040


February 14, 1986, Argued  
June 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff mother for custody and support of the parties' minor child, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, F. Freedman, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which awarded plaintiff mother custody of a child, support of the child, and attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue presented was whether the trial court correctly awarded attorney's fees to the mother in connection with her action for custody and child support against the father of the parties' child. The father contended that the award of attorney's fees was excessive in light of the statutory criteria to be employed by the trial court for such awards. The court found that the trial court had before it evidence relating to those criteria, and additionally, in setting reasonable attorney's fees, testimony from the mother, corroborated and detailed by her counsel, regarding their fee arrangement, the hours devoted by counsel to this matter, and his hourly rate. Under the circumstances, the court did not conclude that the trial court abused its discretion in making its award of reasonable counsel fees in the amount of $ 5,200 based upon 52 hours of legal work at the reasonable hourly rate of $ 100. The financial criteria upon which the unquestioned award of support was based equally established the mother's entitlement to her award of counsel fees supported by the same statutory criteria.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error.

State v. Rodriguez


No. 2637


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 470; 509 A.2d 72; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 983


April 3, 1986, Argued  
May 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of hindering prosecution in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Gerety, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) of the offense of hindering prosecution in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-165(5), 53a-166.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction in the trial court of the offense of hindering prosecution in the first degree, and asserted that the trial court erred when it deprived him of a jury trial on the essential element of the crime when it informed the jury that defendant's friend had committed a murder, and in its denial of defendant's motion for acquittal. The court found error, and held that the trial court erred when it informed the jury that defendant's friend committed murder. The court noted that although defendant did not take exception to the trial court's charge as given, the error committed by the trial court was in such derogation of defendant's fundamental right to a fair trial that review was warranted without defendant's exception. The court noted that an essential element of the crime for which defendant was convicted was that he rendered criminal assistance to his friend when he concealed the shotgun used in a murder. The court held that the trial court's charge to the jury preempted the jury's fact-finding function, and directed a verdict on an essential element of the crime of hindering prosecution in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The court found error with defendant's conviction in the trial court.

State v. Liebowitz


Nos. 2740, 2741


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 403; 509 A.2d 43; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 978


February 7, 1986, Submitted  
May 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of illegal distribution of cocaine, and amended information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of illegal possession of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of illegal distribution of cocaine and illegal possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of illegal possession and illegal distribution of cocaine, he appealed. On appeal the court held that the trial court was not required to instruct the jury as to the statutory authorization of defendant to possess and distribute cocaine. The court stated that a statutory exception authorizing defendant to possess cocaine was not an essential element of the offense unless and until defendant introduced substantial evidence of the applicability of the exception to him. The only evidence presented, that defendant was a physician, was alone insufficient to establish that the statutory exception was an essential element of the offense. The court found that defendant was not deprived of the opportunity to prepare a defense strategy by the trial court's denial of his motion for a bill of particulars. The record indicated that defendant was adequately informed of the specific offenses and of the dates, times, and places where the offenses allegedly occurred. He was also given the identity of an informant and was permitted to test the cocaine given to an undercover officer. Therefore, he was not prejudiced by the denial of the bill of particulars.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Timmons


No. 3078


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 457; 509 A.2d 64; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 982


December 5, 1985, Argued  
May 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree from events surrounding the shooting of his ex-girlfriend's boyfriend. Defendant asserted several assignments of error. The court agreed with the State in that the trial court's denial of a probable cause hearing was harmless error because defendant was acquitted of murder and convicted of a lesser-included offense. The court reasoned that if a probable cause hearing had been held on the murder charge and no probable cause had been found, the State would still have been able to proceed on the lesser-included offense without a probable cause hearing. The court determined that the trial court did not err when if failed to charge the jury at defendant's request regarding defendant's flight from the scene. The court stated that the charge given was an accurate restatement of the law. The court concluded that the trial court did not err when it instructed the jury on defendant's statements to the police after he was read his Miranda rights and regarding his self-defense charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Baldwin


No. 3881


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 477; 509 A.2d 76; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 984


April 4, 1986, Argued  
May 20, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, possession of marihuana with intent to sell and possession of drug paraphernalia, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of cocaine, possession of marihuana and possession of drug paraphernalia, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of possession of cocaine, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-481 (a), possession of marihuana, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-481 (c), and possession of drug paraphernalia, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motions for judgment of acquittal and to set aside the verdict, since the state failed to produce sufficient evidence to establish guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, in its instructions to the jury regarding defendant's failure to testify, and in its instructions to the jury on intent. The court found that the jury could reasonably have concluded, upon the established facts and the inferences reasonably drawn therefrom, that the cumulative effect of the evidence established guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that the jury reasonably and logically could have reached the conclusion it did, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motions. The trial court's reference to defendant's failure to testify was made to emphasize the fact that, although the jury had the privilege and duty to draw inferences as to intent, it was precluded from using defendant's silence as a basis for such an inference. The trial court did not err when instructing the jury regarding defendant's failure to testify.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was the first selectman for a town. He also served as the town's superintendent of highways. DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of attempted sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of attempted sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-70. The record showed that the victim, a female, was returning home from college on a bus when she discovered that the bus terminal was closed. Defendant, who was standing outside the terminal, told the victim to follow him if she wanted to get a taxi. The victim was able to get away before anything further happened. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly denied is motion for a judgment of acquittal because, given the circumstances surrounding the incident, defendant's actions, and his graphic statement of purpose for apprehending the victim, the court concluded that the jury could reasonably have found defendant's intent was specifically to commit sexual assault in the first degree. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Burgos


No. 3252


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 265; 508 A.2d 795; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 958


February 10, 1986, Argued  
May 6, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of heroin with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, and presented to the court, Mack, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham (Connecticut), which convicted him of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a) by possessing heroin with the intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the possession of heroin with the intent to sell in a trial in which his motion to suppress was denied. The court affirmed that conviction, finding that there was adequate probable cause for a warrant to search defendant's home and that the premises to be searched was described with adequate particularity. The court reasoned that the warrant included a detailed description of the building in which defendant's apartment was located and that it directed the executing officer to the affidavit, which contained many references to defendant's apartment. The court also held that the fresh, first-hand information that the unlawful conduct earlier disclosed was still taking place at the premises clearly supplemented and revitalized the "stale" information that was included in the affidavit. The court further found that the warrant was timely executed because the delay between the warrant's issuance and the execution was within the period that was allowable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-33c and because the general nature of the drug trade and the manner in which defendant operated provided credible evidence that the illegal acts were of a continuing nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the possession of heroin with the intent to sell.

Genco v. Connecticut Light & Power Co.


No. 3937


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 164; 508 A.2d 58; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 942


December 13, 1985, Argued  
April 22, 1986, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff diver challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) granting summary judgment to defendant lake owner in the diver's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The diver was diving in a lake owned by the lake owner when she suffered injuries. The diver brought a personal injury action against the lake owner, and the lake owner filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted the motion, and the diver sought review. State v. Wiggins


No. 4022


Appellate Court of Connecticut


7 Conn. App. 95; 507 A.2d 518; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 931

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree, and information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Hale, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-134 (a)(2) and assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-60 (a)(2).


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial defendant was convicted of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-134 (a) (2), and assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-60 (a) (2). Defendant appealed from the judgment rendered thereafter, claiming that the trial court erred: (1) in denying defendant due process of law by allowing an in-court identification which was tainted by a prior impermissibly suggestive photographic identification; (2) in granting the state's motion for joinder and denying defendant's motions for severance; and (3) in denying defendant the right to a trial by jury by failing to disqualify a juror for allegedly sleeping during the trial. The court rejected all of defendant's arguments on appeal and affirmed the convictions. The court held that the manner in which the victim was shown the photographs was not impermissibly suggestive and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the motion for joinder nor in failing to disqualify a juror.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree in the first case, and with robbery in the third degree and assault in the third degree in the second case, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Mulvey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree in the first case and verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the third degree in the second case, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.

He also selected a picture of his assailant from a police photobook, and from a photoboard prepared by the police. The pictures selected were of defendant. The victim also made a positive in-court identification of defendant. In a second incident a female victim was attacked by defendant as she entered her car. He grabbed her purse and ran. The court held that the lower court's discussion of the evidence from which the jury alone could find facts did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Liberty Mobilehome Sales, Inc. v. Cassidy


Nos. 3996, 4198


Appellate Court of Connecticut


6 Conn. App. 723; 507 A.2d 499; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 921


February 10, 1986, Argued  
April 8, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in each case, to declare unconstitutional a certain ruling by the defendant department of consumer protection, and for other relief; the first case was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Barall, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant department of consumer protection and rendered judgment thereon; the second case was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Housing Session at Hartford, where the court, Goldstein, J., granted the named defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; from each judgment, the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a mobile home park owner, appealed decisions of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which dismissed its actions for a declaratory judgment on the ground that it failed to exhaust its administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The park owner disapproved the resale of mobile homes by defendant mobile home owners because the homes did not conform to a nationally recognized building and construction code. The home owners obtained rulings from defendant Department of Consumer Protection (DCP), which held that the failure to meet a nationally recognized building or construction code could not constitute a ground for disapproval unless such failure rendered the home unsafe or unsanitary. The park owner filed with DCP a motion for reconsideration and requested a hearing for the purpose of finding facts. DCP declined to do either. The park owner then filed actions with the trial court, which were dismissed because the park owner had not exhausted its administrative remedies. In affirming the trial court's decision, the court held that the park owner had not conformed to the requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176 to file a petition for a declaratory ruling and therefore failed to exhaust the proper administrative remedies. The court held that the park owner's requests for reconsideration did not constitute the petition for a declaratory ruling required by § 4-176.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Aspinall


No. 2886


Appellate Court of Connecticut


6 Conn. App. 546; 506 A.2d 1063; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 894


December 4, 1985, Argued  
March 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of selling cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of two counts of selling cocaine in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the court erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss because of the delay between the alleged commission of the crimes and the arrest. Defendant also claimed that the trial court erred in denying defendant's further motion to dismiss on the ground that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (a) and (b) violated defendant's state and federal constitutional rights of equal protection and due process of law. The court found that the delay caused no prejudice to defendant. To establish that a pre-arrest delay had caused a denial of the right to due process of law, defendant had to establish a specific showing of prejudice. The court also found that defendant was charged, tried, convicted, and sentenced under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (a) without reference at any time to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480 (b). The court could not find error in the trial court's conclusion that the statutes were not ambiguous as they pertained to the proscribed conduct, that defendant was provided fair warning, and that defendant's right to equal protection of the law was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error.

State v. Weber


No. 2072


Appellate Court of Connecticut


6 Conn. App. 407; 505 A.2d 1266; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 872


December 5, 1985, Argued  
March 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of breach of the peace, one count of interfering with an officer and one count of assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before W. Sullivan, J.; after the court granted the defendant's motion for acquittal as to one count of breach of the peace, verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of breach of the peace and interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered judgment upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of the crimes of breach of the peace, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181, and interfering with a police officer, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's car was ticketed for blocking a pedestrian walkway, and he was told to move it. Defendant, who was intoxicated, began screaming epithets at the officers who ticketed his car and ran after them with the intention of fighting with them. Defendant was placed under arrest and later convicted of breach of the peace and interfering with a police officer. Defendant sought review, and the court found no error. As to defendant's claim of error based on the trial judge's refusal to disqualify himself, the court held that it was precluded from considering the issue because at no time did defendant file a written motion to recuse, an affidavit setting forth factual allegations, or a certificate of good faith by counsel as mandated by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 997. The court denied defendant's free-speech argument and held that insulting or fighting words, which by their very utterance inflicted injury or tended to incite an immediate breach of the peace, were not protected speech. The court upheld the constitutionality of both Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Cretaro v. Equitec Real Estate Investors Fund XII

Lampasona v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 3810


Appellate Court of Connecticut


6 Conn. App. 237; 504 A.2d 554; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 839


November 13, 1985, Argued  
February 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of certain sections of the North Stonington zoning regulations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Walsh, J., upon stipulation of the parties, reserved the matter for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of certain sections of the city zoning regulations, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), upon the stipulation of plaintiff individual and defendant Planning and Zoning Commission of North Stonington, reserved the matter for the court's advice.


OVERVIEW: The individual owned a parcel of land in a rural residential zone. The parcel was nonconforming because it was smaller than the minimum lot size. The individual had a mobile home on the land, which replaced the first mobile home. While the first mobile home was on the property the commission enacted a regulation which prohibited the owner of a mobile home from making more than one replacement of the home. The individual applied for permission to replace her the second mobile home with a third mobile home of equal size, but the commission denied her request. The court held that by depriving the individual of the opportunity to replace her mobile home a second time, the town was depriving her of a vested property right in a nonconforming use without just compensation. The court noted the individual's nonconforming use of the property would not change with replacement of her second mobile home, merely the home would change. The court made the observation that the zoning regulations were written to seek the termination of a valid nonconforming use after a "grace period" of one mobile home replacement, and noted that under state law they had to fall.


OUTCOME: The court provided advice to the trial court which consisted of the finding that the zoning regulation in issue had to fail.

State v. Anderson


No. 3093


Appellate Court of Connecticut


6 Conn. App. 15; 502 A.2d 446; 1986 Conn. App. LEXIS 802


November 12, 1985, Argued  
January 7, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Meadow, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted on a jury verdict of guilty of the charge of third-degree sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a. At trial, defendant unsuccessfully sought to exclude evidence of prior convictions and to suppress of out-of-court identifications of him by the victim and a witness.


OVERVIEW: The victim was walking home from work and was confronted several times by a man driving a car. After following the victim, the man got out of his car and grabbed her breasts. Another man, who was driving by, saw the struggle, stopped, and approached the victim. The assailant then fled. The victim and the witness reported the incident to the police and identified defendant when he was arrested. At trial, the victim and the witness made in-court identifications of defendant, and the state introduced evidence of their out-of-court identifications. On review, the court found that the witness gave uncontroverted testimony that he identified defendant spontaneously as defendant entered the police station. Consequently, the identification was not tainted and defendant's due process rights were not violated by the admission of the evidence. As to the victim, the court found the show-up was unnecessary and suggestive, but based on the degree of certainty displayed by the victim and the length of time between the crime and the confrontation, the identification was reliable.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of third-degree sexual assault.

5 Conn. App. 649; 502 A.2d 933; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1216

December 24, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Covello, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.

The appellee-appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for the dissolution of a marriage, plaintiff wife appealed and defendant husband cross-appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which entered a judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief.


OVERVIEW: In an action for the dissolution of a marriage, the husband and the wife sought review from the judgment of the trial court. The trial court awarded joint custody of the parties' minor child to the parties, if the condition of behavioral modification of the husband were met in the future. The wife argued that it was error for the trial court to conclude that joint custody was in the best interests of the child. The court held that joint custody could not be an alternative to a sole custody award where neither party sought it and where no opportunity was given to the recalcitrant parent to embrace the concept. Further, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56a(b) contained no additional subsection providing for a procedure in the event neither parent sought joint custody. The court held that the trial court erred in awarding joint custody, subject to proof of the meeting of certain conditions by the husband, at a future time, absent an agreement by the parties, or absent a motion by one of them for conciliation after a motion had been made seeking joint custody.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was error in part; thus, the court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with directions to render judgment as on file, except that those portions of the judgment relating to joint custody and to orders concerning discipline and hygiene of the child as they related to the wife were to be omitted.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of robbery in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the denial of his midtrial discovery request amounted to a violation of due process of law, and that the denial of his motion for mistrial, based on an allegedly suggestive identification procedure, constituted reversible error. The court found that the fact that defendant had been denied access to evidence that might be only "arguably favorable" did not mean that his due process rights had been violated. After reviewing the record and defendant's broad claims of prejudice, the court could not conclude that his lack of access to the first photo array seen by the victim prejudiced him in any way or prevented him from obtaining a fair trial. The court also found that defendant's request for an evidentiary hearing was not made in the context of a challenge to the admissibility of the evidence of identification. Defendant failed to make a colorable claim that a substantial likelihood of misidentification existed and he must have also demonstrates the potential for substantial and irreparable prejudice to his case.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no error.

State v. Abbott


No. 3227


Appellate Court of Connecticut


5 Conn. App. 441; 499 A.2d 437; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1173


October 4, 1985, Argued  
November 5, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of hashish and possession of marihuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and presented to the court, Mulcahy, J., on a plea of nolo contendere on the possession of marihuana charge; after the possession of hashish charge was withdrawn, the court rendered judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Twelve (Connecticut), which had found him guilty of possession of marihuana in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction followed his conditional plea of nolo contendere, which was entered pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a, after the trial court had denied his motion to suppress evidence gathered pursuant to a search warrant, and had denied his motion to dismiss. Defendant challenged the warrant and the information contained in the underlying affidavit as unconstitutionally stale. He contended further that probable cause was lacking under the totality of circumstances test, and that the description of the place to be searched lacked constitutional particularity. The court affirmed. The confidential informant provided evidence that revitalized the information made within 90 days, bringing the earlier statements to date and removing any staleness. Applying the totality of the circumstances test, and reading the affidavit in a common sense manner, the court concluded that the affidavit passed muster in that it gave objective evidence of a fair probability that proscribed activity was occurring at the premises and that drugs were located there. The search of the entire premises, including defendant's bedroom, pursuant to the warrant, was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1260 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 2964


Appellate Court of Connecticut


5 Conn. App. 157; 497 A.2d 423; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1122


May 9, 1985, Argued  
September 3, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree and sexual assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, McGrath, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain statements; the matter was tried to the jury before Melville, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of manslaughter in the second degree. The trial court had denied defendant's motion to suppress certain statements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was given Miranda warnings. He then signed a notification form, which nowhere suggested the possibility of waiver of rights. Interrogation began immediately without any further discussion of waiver. Defendant was interviewed for a half-hour during which he made statements which were then reduced to writing. The actual writing consumed an additional 40 minutes. At the end of the process, defendant read and signed the document, after deleting a phrase. The trial court found that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his rights prior to the giving of his statement. The court disagreed and set aside the trial court's judgment. The court found that the record was devoid of any evidence that defendant understood his signature on the notification form represented his intentional relinquishment of a known right or privilege, and that the record disclosed no evidence of an affirmative act of waiver after Miranda warnings were read. The court noted that defendant was born, raised and educated to age 16 in Jamaica and had difficulty communicating with counsel and the court and that there was no indication that defendant was at all familiar with interrogation procedures.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the superior court's judgment and ordered a new trial.

In re David E.

Appellate Court of Connecticut

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), in favor of petitioner, the Commissioner of Children and Youth Services, and terminated the mother's parental rights with regard to her minor son.


OVERVIEW: The son and his siblings were removed from the mother's custody based on reported child abuse. Over the next seven years, numerous attempts to place the son back with his mother were unsuccessful, resulting in the Commissioner's petition. Based on testimony from a psychiatrist, a developmental evaluator, and the son's foster mother, the superior court found that the mother, by reason of continuing mental deficiency, had been unable to provide the son with the care necessary to his well being, and that the deficiency would continue for such time as would be detrimental to the son. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found the judgment legally correct and factually supported. The court held that testimony of a child psychologist as to the son's psychological and behavioral problems in the fault stage of the proceedings was relevant to the mother's ability to deal effectively with her child, but in any event, the other evidence was overwhelming. The court found that the Commissioner met the burden of proof under § 17-43a(b)(3), which met the Yoder criteria and satisfied constitutional due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court judgment.

State v. Bellamy


No. 2982


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 520; 495 A.2d 724; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1059


May 7, 1985, Argued  
July 23, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of harassment, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Gray, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and denied the state's motion for permission to appeal; thereafter, the Appellate Session of the Superior Court set aside the denial of the state's motion for permission to appeal and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut), which dismissed an information charging defendant with the crime of harassment in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183.


OVERVIEW: The dismissal was based on the lack of probable cause for the issuance of the warrant, the state's failure to prove a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183, and the conclusion that the alleged communications were protected free speech. On appeal, the state claimed that the court erred in each of these conclusions and that the information should be reinstated. The court agreed. The court noted that probable cause for a warrant required that the affidavit, read in a common sense manner, gave objective evidence of a fair probability that proscribed activity occurred. On this basis, the court concluded that the affidavit sufficiently established probable cause. The court also found that the superior court erred in dismissing the information, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56, for lack of evidence because the affidavit presented as the basis for probable cause was not intended and did not constitute the state's entire evidence. Finally, the court found that the superior court erred in concluding that the communications were protected free speech because the meager factual record precluded the superior court from making a proper decision on that constitutional basis.


OUTCOME: The court found error. The court set aside the judgment of the superior court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Nelson


No. 2788


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 514; 495 A.2d 298; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1057


May 8, 1985, Argued  
July 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the third degree and robbery in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Dupont, J.; judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the third degree and the lesser included offense of larceny in the fourth degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions for sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the third degree, and the lesser included offense of larceny in the fourth degree from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut). Defendant challenged the admission of the victim's in court identification of him.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a well-educated graduate student, was asleep in her bedroom in a prone position when she was awakened about 6:30 a.m. by someone lying on top of her. The ensuing sexual assault lasted approximately 20 minutes. Although the victim did not have her glasses on, she had a close look at her assailant and provided a detailed description. No out of court identification procedure was ever conducted, but 22 months after the assault, the victim identified defendant, the only black man in the courtroom, as her attacker. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that the in court identification was admissible. First, the court noted that there was no out of court procedure to taint the in court identification and that the defendant had the full opportunity to cross-examine the victim on the in court identification. The court stated that, even assuming arguendo that there was an issue, the identification was reliable under the totality of the circumstances test given the victim's opportunity to view her assailant and her detailed description.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1264 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wiley v. Lloyd


No. 3096


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 447; 495 A.2d 1082; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1043


May 7, 1985, Argued  
July 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from requiring the plaintiffs to disclose certain information prior to obtaining dissolutions of their marriages, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven where the court, Celotto, J., granted the defendant's motion to strike the complaint; thereafter, the court, Hadden, J., rendered judgment dismissing the action, from which the plaintiff Eleanor Theriault appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which dismissed their action to enjoin defendant state health commissioner from requiring the couple to disclose certain information prior to obtaining dissolution of their marriages.


OVERVIEW: One individual was a plaintiff in a martial dissolution action and claimed that the commissioner violated her constitutional rights by requiring her to provide the information requested in a "health from," which requested information regarding her race and that of her spouse, their respective educational backgrounds, number of prior marriages, and marital histories. The trial court granted the commissioner's request to strike the complaint due to a lack of standing. The trial court reasoned that the individuals had suffered no injury because the dissolution had been granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, but on different grounds. The court held that the allegations in the complaint were insufficient, as a matter of law, to overcome the bar of sovereign immunity. The court noted that the individual did not allege that the clerk had even asked for the health form to be completed or that her decree of dissolution was denied based upon her failure to complete that form. The court concluded that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to hear the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, on different grounds, the dismissal of the individuals' complaint.

Jack v. Scanlon


No. 3467


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 451; 495 A.2d 1084; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1044


May 9, 1985, Argued  
July 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries allegedly sustained as a result of the named defendant's negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before M. Hennessey, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court awarded the plaintiff double and punitive damages and the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which awarded plaintiff accident victim double and punitive damages pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-295. The victim had brought an action seeking compensatory damages for the injuries he suffered because of the driver's alleged negligence. The driver contended that § 14-205 was unconstitutional in allowing the double damage award.


OVERVIEW: In response to the victim's action for damages for his personal injuries resulting from the driver's alleged negligence in causing the motor vehicle accident, the court awarded the victim double and punitive damages under § 14-295. The driver sought review of the trial court's damage award and asserted that § 14-295 was unconstitutional because it lacked sufficient standards to guide the court's damage determination decision. The court on appeal affirmed the trial court's judgment based on its determination that (1) the trial court' s damage award determination was properly based on the driver's liability as authorized solely by § 14-295 and the court properly determined that increased damages were justified; (2) the court properly reviewed all of the circumstances of the accident in determining that defendant's conduct was culpable enough to assess the damages against him; and (3) defendant failed to meet his heavy burden of showing that § 14-295 did not provide adequate standards for its proper and consistent administration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1266 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fishman v. Middlesex Mut. Assurance Co.


No. 2218


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 339; 494 A.2d 606; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1029


March 12, 1985, Argued  
June 25, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Upon Reconsideration Affirmed August 6, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for an order to compel arbitration, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Ford, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.

The appellee-appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured filed an application with the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) for an order to compel arbitration under an insurance policy clause. The superior court granted summary judgment for the insured, from which defendant insurer appealed and the insured cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured alleged that her insurance policy with the insurer contained an arbitration provision and that the insurer had refused to arbitrate. The insurer argued that the superior court erred by refusing to dismiss the complaint on the basis of the lack of a recognizance. The insurer contended that the insured's complaint was a "civil action" that required a recognizance pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book §§ 51, 52, 53. The court found that because a proceeding under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-410 did not follow the pattern of an ordinary civil action, it could not be seen as a civil action for purposes of discovery and pleading. Therefore, the discovery process as set out in the Connecticut Practice Book was not applicable to proceedings under § 52-410. The court held that the insurer was not entitled to compliance with its discovery requests or a ruling on them before the insured's claim was adjudicated. However, the court concluded that in an action to compel arbitration under an insurance policy clause, the issue of coverage was an antecedent question for the court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the superior court erred by ordering that the issue of coverage be decided by arbitration. As to the other grounds of the insurer's appeal, the court found no error.

 

1267 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Blue Sky Bar, Inc. v. Stratford


No. 2883


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 261; 493 A.2d 908; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1011


March 15, 1985, Argued  
June 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from enforcing a certain town ordinance prohibiting vending on public or town property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Jacobson, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action commenced by plaintiffs, a corporation engaged in the business of selling ice cream from mobile vending trucks and two ice cream vendors, against defendant Town of Stratford, Connecticut, to enjoin the Town from enforcing an ordinance prohibiting vending from a motor vehicle, the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) rendered judgment for the Town. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Town's ordinance prohibited vending from a motor vehicle upon streets or public property within its limits. On appeal, plaintiffs contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in concluding the Town had had the statutory authority to pass the ordinance. The court affirmed. The court stated that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-37, which provided that a town might make reasonable ordinances with respect to vending upon its public streets, was not in conflict with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148 (c)(7)(H)(iv), which stated that any municipality had the power to prohibit and regulate the business of peddlers in a manner not inconsistent with the general statutes. The court concluded that the Town possessed the statutory authority to prohibit vending from motorized vehicles. The court further found that (1) the trial court did not err in finding that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the Town's police powers; and (2) the ordinance was not violative of the Due Process, Equal Protection, and Commerce Clauses of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the Town.

Russo v. East Hartford


No. 3030


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 271; 493 A.2d 914; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1012


March 5, 1985, Argued  
June 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged unconstitutional taking of the plaintiffs' property by inverse condemnation, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Spada, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) in favor of defendants, the town and its officials, in the landowners' action claiming an unconstitutional taking of private property by inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' property, which they purchased for use as a landfill, was condemned by the town and the landowners were awarded compensation in a prior proceeding. Before the condemnation took place, the legislature passed the Inland Wetlands and Water Courses Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. §§ 22a-36 through 22a-45, which classified the land as an inland wetland, and the town passed two zoning regulations, which required a permit for filling operations. The landowners did not apply for a permit and did not challenge the designation of their land as a wetland. In the current litigation, the landowners complained that these regulations so affected the value of their land from the date they were instituted until the date of condemnation as to amount to an unconstitutional taking. The trial court ruled in favor of the town and its officials. In affirming, the court held that the landowners could not seek what they had already unsuccessfully sought in the prior litigation, a higher price for their land. The court found no justification for an independent action, which sought, in essence, only to relitigate the issues of the prior suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the town and its officials.

Altholtz v. Connecticut Dental Com.


No. 2867


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 307; 493 A.2d 917; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1015


April 3, 1985, Argued  
June 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant commission suspending the plaintiff's dental license for one year, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which found no merit in his claims and dismissed his administrative appeal from a decision by defendant Connecticut Dental Commission to suspend his license to practice dentistry. The dentist contended that the Commission should not have relied on the reports of doctors who were not present.


OVERVIEW: The Commission alleged that the dentist had violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-114(2), (15) (Rev. 1979) by overbilling and rendering treatment in an unskillful manner. It issued a hearing notice ordering the dentist to appear and defend. The Commission retained two dentists to evaluate his work. At the hearing, both of their reports were introduced into evidence over the dentist's hearsay objection. The dentist acknowledged that the conclusions in the reports were correct regarding his billing and dental work, so the Commission suspended his dental license for two six-month periods. The dentist appealed, and the trial court dismissed his action. On appeal, the court held that the reports were made by dentists with no bias or interest in the case, were based on personal consultation and examination, and contained no facial inconsistency. Because they did not substantially prejudice the dentist, who failed to have the evaluating dentists subpoenaed, the court concluded that the reports were admissible. The court also held that the dentist had been given notice of the case against him and an opportunity to be heard by a fair and impartial body, so his due process rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court was correct in dismissing the dentist's appeal and found no error.

 

1270 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Gorman v. Waterbury


Nos. 2147, 2148


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 226; 493 A.2d 286; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 1017


March 14, 1985, Argued  
June 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from two decisions of the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district dismissing the plaintiffs' claims for workers' compensation benefits, brought to the compensation review division which affirmed the commissioner's decisions, and the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, widows of two former members of a police department, appealed a judgment of the Workers' Compensation Commissioner for the Fifth District which dismissed the widows' separate actions against defendant city, seeking workers' compensation benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c for the death of their husbands.


OVERVIEW: The widows, in separate actions, sought death benefits for their husbands under § 7-433c. The Commissioner denied their claims and the widows appealed. The court consolidated the appeals and held that the first widow was not entitled to benefits under § 7-433c because her husband died six years prior to the enactment of § 7-433c and it had no retroactive effect. Additionally, the newest enactment of § 7-433c did more than merely restate rights that had existed since 1959, it conferred benefits that had not already been established. The second widow argued that to qualify for benefits under § 7-433c, only the condition of hypertension or heart disease need be suffered while on duty or off duty by a regular member of a police department. The court found that § 7-433c provided that both the condition of hypertension or heart disease and the death resulting from the condition had to be suffered while the individual was on or off duty as a regular member of a police or fire department. Unlike a police officer on active status, the second widow's husband could not have been injured in the line of duty because he was retired; thus, he did not meet the eligibility requirements of § 7-433c.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Tucker v. Neighborhood Legal Services, Inc.

Appellate Court of Connecticut

June 4, 1985, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Housing Session at Hartford (Connecticut) that dismissed the lessor's action under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988 for deprivation of constitutional rights and attorney fees against defendants, a legal services company and former and current tenants. The trial court held that it lacked both subject matter and in personam jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The lessor's complaint alleged that Conn. Gen. On review, the court found that there was no allegation that any of the named defendants were state agencies or officials, and that the appearance of a legal services company in court on behalf of its clients, even if state funded, did not satisfy the requirement of state action under § 1983. 1272 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Candito


No. 2622


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 154; 493 A.2d 250; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 988


March 5, 1985, Argued  
May 28, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of failure to appear in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for failure to appeal, arguing that the trial court erred: (1) in finding that the evidence of willfulness was sufficient; (2) in penalizing defendant for not pleading guilty; and (3) in its charge to the jury. The court held that the proof of willfulness depended on inferences reasonably drawn from the direct evidence presented by the State, particularly the testimony elicited from the interviewing probation officer, which indicated that defendant received unambiguous notice of the court date. Simply because defendant received a harsher penalty than his co-defendant, who pled guilty, did not mean that defendant was penalized for exercising his constitutional rights because co-defendants were not without variance and did not need, in terms of punishment, to be treated similarly because they were rarely, if ever, exactly similar. The trial court's charge was legally correct and was presented the case to the jury in a just and fair manner. The charge fully articulated each element of the crime charged, repeatedly stressed the State's burden of proof on each element, and repeatedly emphasized the jury's fact-finding function.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Stephen Reney Memorial Fund v. Old Saybrook


No. 2725


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 111; 492 A.2d 533; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 967

May 21, 1985, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fund appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which rendered judgment for defendants, the town and the zoning enforcement officer (ZEO), dismissing the fund's action for a declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of Saybrook, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 61.1.


OVERVIEW: The fund received tentative approval for the construction of night lights to illuminate the town's high school athletic field, which was located in a residential area, from the ZEO. The ZEO found the lighting facilities were not in conformity with the town's zoning ordinance, Saybrook, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 61.1, and issued a cease and desist order. Pagano v. Board of Education


Nos. 2800, 2805


Appellate Court of Connecticut


4 Conn. App. 1; 492 A.2d 197; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 939


February 5, 1985, Argued  
May 14, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in the first case, from a decision of the named defendant terminating the plaintiff's teaching contract and action, in the second case, to recover damages for the plaintiff's wrongful discharge, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Kline, J.; judgments dismissing the appeal in the first case and awarding damages to the plaintiff in the second case, from which the plaintiff appealed and, in the second case, the defendant cross appealed to this court.

The appellant-appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error in the first case; error in the second case; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from the decision of defendant, a county board of education, terminating his teaching contract. In a second case, the board appealed the trial court's judgment in favor of the teacher in his wrongful discharge action.


OVERVIEW: In 1979, the board voted to terminate the teacher for moral misconduct after a hearing panel recommended to reprimand and suspend him. The teacher filed an administrative appeal and the termination was set aside because he was deprived of due process. The board held multiple meetings on the termination. At a meeting on July 26, 1982, the teacher challenged the board's jurisdiction and refused to present argument. The board then voted to terminate his contract. The teacher filed an appeal, which was tried with his action for wrongful discharge. The trial court dismissed the administrative appeal, but granted him damages on his wrongful termination claim. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the administrative appeal and reversed the judgment in the wrongful termination action. Contrary to the order in the first administrative appeal, the teacher's termination by the board in 1979 did not violate his due process rights. The procedure gave him the full opportunity to meet the case against him and to present his own case. Therefore, he was not wrongfully discharged. The law of the case doctrine did not apply due to an intervening United States Supreme Court decision.


OUTCOME: The court found not error with regard to the judgment for the board in the teacher's action appealing the board's decision that terminated her. The court set aside the judgment for the teacher in her wrongful discharge action and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to render a judgment for the board.

Neri v. Powers


No. 2734


Appellate Court of Connecticut


3 Conn. App. 531; 490 A.2d 528; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 933


March 8, 1985, Argued  
April 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant department of transportation and its defendant commissioner to close a certain railroad crossing located in the town of Clinton, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the court, M. Hennessey, J.; judgment for the defendants from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut), which was entered for defendants, department of transportation (DOT) and its commissioner, dismissing the landowners' appeal from defendants' decision to close a certain railroad crossing located in the town.


OVERVIEW: The case began as an administrative appeal to the trial court pursuant to the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-166-4-189, and by agreement of the parties and the trial court, became a vehicle for deciding an issue not within the scope of the administrative proceedings. Because neither the parties nor the trial court had the power to make such a change, the court sustained the judgment of the trial court dismissing the appeal of the landowners. On appeal, the landowners claimed that the DOT had no power to close the railroad crossing because that power was lodged solely in the federal secretary of transportation pursuant to federal statutes, and the trial court erred by finding that the landowners had not established a right of way by necessity over the crossing. The landowners appealed to the trial court from the DOT's letter referring to a decision directing the closing of the crossing. To the extent that the trial court exercised its jurisdiction over the landowners appeal from a decision other than a final decision pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183 (a), it exercised jurisdiction, which it did not have, and the landowners' appeal was dismissable.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Shelby Mut. Ins. Co. v. Della Ghelfa


No. 2130


Appellate Court of Connecticut


3 Conn. App. 432; 489 A.2d 398; 1985 Conn. App. LEXIS 897


December 5, 1984, Argued  
March 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover the amount of basic reparations benefits paid to the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Satter, J., rendered summary judgment for the plaintiff, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant Zbigniew S. Rozbicki cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part on both appeals; judgment directed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a no-fault insurer, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which, on summary judgment, limited its reimbursement recovery against defendants, the insured and his attorney, to $ 5,000 in policy proceeds awarded for which the insured also received proceeds from a judgment against the tortfeasor's insurance company.


OVERVIEW: The no-fault insurer claimed that it paid benefits in excess of the policy limits, based on regulatory required increased coverage. The insurer further claimed that the attorney improperly disbursed the judgment funds, thus violating the insurer's rights to the funds. On appeal, the court found that, although Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 38-320(a), (d), appeared to limit recover of basic reparations benefits to $ 5,000, based on the language, history, and purpose of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 35-325(b), the entire amount of required benefits paid constituted basic reparations benefits, which were subject to reimbursement and lien rights. The court found that the superior court erred in striking one of the attorney's asserted special defenses that asserted that the insurer waived its lien rights by a letter by failing to make demand, by failing to give notice of enforcement, and by failing to enforce its claim prior to the disbursement of funds from the tortfeasor's insurer. The court remanded for determination of that issue and concluded that the motion for summary judgment should have been granted to the full extent.


OUTCOME: The court found error and set aside the judgment. The court remanded the case with direction to render judgment for the insurer for the full amount of the claim against the insured and the attorney, unless he were able to establish his special defense in a hearing limited to that issue.

State v. Bowman

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70, defendant challenged his conviction. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in allowing the State to introduce testimony of defendant's alleged prior sexual misconduct and in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal.
