Cooper v. Cavallaro


No. 2387


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 622; 481 A.2d 101; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 684


June 6, 1984, Argued  
September 18, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in the first case, to determine title to certain personalty, and appeal from probate, in the second case, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and referred to Hon. Joseph W. Bogdanski, state referee; judgment in each case for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiffs, a decedent's heirs and an executor of one heir's estate, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which determined that a mortgage note and bank accounts belonged to defendant executor, who held the accounts and note jointly with a right of survivorship with the decedent, who was the executor's mother.


OVERVIEW: Claiming the existence of a constructive trust of all joint assets, plaintiffs instituted an equitable action against the executor individually. The trial court concluded that plaintiffs failed to sustain the burden of proof necessary to establish a constructive trust of the assets and that the language of the decedent's will, which directed the executor to provide for plaintiffs at his earliest discretion, was precatory in nature. On appeal the court found that plaintiffs were required to prove a fiduciary relationship between the decedent and the executor before the executor was required to prove fair dealing or the absence of undue influence. Plaintiffs failed to prove a fiduciary relationship and failed to overcome the presumption that the title to the assets in the joint accounts vested in the executor as the survivor as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36-3. Because the joint accounts held the decedent's only assets and they passed to the executor as the survivor, nothing remained to pass under the will. Even if that was not true, the decedent's will left it to the executor's discretion to provide for plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the executor.

 

1282 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bush v. Quality Bakers of America


Nos. 2057, 2610


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 363; 479 A.2d 820; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 659


May 1, 1984, Argued  
August 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the defendants from the finding and award of the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district, brought to the compensation review division; from the decision affirming the commissioner's finding and award, the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In combined appeals in a workers' compensation case, defendants, an employer and an insurer, sought review of the Compensation Review Division (Connecticut), which held in favor of plaintiff widow of deceased employee in her action for survivor's benefits. The employee died after playing racquetball with his employer's president.


OVERVIEW: The widow filed a claim and the employer did not file a notice of intent to contest the claim within 20 days as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-297(b). The Division entered a finding of compensability on the basis of § 31-297(b) and found that the employee's death did not arise out of and in the course of his employment. Defendants contended that § 31-297(b) was unconstitutional. The court held that the exclusive compensability, where the employer did not contest liability within 20 days of written notice, did not violate the employer's right to procedural due process and equal protection of the laws. The court held that a presumption of law had to be based upon facts of universal experience and be controlled by inexorable logic. The court concluded that the purpose of § 31-297(b) was to correct some of the glaring inequities and inadequacies of the Workmen's Compensation Act. Thus, the court concluded that defendants failed to meet their burden of proving that § 31-297(b) was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the court held that defendants were precluded from contesting the finding that the employee's death arose out of and in the course of his employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which held in favor of the widow in her action against defendants for survivor's benefits.

 

1283 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ritcher v. Childers


No. 2414


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 315; 478 A.2d 613; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 655


February 29, 1984, Argued  
July 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover child support arrearages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, in two counts, seeking, in the first count, a share of a settlement won by the plaintiff in a Georgia wrongful death action; the court, Driscoll, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the first count of the counterclaim and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff mother's motion for summary judgment regarding the father's cross-claim that he was entitled to a portion of a wrongful death settlement that the mother received due to the death of the parties' child.


OVERVIEW: The mother sought arrearages in child support from the father. The father cross-claimed, arguing that he was entitled to a portion of the wrongful death settlement the mother received arising from the death of their son. The trial court granted the mother summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that the Georgia wrongful death statute, which controlled the wrongful death action, had changed between the time of the son's death and when the wrongful death judgment was finalized. One of the main changes in the wrongful death statute was who could recover. Under O.C.G.A. § 105-1307, in effect when the son was killed, only the mother, if living, could recover for a minor's wrongful death. As amended, O.C.G.A. § 74-108(b) provided for a shared recovery between the parents of a decedent minor. Section 74-108(b) did not state that it was to be applied retrospectively; thus, the trial court was correct in finding that § 74-108 did not apply. While there was Georgia case law that stated that § 74-108 had retrospective effect, the father failed to point the trial court to the case, and the trial court could not be expected to undertake an original examination of foreign law.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

 

1284 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Neiditz v. Morton S. Fine & Associates, Inc.


No. 2275


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 322; 479 A.2d 249; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 657


February 29, 1984, Argued  
July 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defendant's negligent preparation of a land survey, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Alva P. Loiselle, state referee; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant surveyor appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which entered judgment for plaintiff landowners in an action for damages resulting from the surveyor's negligent preparation of a land survey. The trial court applied Conn. Gen. Stat. § 37-3a retroactively and it permitted interest at the rate of eight percent per annum from the date the damages became payable.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that errors in a site plan, which delineated the boundaries, courses, and dimensions of their land prepared by the surveyor for submission to the Town of West Hartford in connection with an application for a zone change, resulted in economic loss to them. The trial court awarded damages to the landowners for the increased costs of developing their realty that it found were causally connected to the errors in the site plan. On appeal, the court held that but for the surveyor's negligence, the owners would not have had to comply with the conditions imposed by the Town to obtain a zoning change. The surveyor was not found negligent without expert testimony as to its standard of care, and the owners property taxes were properly awarded as damages. The court concluded that the facts found were supported by the evidence and were not clearly erroneous. It was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to determine that the statutory eight percent interest rate that became effective in 1979 applied to the money due the landowners from the survey since 1973.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the trial court did not err when it awarded damages to the owners against the surveyor for his negligent preparation of a land survey.

 

1285 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Giorgio


No. 2082


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 204; 477 A.2d 134; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 625


April 11, 1984, Argued  
June 26, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with criminal impersonation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Aronson, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut) of criminal impersonation, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-130. On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in ruling that his presence was required during the trial, in denying his motion to dismiss and his motions for judgment of acquittal, and in failing to charge as defendant requested.


OVERVIEW: Driving down a state highway, defendant pulled alongside a female driver, flashed a badge, and pointed at her. When she stopped, defendant again flashed the badge and warned her about speeding. On appeal, the court held that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book §§ 967, 968, and 969 substantiated the proposition that there was no right of absence of a defendant from his criminal trial. Reference to Fed. R. Crim. Proc. 43 confirmed that conclusion. Thus, the trial court did not violate any constitutional right in requiring that defendant be present. The court held that the term "public servant" was adequately defined and § 53a-130(a) provided a reasonable degree of certainty as to the conduct prohibited. Section 53a-130(a) was not unconstitutionally vague and the motion to dismiss was properly denied. Defendant's motion for acquittal was also properly denied; the State met its burden of proving the negative fact that he was not a public servant at the time of the offense. Defendant's contention that the State was required to prove which specific public servant defendant was impersonating was baseless. The trial court's charge as to the term "public servant" was sufficient for the jury's guidance.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

1286 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Satti


No. 2101


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 219; 477 A.2d 144; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 627


January 5, 1984, Argued  
June 26, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the third degree and of breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, where the court, Murray, J., denied the defendant's motion for accelerated rehabilitation, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Session of the Superior Court, where the court granted the state's motion to dismiss the appeal; the court, Fishman, J., following the defendant's plea of nolo contendere, rendered judgment of guilty and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Connecticut, Judicial District of New Haven, which convicted him, upon his plea of nolo contendere, of assault in the third degree and breach of the peace. He claimed the trial court erred by denying his motion for accelerated rehabilitation, which he made prior to the entry of his plea. His appeal from the denial of the motion had been dismissed because there was no final judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that, upon entering a plea of nolo contendere, defendant waived certain constitutional rights, including the right to assert the privilege against self-incrimination and the right to require the State to prove guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. He also waived all nonjurisdictional defects and all defenses. After such a plea, he was limited in the claims he could make on appeal. He could not raise claims of constitutional violations occurring before his plea, although he could attack the voluntary or intelligent character of his plea. The court held that defendant could not appeal the denial of an application for accelerated rehabilitation after pleading nolo contendere. His plea was made without reservation. He made no claim that his plea was not voluntarily and intelligently made. He had waived almost all rights he might have had prior to the entry of his plea. Further, the denial of an application for accelerated rehabilitation was not equal to a deprivation of a constitutional right. Accelerated rehabilitation was a statutory alternative to the traditional course of prosecution available for some defendants and dependent upon the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

State v. Soriano


No. 2701


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 127; 476 A.2d 633; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 600


April 3, 1984, Argued  
June 12, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Driscoll, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) of the offense of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction in the trial court of the offense of robbery in the first degree, and asserted that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress the testimony of two witnesses who were present at the robbery, who observed defendant at the scene of the robbery, and who made photographic identifications of defendant. The court noted that the witnesses were an employee of the robbed store and a customer who was present at the time of the robbery. The court noted that the robbery lasted only seconds. Defendant asserted that the pretrial identifications were suggestive and resulted in a denial of his due process rights. The court found no error, and noted that defendant's photograph in an array was the only one which showed a placard hanging from the neck that displayed numbers and the words "New York Police Department." The court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that there was no irreparable identification error, because the witnesses were confident of their identification, they saw defendant at close range during the robbery, they had an unobstructed view in a well-lit store, and they had ample time to view defendant.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

1288 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Diaz v. Board of Directors of 1967 Police Pension Fund


No. 2376


Appellate Court of Connecticut


2 Conn. App. 43; 476 A.2d 146; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 612


February 29, 1984, Argued  
May 29, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Ford, J., rendered judgment granting the defendant's motion to dismiss, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which granted the motion of defendant, the board of directors of a city's police pension fund, to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction the officer's suit for an injunction to compel the board to grant him disability retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: A police officer for a city suffered a back injury in the course of his employment and applied for disability benefits pursuant to a pension agreement adopted by the city. The board denied the officer's application. The officer sued the board for an injunction ordering the board to grant his application, and the trial court granted the board's motion to dismiss the suit for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. Although there was no statutory procedure for an appeal from the board's decision, the officer's complaint included an allegation that the board breached the pension agreement. Thus, the trial court had jurisdiction over the breach of contract claim. The pension agreement was incorporated into the city's code of ordinances, and City of Danbury, Conn., Code of Ordinances § 14-59 provided for six-year limitations period for filing an action based on the agreement. Even without a statutory right of appeal, the trial court had jurisdiction over the officer's allegations that the board's action deprived him of his constitutional right of due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment which granted the board's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction a police officer's suit for an injunction to compel the board to grant him disability retirement benefits. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Small

Appellate Court of Connecticut


1 Conn. App. 584; 474 A.2d 460; 474 A.2d 461; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 576


December 6, 1983, Argued  
April 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-134 (a) (3) and 53a-60 (a) (2) respectively.


OVERVIEW: The victim was robbed and beaten by a young male. A witness saw the perpetrator from a distance of about two feet. Two others told the witness that the perpetrator's name was Pete or Peter. Five days after the incident, the witness picked out the defendant's photograph out of an array of eight photos. The photograph was of the defendant as a juvenile. The victim was unable make any identification from the photo array. The defendant objected to the photo array on the basis that several of the photographs showed individuals much heavier than him and either much older or younger. The defendant also objected because some of the photos had names on them which were not Pete or Peter. The witness made an in-court identification of the defendant. The defendant was convicted. The court affirmed finding that even though the identification procedure was impermissibly suggestive, the identification itself was nevertheless reliable in light of the totality of the circumstances. The court held the use of the defendant's photograph was not prohibited by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-124 (a) and 46b-121 because there was no evidence presented that it part of the record of a juvenile proceeding.


OUTCOME: The defendant's convictions of robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree were affirmed.

Kredi v. Benson


No. 2061


Appellate Court of Connecticut


1 Conn. App. 511; 473 A.2d 333; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 562


January 12, 1984, Argued  
April 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Summary process action, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Housing Session, and tried to the court, Foti, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which was rendered in favor of plaintiff landlords in a summary process action brought by the landlords to recover possession of premises rented to the tenants on the ground of nonpayment of rent.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court rendered judgment in favor of the landlords in their action to recover possession of leased premises for nonpayment of rent, the tenants appealed and asserted that the trial court erred in allowing the landlords to amend their complaint. The court found no abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court in allowing the amendment concerning the amount of rent due under an oral contract because the basic facts were that the tenants leased an apartment from the landlords, the rent was due, and the rent was not paid. The court therefore held that the tenants were not prejudiced by the allowance of the amendment. The tenants also claimed that the trial court erred in denying their motion for a jury trial and asserted that they had a constitutional right to a trial by jury in a summary process action. The court held that the trial court properly denied the request for a jury trial pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-215. The court further held that § 52-215 was not unconstitutional because there was a rational basis for the conditions and regulations it placed on the right to a jury trial. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the landlords and the trial court's denial of the tenants' request for a jury trial.

Shuchman v. State Employees Retirement Com.


No. 2307


Appellate Court of Connecticut


1 Conn. App. 454; 472 A.2d 1290; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 549


October 11, 1983, Argued  
March 27, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction directing the defendant to allow the plaintiff to purchase retirement credit for out-of-state service, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Corrigan, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which ruled in favor of defendant State Employees Retirement Commission, in the employee's action for a mandatory injunction, seeking a judgment directing the Commission to allow him to purchase retirement credit for his out-of-state teaching services despite his failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-177.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his employment with a state university, the employee had worked full time with the departments of education in two other states. The employee sought and was denied retirement credit under the State Employees Retirement Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 5-152-5-192d because he failed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-177 to make a retirement contribution within one year of his first full time employment with the State of Connecticut. On appeal, the court found that a memorandum from the university registrar to the personnel assistant that stated that the employee was interested in purchasing retirement credit and requesting that the information be sent to the employee and memorandum from the personnel assistant to the employee were admissible business records. The documents provided evidence that the employee was given information within the time necessary for him to meet the statutory requirements. The fact that the act distinguished between teachers purchasing in State versus out-of-state retirements credits did not violate the employee's equal protection rights because the State had a legitimate interest in conferring greater benefits on those who had previously served the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the Commission, which held that the employee was not entitled to purchase retirement credit for his out-of-state teaching services.

State v. Lenczyk


No. 2007


Appellate Court of Connecticut


1 Conn. App. 270; 470 A.2d 1240; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 512


January 3, 1984, Argued  
February 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain in the fifteenth geographical area and tried to the jury before Hale, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of larceny in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold scrap aluminum to a certain company. The aluminum belonged to a third party. Defendant testified that he found the aluminum stockpiled on the third party's premises, but that he thought the aluminum had been abandoned. Defendant contended that the trial court's jury instruction was constitutionally impermissible because it relieved the state's burden of proving the commission of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the instruction's reference to the reasonable man standard did not relieve the state of its burden. Defendant was focused on merely one portion of the instruction, which had to be considered as a whole. When considered as a whole, it was clear that the trial court informed the jury that it was not sufficient that the jury find that, as a reasonable person, the defendant ought to have known that the aluminum was probably stolen or that he ought to have ascertained whether it was stolen. Viewed as a whole, the charge made it clear that it was the jury's duty to determine whether the state had met its burden on every element of the crime charged beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Trumbull v. Trumbull Police Local 1745, etc.


No. 2296


Appellate Court of Connecticut


1 Conn. App. 207; 470 A.2d 1219; 1984 Conn. App. LEXIS 508


November 2, 1983, Argued  
January 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application by the plaintiff to vacate the decision of the state board of mediation and arbitration, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport, where the court, Grillo, J., denied the application, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which denied the town's motion to vacate an order of the State Board of Mediation and Arbitration. The arbitration order required the town to comply with an agency shop provision of the town's collective bargaining agreement with defendant union.


OVERVIEW: After failing to reach a collective bargaining agreement, the parties submitted the matter to arbitration. The arbitration report included a recommendation that the town adopt the union's proposal for an agency shop fee, which required the town to summarily discharge nonunion employees who failed to pay an agency shop fee to the union in amount equal to union dues. The town refused to enforce the agency shop provision, and the union filed a grievance. A subsequent arbitration award directed the town to comply with the agency shop provision, and the town filed the instant action. On appeal, the court held that the arbitrators did not exceed their authority within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-418(d). The court reasoned that the arbitration submission was unrestricted and that the award conformed to the submission. The court further found that the town was attempting to enlarge the scope of the court's limited review by basically seeking a second determination of the dispute on the merits after being unsuccessful in arbitration and in the trial court. The town also could not raise claims on the part of nonunion employees because they were not parties to the arbitration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's confirmation of the arbitration order.

State v. Johnson


CR 970135375


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3530



December 23, 1999, Decided  
December 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Twelve motions filed by defendant denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, charged with capital felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(5), filed numerous motions requesting a bill of particulars concerning the aggravating factors, seeking to strike the notice of the aggravating factors, and seeking preclusion of the penalty phase hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with capital felony murder. Defendant moved to strike the notice of aggravating factors, claiming plaintiff State did not relate the aggravating factors to the offense committed. The death of the victim was the offense; thus plaintiff complied with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i). Defendant argued that the allegation that the crime was committed in a cruel, heinous, or depraved manner was unconstitutionally vague. The terms could be limited and construed in a jury instruction. Defendant was on sufficient notice as to the type of assault weapon the State claimed was used. Defendant's claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(7) was unconstitutional was prematurely raised. Defendant's motions to preclude the penalty phase hearing were denied. Claim that Connecticut's capital sentencing scheme impermissibly placed a preponderance burden of proof on defendant was foreclosed. Death penalty statutes were not unconstitutional as a matter of federal or state law.


OUTCOME: All 12 of defendant's motions were denied. Plaintiff adequately related the aggravating factors to the offense committed. Death penalty statutes were constitutional. Defendant was on sufficient notice regarding the type of assault weapon he allegedly used.

 

1296 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Packer v. Thomaston Bd. of Educ.


CV 970075242


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3461



December 21, 1999, Decided  
December 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: No damages remedy lies under article first, 10 of this state's constitution and the defendant's motion to strike as regards that claim granted. Defendant's motion to strike claim for damages under fourteenth amendment of federal constitution denied and the plaintiff shall re-plead accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of education moved to strike count one for injunctive relief and count two for damages under either the Connecticut or United States constitutions in an action arising from plaintiff's expulsion from school.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff student sued for injunctive relief and damages arising from defendant school board's decision to expel him, which was later reversed on constitutional grounds. Defendant moved to strike counts one and two. The claim for injunctive relief was moot since plaintiff returned to school and graduated. The claim for damages arising under the state constitution was dismissed because no common-law right of action for damages existed pre-1818 for the temporary deprivation of a public school education. Regarding the federal constitutional claim, the alternative remedy was inadequate, there was no explicit direction from Congress that a damages remedy should not lie, and no factors counseled hesitation. While the earlier injunctive relief returned plaintiff to school, it provided no remedy for injuries such as humiliation and embarrassment, damage to reputation, loss of consortium with peers, loss of participation in extracurricular activities, and recompense for legal expenses.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted in part because the claim for injunctive relief was moot and no damages remedy was available under the state constitution, but denied in part because plaintiff could bring an action for damages under the federal constitution when the alternate remedy was inadequate and neither Congress or special factors foreclosed it.

Town of Darien v. Estate of D'Addario


CV 990172714


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3429



December 21, 1999, Decided  
December 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Darien's application to conduct Phase I environmental testing granted. Darien must receive judicial permission prior to conducting Phase II environmental testing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town applied for an order in the Superior Court of Connecticut, Judicial District of Stamford; plaintiff sought to conduct inspection and environmental testing on defendants' land in contemplation of condemnation for municipal purposes. Defendants sought determination of, among other issues, whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-13 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff town applied for an order to conduct inspection and environmental testing on defendants' land, in contemplation of condemnation for municipal purposes. Parties sought determination of legal issues surrounding application. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-13, allowing entry onto proposed condemned land to conduct an inspection, was constitutional because it was not a taking. The court also held that notice under § 48-13 was not the formal notice required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-129, because neither legislative history nor statutory language indicated a legislative intent to interpret the statutes together. Thus, failure to comply with § 8-129 did not render application defective. Further, notice was only required to property owners or affected owners, not to lienholders. Accordingly, the court granted application, but limited testing to physical inspection, and required further judicial permission for collection of land and soil samples.


OUTCOME: Application to conduct inspection granted, because statute permitting entry onto land for inspection purposes was constitutional, because no formal notice requirement was needed, and because lienholders did not have to be notified. However, further sampling of soil and water were subject to judicial approval and a showing of necessity.

 

1298 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cintron v. Valentin


FA 990498286


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3547



December 14, 1999, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner moved on default for a petition of support based on an acknowledgement of paternity signed by defendant pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because petitioner failed to show that defendant was the father of her child and charged with support and maintenance, petitioner's support petition was denied. Because neither petitioner nor defendant appeared, the State moved for default and sought an order for child support. The basis of the State's position was an acknowledgement of paternity signed by defendant pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172. However, it was not a certified copy. The court found that because under § 46b-172 the acknowledgement was required to be filed with the Department of Health, it was a public record. As such, in order for evidence of public records to be admissible, a properly certified reproduction of the public record needed to be produced. Although the State sought default, evidence still needed to be presented in order to enter a default judgment on a support petition. Because a certified copy of the acknowledgement had not been filed, there was no prima facie evidence to order support on default.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for support because petitioner on default failed to submit a certified copy of the acknowledgement of paternity signed by defendant and thus there was no prima facie evidence to order support and maintenance.

 

1299 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Mut. v. Racine


CV 980144319


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3195



November 22, 1999, Decided  
November 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' Motion to Restore denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants moved to restore plaintiff to a declaratory judgment action after plaintiff withdrew. The declaratory judgment action was to determine plaintiff's obligation under an insurance policy with defendant insureds.


OVERVIEW: Intervenors sued defendant homeowners in another action regarding the injury of intervenors child in defendant homeowners' residence. Plaintiff instituted this declaratory judgment action to determine its rights under its insurance policy with defendant homeowners. Plaintiff later withdrew its action. Defendants and intervenors (hereafter, collectively, defendants) filed motions to restore plaintiff to the declaratory judgment action, fearing the loss of discovery that might not otherwise be ordered in the underlying injury action. The court denied the various motions, holding that plaintiff's right to withdraw was absolute. The court found that, even if the withdrawal statute permitted the court discretion to restore plaintiff to the action, it was unwilling to exercise it because there was no showing that the discovery material ordered to be released would not be discoverable in a subsequent action. There was also no showing of how defendants would be prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to restore plaintiff to declaratory judgment action because defendants made no showing of the manner in which they would be prejudiced or of their inability to obtain similar discovery in the underlying injury action.

 

1300 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Greenberg v. Haddam Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV 990087811S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3129



November 19, 1999, Decided  
November 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision of defendant Haddam Zoning Board of Appeals (Connecticut) denying her application for a variance in which she sought to partially convert an existing garage to residential use.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought to renovate a garage to create a one-bedroom dwelling for her sons. The garage structure did not conform to setback regulations. The court held that: (1) plaintiff was aggrieved by defendant's decision and had standing; (2) the garage's location on an irregularly shaped lot coupled with plaintiff's preference for renovating it, did not amount to a legally cognizable hardship; (3) plaintiff failed to prove it could derive no benefit from the parcel absent a variance; (4) substantial evidence supported defendant's decision, therefore it did not act illegally or arbitrarily, nor did it abuse its discretion; (5) plaintiff failed to demonstrate partiality or predisposition of a board member; (6) defendant's decision was not voided for failing to send notice where plaintiff received timely, actual notice; and (7) because the property was already put to beneficial use, plaintiff was not deprived of the reasonable and proper use of it.


OUTCOME: Decision upheld; no legally cognizable hardship; substantial evidence supported defendant's decision which was not illegal or arbitrary, nor an abuse of discretion; plaintiff failed to demonstrate partiality or predisposition of a board member; defendant's decision was not voided where plaintiff received timely, actual notice; no taking of property.

Town of Canterbury v. Rocque


CV 990061482S

1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3101

November 17, 1999, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection moved to dismiss this action in Superior Court of Connecticut, Judicial District of Windham, at Putnam, for declaratory judgment filed by the town of Canterbury based on an absence of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff town sought to have a regulation promulgated by the Department of Environmental Protection (agency) declared unconstitutional under both the federal and state constitutions. The agency asserted that the municipality failed to exhaust administrative remedies and lacked standing to adjudicate the unconstitutionality of a state regulation. The court agreed that the municipality lacked standing to address the constitutionality of a state regulation; an attack upon the constitutionality of a state regulation by a municipality was an attack by the governmental subordinate upon its superior.


OUTCOME: Motion granted; plaintiff town lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of a state regulation, and therefore, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to decide the issue.

Bazzano v. City of Hartford


CV 980584611S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3145



November 17, 1999, Decided  
November 18, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to strike counts six and seven of plaintiff's complaint on the ground that no appellate court in Connecticut recognized a cause of action for money damages under the state constitution as to a supervisor or municipality for the alleged unconstitutional conduct of its police officers.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a 10 count complaint alleging violations of the state constitution and various state tort laws. Plaintiff alleged that he suffered personal injuries and emotional distress when defendant police officers used unnecessary and unreasonable force. Defendants moved to strike counts six and seven on the ground that no Connecticut appellate court recognized a cause of action for money damages under the state constitution as to a supervisor or municipality for the alleged unconstitutional conduct of its police officers. The court found that there were special factors counseling hesitation in the creation of a damages remedy. The deterrent effects of the Bivens remedy would have been lost if the court was to imply a damages cause of action directly against the municipality and a supervisor. Plaintiff stated a claim for relief under provisions of the Connecticut constitution and state tort law that afforded him adequate redress. The motion to strike was granted.


OUTCOME: Motion to strike granted; there were special factors counseling hesitation in the creation of a damages remedy. The deterrent effects of the Bivens remedy would have been lost if the court was to imply a damages cause of action directly against the municipality and a supervisor in the present case.

Polatnick v. Westbrook Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV 980084267


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2746



October 12, 1999, Decided  
October 12, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision of defendant zoning board, which overruled a decision to issue plaintiff a certificate of occupancy for her newly built home under Westbrook, Conn., Zoning Regulation 12.00.03 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3(f).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff purchased property in reliance on a building permit issued by the city's zoning enforcement officer (ZEO), and built a house thereon. Defendant zoning board reversed the ZEO's decision to issue plaintiff a certificate of occupancy for the home under Westbrook, Conn., Zoning Regulation 12.00.03, finding that the building permit should never have been issued because the site plan did not meet relevant regulations. The court held that a zoning permit operated as a certification in writing for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3(f). Absent a finding that plaintiff's house failed to comply with the original zoning permit, defendant zoning board had no reasonable basis for overruling the ZEO's decision to issue a certificate of occupancy. Municipal estoppel prevented defendant zoning board from requiring plaintiff to bring the house into compliance with existing zoning regulations rather than the original zoning permit. The decision of defendant zoning board was reversed.


OUTCOME: Appeal sustained and decision of board reversed on the grounds that municipal estoppel limited the enforcement power of defendant zoning board where the home conformed to the originally issued zoning permit.

School Props. Assocs. v. Westport Conservation Comm'n


CV 910119691, CV 910119690


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2676



September 27, 1999, Decided  
September 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in favor of the defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brought an administrative appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43 of defendant's decision relating to certain unimproved wetlands arguing that defendant's decision resulted in an unconstitutional taking of its property without compensation and also sought a declaration invalidating the Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act and Waterway Protection Line Ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43, plaintiff brought an administrative appeal of defendant's decision denying authority to conduct regulated activities on its property arguing that defendant's decision resulted in an unconstitutional property taking without compensation in violation of its due process rights. Plaintiff alleged that defendant improperly delegated its decision-making decision to its staff. Plaintiff also sought a declaratory judgment to invalidate the Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-36a et seq., and Waterway Protection Line Ordinance, Westport, Conn., Code § 148-1 et seq. The court affirmed defendant's decision. Plaintiff failed to prove that defendant illegally delegated its authority to its staff. Defendant's administrative record was sufficient to supports its ultimate conclusion because its findings indicated that without its limitations plaintiff's proposed activity would encroach on protected wetlands. The court refused to invalidate the challenged ordinances because they were rationally related to protect public health and safety.


OUTCOME: In affirming defendant's administrative decision, the court held that plaintiff failed to prove that defendant unjustly delegated authority to its staff and that defendant's administrative record properly supported its decision protecting adjacent wetlands. The disputed ordinance and act were not invalidated because they were rationally related to public interest protection.

 

1305 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Golden v. Johnson Mem. Hosp.


CV 980582094S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2536



September 17, 1999, Decided  
September 17, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The motions for summary judgment of each Defendant are granted. Judgment shall enter accordingly for each Defendant. No costs shall be awarded to or assessed against any party hereto.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Alleging misdiagnosis of tissue samples, plaintiff filed medical malpractice claim against defendant health-care providers. Defendants moved for summary judgment, contending that statute of limitations, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584, barred plaintiff's suit. In opposition, plaintiff asserted that continuing course of conduct tolling doctrine applied and limitations period was unconstitutionally applied.


OVERVIEW: After being diagnosed with advanced Hodgkins Disease in 1997, plaintiff brought medical malpractice claim against defendants that alleged misdiagnosis of tissue samples during the 1980s. Defendants moved for summary judgment, asserting that action had long since been barred by applicable statute of limitations, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584. Alternatively, plaintiff contended that continuing course of conduct tolling doctrine applied and that three-year limitations period was unconstitutional as applied. Court granted defendants' separate motions for summary judgment, holding that § 52-584 barred plaintiff's action because more than three years had elapsed since occurrence of alleged misdiagnosis. Continuing course of conduct doctrine was inapplicable because there was only a single medical service provided and there was no breach of any duty that thereafter remained. Section 52-584 applied regardless of whether plaintiff had not, or in the exercise of care, could not reasonably have discovered nature of the injuries within three-year time period.


OUTCOME: Court granted summary judgment to defendants, holding that plaintiff's medical malpractice action commenced more than three years from date of alleged misdiagnosis was barred by statute of limitations regardless of whether plaintiff had not or could not reasonably have discovered nature of the injuries within that time period.

Shashaty v. Commissioner


CV 990335534S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2457



September 8, 1999, Decided  
September 8, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent corrections commissioner moved to dismiss habeas petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus, arguing petitioner had failed to state a claim for which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Habeas petitioner, incarcerated in state's correctional system, filed for a state writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner sought to use the writ as a vehicle to expunge certain disciplinary reports from his prison records. Respondent corrections commissioner moved to dismiss the petition on the grounds that it failed to state a cause of action for which relief could be granted. State trial court agreed and ordered petition dismissed, noting that habeas is a remedy available only if the party seeking relief avers that he is illegally confined or has otherwise been deprived of his liberty. Since petitioner neither claimed a liberty interest in the collateral effects of the disciplinary reports (loss of prison employment, ineligibility for recreational or educational programs, ineligibility for early release, etc.) nor that his confinement was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual, he had not stated a claim for which habeas relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: Application for state writ of habeas corpus was dismissed. Petitioner did not claim that his liberty interests had been violated or that his confinement was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual, and thus he stated no grounds for relief for which habeas was an available remedy.

Caswell Cove Marina Assoc. v. Planning & Zoning Bd. of Milford

September 3, 1999, Decided

DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter came before the court when plaintiff not-for-profit condominium association and individual unit owners appealed from a decision of defendant Planning and Zoning Board in which defendant denied, in part, plaintiffs' application for modification of a special permit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff not-for-profit condominium association and individual unit owners applied to defendant Planning and Zoning Board for an amendment of its special permit to allow construction of a pier, ramp, and floating docks on their marina property. Although defendant originally approved plaintiffs' application, plaintiffs thereafter agreed to withdraw that application and submit a new, virtually identical one when the owners of adjacent condominiums threatened to appeal on the grounds of lack of proper notice. Defendant thereafter denied the application in part on the grounds that the contemplated construction would constitute an invasion of privacy to the owners of adjacent condominiums. The court rejected plaintiffs' arguments that defendant could not reverse its previous decision, holding that a material change of external circumstances affecting the merits of plaintiffs' application occurred. Nevertheless, the court sustained plaintiffs' appeal because the record did not contain substantial evidence warranting the denial of their application.


OUTCOME: The court sustained plaintiffs' appeal since defendant abused its discretion in denying the application to modify the special permit when the record did not contain substantial evidence showing that the contemplated construction would adversely affect the privacy of certain adjacent condominium owners.

1309 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Papp v. City of Shelton


CV 960056489S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2358



August 26, 1999, Decided  
August 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a complaint against defendant city for negligent nuisance, and defendant filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming that as a matter of law there was no basis for a nuisance claim against defendant. Defendant further argued that plaintiff's claim was barred by the statute of limitations, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a complaint against defendant city and asserted that defendant created a nuisance when it defectively extended a storm water drainage system beyond its original design. Defendant moved for summary judgment, claiming that there was no basis for a nuisance claim as a matter of law, and that plaintiff's claim was barred by the statute of limitations, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584. On review, the court looked at the elements of plaintiff's claim and noted that, in addition to the traditional elements of a nuisance claim, plaintiff had to prove that the condition constituting the nuisance was created by the positive act of defendant. The court could not determine whether defendant's actions or inactions constituted a "positive act" in the case. Therefore, the court could not rule in favor of defendant. Defendant also asserted that the three-year tort statute of limitations applied, and submitted that the action was founded upon a tort. The court noted that the complaint could be viewed in various ways. Therefore, further information was needed in order to properly classify the action. Thus, the motion for summary judgment was denied as to both issues.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's summary judgment motion insofar as it claimed that, as a matter of law, a nuisance claim had not been set forth in plaintiff's complaint. As to the statute of limitations claim, the court held that there was not an appropriate factual record to decide the issue, where the complaint could be viewed under various theories as to the nature of the claim.

Burke v. Wezner


CV 980413665S, CV 980414260


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2352



August 25, 1999, Decided  
August 25, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: It is the conclusion of the court that the condition of probation imposed on the petitioner excluding him from this state is invalid under the United States Constitution. That condition is therefore ordered stricken from the sentence imposed on August 29, 1996. In all other respects said sentence shall remain as imposed. The petitioner in CV 98-0413665S is therefore granted to that extent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner convicted and sentenced for reckless endangerment and criminal mischief filed two habeas corpus petitions, which were consolidated for trial, alleging ineffective assistance of counsel, and seeking relief from court-imposed fines and banishment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-74.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner convicted and sentenced for reckless endangerment and criminal mischief was given probation with the condition that petitioner have no contact with the victim or the victim's family, and that he leave the state and not return. Petitioner filed two habeas corpus petitions, which were consolidated for trial. Petitioner's pro se claim sought relief from court-imposed fines and banishment, while his second claim alleged ineffective assistance of counsel based on failure of counsel to object at sentencing. The court held that as sentence had already been pronounced, it was highly doubtful that a protest after the fact would have reversed the outcome. However, the court held that because petitioner had not intentionally rendered himself unable to pay the fines, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-74, the court remitted the fines to further the interests of justice. Finally, the court found that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-30(a), the probation condition banishing petitioner from the state was invalid under the U.S. Const.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's first claim, holding that the ineffective assistance of counsel claim was meritless, but revoked the fines in light of petitioner's age and financial status and the interests of justice. The probation condition of banishment was found unconstitutional.

Mackall v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Greenwichjoel Lutzker


CV 980166185S, CV 980166067S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2311



August 23, 1999, Decided  
August 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained and the Commission's decision null and void.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner and plaintiff contract purchaser of property appealed the decision of the Greenwich Planning & Zoning Commission denying plaintiff contract purchaser's application for permission to connect to the public sewer system, contending that the commission's decision was arbitrary and unreasonable because a septic system could not be built on the property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contract purchaser applied to the Greenwich Planning & Zoning Commission for permission to connect property to public sewer system. The commission denied permission because it concluded that a septic system could be built on the lot. Plaintiff contract purchaser and plaintiff owner appealed the commission's decision, contending it was arbitrary and unreasonable because the health department would not approve a septic system for the property. The superior court reversed and declared the commission's decision null and void because the commission exceeded the authority granted by the Charter of the Town of Greenwich, Connecticut § 269(a)(d)(6). This was because the commission did not state facts that supported finding that extending the sewer line would adversely effect conservation and development plans, it merely concluded that a sewer line extension was precluded because the property was not part of the planned sewered area. Moreover, the commission denied the application based on speculation that a septic system could be built on the lot, when, in fact, a septic system could not be built on the land.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff contract purchaser's appealed was sustained and the commission's decision to deny plaintiff permission to connect property to sewer line was declared null and void because the commission exceeded authority granted to it in town charter by failing to state facts which supported its finding that extension would adversely effect conservation and development plans, and speculation that a septic system could be built on the lot.

 

1312 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rizzo


CR 97262883


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2194



August 12, 1999, Decided  
August 12, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Rizzo, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 394 (Conn., Oct. 7, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's MOTION FOR A HEARING PURSUANT TO CONN. GEN. STAT. 53A-46b(b)(1) TO ESTABLISH THAT THE DEATH PENALTY IS ADMINISTERED IN AN ARBITRARY MANNER denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought to continue his sentencing so that he could develop and present evidence that the death penalty was administered in an arbitrary manner by the state of Connecticut. Defendant pleaded guilty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(a)(9) for capital felony murder, murder of a person under 16 years of age. A hearing was held in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46(a)(b)(2) and the jury mandated the imposition of a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to capital felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(a)(9), murder of a person under 16 years of age. A hearing was held in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46(a)(b)(2). The jury, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(f), determined that the aggravating factor found proven beyond a reasonable doubt outweighed the mitigating factors found proven by a fair preponderance of the evidence and thereby mandated the trial court to impose a death sentence. Defendant filed a motion to continue his sentencing so he could develop and present evidence that the death penalty was administered in an arbitrary manner by the state. The court denied the motion finding that defendant had ample notice and opportunity to be prepared to present the evidence requested in a timely fashion. The court held that for defendant to raise an equal protection claim on the basis of racial discrimination, he had to prove the decision-maker in his case acted with a discriminatory purpose. The court found defendant's motion did not allege purposeful discrimination in his particular case but instead attacked the entire legality of the state's capital sentencing scheme.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion was denied on the basis that he had ample notice and opportunity to be prepared to present the evidence requested in a timely fashion. Furthermore, defendant's motion did not allege purposeful discrimination in his particular case, but attacked the entire legality of Connecticut's capital sentencing scheme.

Bloomfield Ctr. Fire Dist. v. Connecticut Dep't of Labor


CV 990587070S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2287



August 11, 1999, Decided  
August 11, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fire district sought a temporary injunction restraining defendant Connecticut labor board from conducting binding interest arbitration pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-473c pending disposition of a petition for decertification of defendant union.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff fire district sought to enjoin defendant Connecticut labor board (SBLR) from conducting binding interest arbitration pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-473c pending disposition of a petition for decertification of defendant union. In response, the court granted defendant SBLR's motion to dismiss on grounds of sovereign immunity. The court explained that the doctrine could be asserted when a plaintiff sought to control the activities of a state. Here, the court explained, defendant SBLR would be barred from conducting collective bargaining if plaintiff succeeded; thus, an action against the state was involved. The court then rejected plaintiff's assertion that the imposition of binding arbitration would be illegal because defendant union no longer had the support of its members. In construing § 7-473c(b), delineating powers of defendant SBLR, the court observed that the provision mandated binding arbitration when the parties could not negotiate an agreement. In the absence of any statute limiting arbitration when decertification petition was pending, the obligation to conduct binding arbitration was mandatory and within defendant SBLR's authority, the court concluded.


OUTCOME: Petition by plaintiff fire district for temporary injunction to restrain defendant state labor board from conducting binding interest arbitration pending disposition of petition for defendant union decertification denied, and defendant's motion to dismiss granted, as sovereign immunity barred suit involving obligatory action of defendant board when collective bargaining agreement with certified union remained unnegotiated.

 

1314 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Modern Cigarette v. Town of Orange


CV 980414676S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2168



August 10, 1999, Decided  
August 10, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment entered in favor of plaintiff declaring Town of Orange's ordinance invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff vendor sought a declaratory judgment that a municipal ordinance barring a state-licensed vendor from distributing cigarettes by vending machine was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant municipality argued that its ordinance banning the sale of cigarettes by vending machine was valid, because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-289a(h) expressly provided that municipalities were not precluded from imposing more restrictive conditions of the use of cigarette vending machines than mandated by state law. The court disagreed, saying that the ordinance was preempted by state law, which limited vending machines to locations accessible only by adults. Because plaintiff cigarette vendor was licensed by the state, defendant exceeded its powers in attempting to remove a right authorized by the state, the court explained. The clear language of § 12-289a(h) indicated that machines would continue to be "used," and the outright prohibition of the machines -- as opposed to added restrictions -- was not legislatively intended, the court reasoned. As a direct conflict existed between the statute and ordinance, both having the common objective of reducing access by minors to tobacco, the ordinance must yield, the court ruled. Nor could defendant use its police powers to protect the public welfare when the resulting ban conflicted with the state statute, the court added.


OUTCOME: Declaratory judgment granted that defendant's municipal ordinance barring a state-licensed vendor from distributing cigarettes by vending machine was invalid, because ordinance exceeded state statutory authorization allowing more restrictive municipal conditions on "use" of vending machines, and because ordinance preempted by conflicting state law under which plaintiff was licensed to sell cigarettes by vending machine.

In re Zarko H.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2136



August 5, 1999, Decided  
August 5, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, Department of Children and Families, sought an articulation of an order from the trial court (Connecticut), which suo moto vacated an Order of Temporary Custody without an evidentiary hearing, and immediately restored the child to the custody of his parents.


OVERVIEW: The court rendered an articulation of the Order vacating an Order of Temporary Custody (OTC) and immediately restoring the child to the custody of respondents, his parents. The court stated that where, as here, an OTC was given on a social worker's written affidavit, fundamental fairness demanded that the order be dissolved upon displaying to the court subsequently obtained written documentation of changed circumstances. The court stated that when respondents demonstrated through a rent receipt that they could now provide housing for the child, the order was dissolved. The court found petitioner's suggestion that the housing was only assured for one month and the parents had no established means to support themselves displayed a total disregard of the requirement that the risk of physical danger to a child must have been immediate and that his immediate removal would be necessary to ensure his safety. The court stated that the predicted benefit to the child from being precipitately removed from immediate physical danger was not outweighed by the predictable emotional harm, resulting from such removal, and on that basis the court refused to continue the OTC.


OUTCOME: The court rendered an articulation of the Order which dissolved an Order of Temporary Custody and stated that based on documentation of changed circumstances the court found that the child's removal from his parents was no longer necessary to ensure his continued safety.

Medina v. Town of Watertown


CV 970140408


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2120



August 3, 1999, Decided  
August 3, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brought an action (Connecticut) contending that a provision defendant town's zoning regulations that prohibited her from displaying an "open" flag at her business was a violation of her constitutional right of free speech. She sought a permanent injunction against defendants, the town and its zoning enforcement officer, prohibiting the enforcement of the regulation, and an award of punitive damages and attorneys fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff operated a business at a busy intersection. Defendant zoning officer advised plaintiff that defendant town's zoning regulations prohibited the display of "open" and all other commercial flags within the town. Plaintiff contended that the regulation violated her constitutional right to freedom of speech. The parties conceded that the "open" flag that plaintiff wished to display concerned lawful activity and was not misleading, and that public safety on the highway was a significant and legitimate governmental interest. The court found that the regulation directly advanced defendant town's interest in public safety by prohibiting those displays that cause the greatest distraction, e.g., flags, banners, etc., because these devices caused the greatest distraction to motorists because they moved and were not easily read. The court concluded that the regulation was not more extensive than necessary because while barring the most distracting advertising devices, it did permit plaintiff to use stationary signs for advertising. Therefore, the court held that plaintiff failed to demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt that regulations violated plaintiff's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff's action and held that plaintiff failed to sustain her burden of demonstrating beyond a reasonable doubt that the zoning regulation violated plaintiff's constitutional right of free speech.

Bank of New Haven v. Karas Motors


414574


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2005



July 27, 1999, Decided  
July 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to strike granted as to count one. Defendant's motion to strike denied as to counts two, three and four.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to strike plaintiff's claims based on defendant's negligence per se violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-150, negligence, conversion, and violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practice Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was the first lienholder on a motor vehicle that was towed to defendant. Defendant stripped the vehicle and sold the parts at auction. Plaintiff alleged that defendant's acts constituted negligence per se in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-150, negligence, conversion, and violated the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a. Defendant moved to strike the complaint. The court granted defendant's motion to strike the negligence per se violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-150 because plaintiff was not within the class of persons the statute was intended to protect. However, defendant's motion to strike the remaining counts was denied because defendant was negligent in not notifying plaintiff when it sold the vehicle, and as a result plaintiff suffered damages. Moreover, defendant had no right to sell the motor vehicle without giving plaintiff actual notice of the sale. Therefore, plaintiff had sufficiently alleged a cause of action for conversion. Finally, defendant's sale of automobiles was sufficiently related to the business of a garage to be a "trade or commerce" within the meaning of CUTPA.


OUTCOME: Motion to strike granted on negligence per se count since plaintiff was not within the class of persons protected. Motion to strike denied as to remaining counts because defendant was negligent in not notifying plaintiff of sale, sale was not statutorily authorized and constituted conversion, and sale of automobiles was sufficiently related to business of a garage to be a "trade" within the meaning of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act.

Samben Realty Co. v. Watertown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV 970143362S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1726



June 22, 1999, Decided  
June 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision of the Watertown Planning & Zoning Commission (Connecticut) to reduce the size of retail businesses in all business zones with special permits for those already existing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Planning and Zoning Commission (Commission) amended the zoning laws to reduce the size of retail businesses with special permits for already existing businesses. Plaintiff realty company appealed the amendments to the zoning plan, alleging that they were not supported by a comprehensive plan, that there was not substantial evidence to support the change, and that the scope exceeded the Commission's authority. Plaintiff also alleged that the amendments were an unconstitutional taking, that the Commission prejudged the amendments, and that they were void for vagueness. The court held that the plan was within the zoning regulations and therefore supportable. The record also showed that the Commission was concerned with traffic and parking problems and there was ample evidence to support the changes. The court also noted that it had long been held that zoning changes were within the police power of the Commission and that zoning changes were not unconstitutional takings when providing for the safety of pedestrians. The court also found that the changes were not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's appeal of the zoning changes was dismissed because there was sufficient evidence to support the changes, they were within the plan of development, there was no taking, they were not void, and the Commission acted within its authority at all times.
