DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed suit to appeal the decision of defendant, which enacted amendments to the zoning regulations limiting the size of retail establishments in business districts.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff commercial partnership filed suit against defendant local planning and zoning commission, which amended the zoning regulations to limit the size of retail businesses in all business zones. Reviewing defendant's actions to determine whether the zone change was in accord with a comprehensive plan and was reasonably related to the normal police power under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2, the court upheld the amendments. The court, in dismissing plaintiff's appeal, also found that because the amendments were reasonably related to control traffic and congestion and, as such, were within the enumerated police powers of § 8-2, the amendments were valid.


OUTCOME: Amendments to zoning regulation upheld, and plaintiff's appeal dismissed, where there was evidence that the regulations were in accordance with comprehensive plan of preventing traffic and congestion, and where such preventive goals were reasonably related to defendant's police powers.

Rabatin v. Connecticut Dep't of Social Servs.


CV 970140476


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1652



June 21, 1999, Decided  
June 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Department's decision affirmed and appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision from defendant Department of Social Services, which upheld the state's lien against plaintiff's workers' compensation benefits. Defendant premised its decision on a holding that plaintiff's daughter had received state assistance, for which plaintiff was liable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-93, and that plaintiff's benefits were available to secure reimbursement to the state pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-94.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought review of a decision that upheld defendant Department of Social Services' claim of a lien against plaintiff's workers' compensation benefits pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17b-93, 17b-94. Defendant premised its decision on a finding that plaintiff's daughter had received assistance, for which plaintiff was liable under § 17b-93, and plaintiff's claim was available to secure reimbursement to the state for such assistance. The court held that plaintiff's workers' compensation claim was a cause of action, and so subject to the provisions of § 17b-94, creating a lien in favor of the state. The court also held that plaintiff's compensation benefits were not exempt from a lien by the state because § 17b-94 provided that proceeds from such a cause of action were assignable to the state for payment of the amount due under § 17b-93, irrespective of any other provision of law. Accordingly, defendant's decision claiming a lien on plaintiff's workers' compensation benefits was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Decision upholding the state's lien against plaintiff's workers' compensation benefits was affirmed because plaintiff's workers' compensation claim was a cause of action, and so was assignable to the state for payment of amount due as reimbursement for assistance provided by the state to plaintiff's daughter.

Sealy Conn. v. Watertown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV 970143349


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1732



June 21, 1999, Decided  
June 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged amendments to zoning regulations governing business districts approved by the Watertown Planning & Zoning Commission (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner challenged newly-enacted amendments to zoning regulations governing business districts on grounds that appellee zoning commission acted illegally by not stating its reasons on the record and did not consider the comprehensive plan. The court disagreed, ruling that the appellee's action accorded with a comprehensive plan and was reasonably related to the normal police powers allowed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2. Pointing to § 8-3, the court said that appellee did not need to explicitly state its reasons, because its reasons -- that increased traffic could be controlled by limiting the size of businesses -- could be culled from throughout the record. Such reasons, the court added, were reasonably related to the general welfare of the community. While appellee had no comprehensive plan as such, the court noted that the "plan," found in the zoning regulations, allowed for the regulation of traffic circulation, a topic consistent with the amendments. Nor did appellant sustain its burden of proof that the amendments were unconstitutionally vague, the court concluded, noting that the amendments, when read together with the amended section, were clear.


OUTCOME: Appellant's challenge of amendments to zoning regulations governing business districts dismissed, because purpose of amendments -- to control traffic by limiting size of businesses in districts -- was legitimately related to community welfare and accorded with the comprehensive plan, found in the regulations.

Mulkerrin v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of New Canaan

DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the decision of the Planning and Zoning Commission of the Town of New Canaan, Connecticut, denying their resubdivision application.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, through various transfers, wished to subdivide several acres into lots of which one did not have the required amount of direct frontage on a right-of-way. Their zoning request was denied by the Planning and Zoning Commission (Commission), and the plaintiffs appealed, alleging that the denial was illegal, arbitrary, and an abuse-of-discretion. OUTCOME: Plaintiffs' appeal of the Planning and Zoning Commission's denial of their subdivision application was dismissed because the evidence sustained the Commission's findings, and the Commission did not act arbitrarily, illegally or abuse its discretion.

Byars v. City of Waterbury


NO. CV99-0152489S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1741



June 3, 1999, Decided  
June 3, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs application for a temporary injunction denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents and plaintiff students sought temporary injunctive relief to enjoin defendant city and defendant school board from enforcing the school attire policy against plaintiff students in plaintiffs' suit alleging that the school attire policy violated plaintiffs' federal and state constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The court denied the request for temporary injunctive relief, finding that plaintiff parents and plaintiff students had not met their burden of proof by failing to show that plaintiffs would prevail at a trial on the merits. The court found that plaintiffs had failed to demonstrate that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-221f was unconstitutional, noting that plaintiffs had not challenged the constitutionality of the statute, which authorized defendant school board to establish either a mandatory or voluntary uniform policy in its schools at its discretion. The court further found that the school attire policy was rationally related to the legitimate educational interest in reducing distractions, creating a safe environment, reducing clothing costs, promoting a sense of community among students, preparing students for the work environment, and enhancing the public perception of the school system, noting that plaintiffs had not argued that the rights allegedly violated were fundamental rights. The court concluded that temporary injunctive relief was not available to plaintiffs where plaintiffs' constitutional rights were not violated by the school attire policy.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for a temporary injunction from plaintiff parents and plaintiff students where plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of proof in showing that they would prevail on the merits at trial; plaintiffs never challenged the constitutionality of the statute regarding school attire policies, which was rationally related to the legitimate state interest in promoting safe, distraction-free public education.

DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion for supplemental order denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff moved for a supplemental order granting it priority of its mortgage foreclosure over defendant's utility receivership.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a mortgage foreclosure action on several properties. Defendant was appointed as a receiver of rents pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-262f, which provided for the establishment of utility receiverships. Plaintiff moved for a supplemental order granting it priority over the utility receivership. Plaintiff's procedural due process rights also were not infringed upon by the summary proceedings provided in § 16-262f.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's motion for supplemental order giving it priority over defendant's utility receivership was denied, because the legislature intended for utility receiverships to have priority over mortgage foreclosure actions.

Straits Commer. Assocs. v. Watertown Planning & Zoning Comm'n

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commercial enterprise brought suit in an attempt to block the zoning changes ordered by defendant municipal agency, arguing noncompliance with the statutory requirements for such changes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff commercial enterprise filed suit seeking to block certain zoning changes made by defendant municipal agency. Plaintiff objected to the proposed changes on the ground that they violated the comprehensive plan. The trial court rejected the plaintiff's objections and held for defendant, reasoning as follows: (a) modifications dealt with the municipality's comprehensive plan, which is a general plan to control and direct the use and development of property in a municipality by dividing it into districts according to present and potential uses of the property; (b) in order for a zoning change to be upheld, it must be in conformance with the comprehensive plan and reasonably related to normal police powers enumerated in state law; (c) the evidence supported zoning changes, as they dealt with traffic patterns, a legitimate concern; (d) regulations were sufficiently particular as to give notice of their objective; and (e) notice provisions were adequate.


OUTCOME: Judgment was granted to defendant municipal agency; zoning changes in question were motivated by traffic patterns, a permissible concern, and were valid since they were in conformity with the comprehensive plan.

 

1328 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Latina v. State


CV 990587010S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1353



May 19, 1999, Decided  
May 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: DOL's motion to dismiss complaint, insofar as it is directed against it, granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Labor (DOL), filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff's complaint that was brought after defendant DOL denied plaintiff's application for unemployment compensation. Defendant DOL contended that the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee brought an action against defendant former employer for wrongful termination, and against defendant Department of Labor (DOL) for the denial of unemployment compensation. Defendant DOL filed a motion to dismiss contending that the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction. The court stated that the doctrine of sovereign immunity implicated subject matter jurisdiction and, therefore, was a basis for granting a motion to dismiss. The court also stated that a state is immune from a suit unless it consented to be sued. The state may consent to be sued in certain cases by appropriate legislation waiving its sovereign immunity. In addition, sovereign immunity did not bar suits against state officials acting in excess of their statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. The plaintiff employee's action against defendant DOL did not demonstrate that sovereign immunity had been waived. Furthermore, the complaint did not contain any allegation that defendant DOL had acted in excess of its authority or acted pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Therefore, the court granted defendant DOL's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted because the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The sovereign immunity of defendant Department of Labor (DOL) had not been waived and the complaint contained no allegations that the defendant DOL acted in excess of its authority or acted pursuant to an unconstitutional statute.

Sarlom v. Watertown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV 970143368S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1368



May 19, 1999, Decided  
May 20, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limited liability corporation appealed from an action of the Watertown Planning & Zoning Commission (Connecticut), which amended the zoning regulations regarding the permitted size of retail businesses in all business zones.


OVERVIEW: Defendant planning and zoning commission amended the zoning regulations in three of its business districts, limiting the permitted size of retail businesses therein. Plaintiff, a limited liability company that owned certain developed and undeveloped property in one of those districts, appealed from defendant's decision, asserting that defendant did not establish an effective date for the amendments, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 8-3(d), the content and adequacy of the notice provisions were fundamentally unfair, defendant's members prejudged the issues, and the zoning change effectively precluded any further development of plaintiff's property. The court disagreed, finding that defendant did set an effective date and did not violate the concepts of fundamental fairness. There was no evidence that the minds of defendant's members were so intractable as to demonstrate either unfairness or a pre-determined outcome. Finally, since plaintiffs were not denied any use of their land, there was no unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's appeal dismissed; zoning regulation amendments which significantly limited the further development and use of plaintiff's property in designated business district were not reversed because defendant zoning commission properly notified public, invited public comment, provided opportunity to be heard, and did not deny plaintiffs of every use of their land.

Sealy Conn., Inc.V. Watertown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV 970143349


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1375



May 19, 1999, Decided  
May 20, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant planning and zoning commission voted to amend its zoning regulations regarding the permitted size of retail businesses in all business zones. Plaintiff, who owned property in affected business district, argued that defendant acted illegally and in the abuse of its discretion because it did not state its reasons on the record; did not consider the comprehensive plan; and that its decision constituted a taking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant planning and zoning commission voted to amend its zoning regulations pertaining to its business districts. In the central district, the permitted use was reduced from a gross floor area of 20,000 square feet to a maximum gross floor area of 10,000 square feet. Plaintiff, who owned property in the central district, argued that defendant acted illegally. Plaintiff first claimed that defendant did not state the reasons for the approval of its amended regulations on the record. The court stated that defendant did not have to state its reasons on the record, and that it was the duty of the reviewing court to search the record for evidence supporting the decision of defendant. The court found that the decision was supported by substantial evidence, as the record showed that traffic was a topic of concern. Further, the court found that there was ample evidence demonstrating that the amendments were consistent with the comprehensive plan, which was in this case found in the zoning regulations themselves. Finally, the court held that plaintiff failed to meet its burden of demonstrating that the regulations as applied were vague or unascertainable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff's appeal from a decision of defendant planning and zoning commission, which voted to amend its zoning regulations regarding the permitted size of retail businesses in all business zones, on the grounds that the decision was supported by substantial evidence and consistent with the comprehensive plan.

 

1331 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Simard v. Salinas


CV 990493042S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1272



May 18, 1999, Decided  
May 18, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's administrative appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision from defendant Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Motor Vehicles suspending his motor vehicle operator's license pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b. Plaintiff claimed the hearing officer erred in relying on a presumption in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(f) when he found that plaintiff's blood alcohol content exceeded 0.10 percent because plaintiff rebutted the presumption by presenting expert evidence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought review of a decision from defendant commissioner of the department of motor vehicles suspending his motor vehicle operator's license pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b. Plaintiff claimed that he rebutted the presumption of intoxication found in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(f) as a matter of law by presenting expert evidence that alcohol trapped under his dental plate could have affected his breath test results. Plaintiff further argued that the presumption was unconstitutional as applied to him because it was mandatory. The appeal was dismissed. The court held that there was substantial evidence in the record to support the hearing officer's decision. Plaintiff's expert testimony did not rebut the statutory presumption of intoxication where it showed only the possibility that plaintiff's blood alcohol content was less than 0.10 percent. To rebut the statutory presumption the evidence had to do more than raise a mere theoretical possibility that the presumed fact did not exist. Also, the presumption was constitutional. According to the court, a hearing officer could rely on the presumption if he or she disbelieved the expert evidence presented to rebut it.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's appeal of a decision from defendant commissioner of motor vehicles suspending his motor vehicle operator's license for driving while intoxicated was dismissed. There was substantial evidence in the record to support the hearing officer's decision, and plaintiff's expert testimony did not rebut a statutory presumption of intoxication where it showed only the possibility that plaintiff's blood alcohol content was less than 0.10 percent.

Six Six One Middle Turnpike Assocs. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n Mansfield

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner, a corporation, challenged a rezoning decision of defendant municipal zoning commission changing zoning classifications for an area that encompassed portions of its property, claiming the procedure followed at a public hearing violated its due process rights because defendant failed to give its reasoning for the revisions and the sole comment specific to plaintiff's property was made by a member during closed deliberations, thereby depriving plaintiff of the opportunity to cross-examine or rebut the comment. SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN

Friends of Hillhouse Ave. v. Yale Univ.


CV 980419300S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1143



April 28, 1999, Decided  
April 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petition for Permanent Injunctive Relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following defendant university's decision to demolish a building allegedly located within a district listed on the National Register of Historic Places, 16 U.S.C.S. § 471a, plaintiffs organized to seek injunctive relief to prevent the demolition under the authority of Connecticut Environmental Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Connecticut Environmental Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 et seq., plaintiff preservationists sought permanent injunctive relief in order to prevent defendant university from demolishing a certain building, alleging that the building was located in a district listed on the National Register of Historic Places, 16 U.S.C.S. § 471a. The court held that, considering all the evidence presented, the demolition of the building would not be unreasonable. Defendant rebutted the prima facie case put forth by the plaintiffs but also proved that renovation was not a prudent alternative to demolition. Any effort to restore the building would be a replica not a restoration of the building's original design. Defendant's cost to restore the building would be substantially more than the fair market value of the property after renovation was complete. Therefore, defendant had demonstrated, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-17, that the proposed demolition was consistent with the reasonable requirements of the public health, safety, and welfare.


OUTCOME: The court denied the plaintiffs' petition for permanent injunctive relief and entered judgment in favor of defendant university. Defendant demonstrated renovation of a purportedly historic building was not a prudent alternative to demolition. Any effort to restore the building would only create a replica of the building's original design. Therefore, proposed demolition was consistent with the requirements of public health, safety, and welfare.

 

1336 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lane v. Lane


FA 950405610


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1132



April 27, 1999, Decided  
April 28, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motions for transcript and the plaintiff's motion to waive fees denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed motions asking the court to provide complete transcripts of the judicial proceedings modifying the custody of her children and to waive the fee required for plaintiff to file an appeal because she was indigent.


OVERVIEW: Following the court's modification of the custody orders regarding her children, plaintiff asked the court to provide her with transcripts of the proceedings free of charge and to waive the fee for filing an appeal because she was indigent. The court stated that there was a narrow category of civil cases in which a state must provide access to its judicial processes without regard to a party's ability to pay. The court stated that proceedings to terminate parental rights was one example because such a proceeding was irretrievably destructive of the most fundamental family relationship. However, the court held a change of custody did not fall within the narrow category because it did not sever the parent-child bond. The court therefore denied plaintiff's motions for transcripts free of charge. The court held that in order for plaintiff to be entitled to an appeal she was required to satisfy the court that the appeal was nonfrivolous. The court concluded that plaintiff was not entitled to an appeal of the modification of custody because the issues which she intended to raise were frivolous. The court, therefore, denied the motion to waive the fee for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff's motions that the court provide transcripts free of charge because a modification of custody proceeding did not fall within the narrow category of civil cases in which the state was required to provide access to the judicial process without regard to a party's ability to pay. The court denied plaintiff's motion that the court waive the fee for an appeal because it held plaintiff's appeal was frivolous.

 

1337 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


B&D Molded Prods. v. Vitek Research Corp.


CV 97060362S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1081



April 20, 1999, Decided  
April 21, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion as to the first count granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for summary judgment based on the statute of limitations on plaintiff owner's claim that defendant improperly used, stored, disposed, or discharged hazardous waste as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-115(1) during defendant's lease of plaintiff's property.


OVERVIEW: The lease between the parties required defendant, as lessee, to comply with all federal and state laws during the term of the lease. Defendant argued that the six-year statute of limitations barred plaintiff owner's claim for the creation of pollution on plaintiff's property. The court held that any continuing obligation on defendant created by environmental laws ran to the government and not to plaintiff. The duty to remediate only became operative to the extent government authorities concluded remediation was possible or necessary. Whenever the continuing duty doctrine was applied to extend the limitations period, the duty must be found to have run to the party claiming the injury. Therefore plaintiff was not insulated from defendant's statute of limitations defense. There was no claim of a special relationship between the parties or that after the term of the lease defendant engaged in wrongful conduct related to wrongful acts committed during the term of the lease. However, any continuing statutory obligation defendant might have had as a result of pollution it caused during the lease ran only to the state or federal government.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for summary judgment was granted because the statute of limitations barred recovery for pollution caused by defendant where defendant had no continuing duty to plaintiff which would extend the limitations period.

Gomola v. Eastwood


CV 980358191


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 974



April 13, 1999, Decided  
April 13, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervening defendant firefighter sought temporary injunctive relief to have the court decide whether plaintiff firefighter's formal installation to a captaincy slot ought to be enjoined, and to decide whether defendant's constitutional rights under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV were violated.


OVERVIEW: In an action involving two firefighters vying for promotion to a single captaincy slot due to an incorrectly scored written exam, intervening defendant firefighter sought temporary injunctive relief, defendant asked the court to determine whether plaintiff firefighter's formal installation ought to be enjoined, and to decide whether defendant was victimized by unlawful overstepping by the Fire Commission in derogation of any due process entitlement defendant might have had in his originally higher place on an uncorrected pre-amendment examination results list. The court concluded that the Commission acted properly, within its rights and powers, and that defendant had no compelling claim to procedural protections deriving from any entitlement purportedly bestowed by his original place on the incorrectly scored list. Because defendant's higher rank was due to incorrect scoring, he did not have a legitimate claim of entitlement to the higher rank. The court held that defendant did not have a constitutionally protected interest in his ranking and denied all equitable relief sought.


OUTCOME: The court found that intervening defendant did not have a legitimate claim of entitlement to the single captaincy slot and denied the equitable relief sought.

101-115 S. Main v. City of Waterbury


CV 940120628S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 796



March 26, 1999, Decided  
March 30, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion for summary judgment on the grounds that a genuine issue of material fact exists denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment from the Board of Tax Review (Connecticut) denying its request to revalue its property for the grand list for the years 1993-1997. Defendant city moved for summary judgment on grounds that its property valuations conformed to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62h.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer filed suit against defendant city seeking revaluation of its property. Plaintiff claimed that defendant failed to implement decennial revaluation for the grand property tax list of October 1, 1990. Plaintiff alleged that defendant improperly continued to value plaintiff's property at the October 1, 1980 fair market valuation and that resulting grand lists for October 1, 1993-1997 were grossly excessive, disproportionate, and unlawful valuations. Defendant moved for summary judgment, arguing that it properly stayed the valuations pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62h. The court found that section 12-62h allowed municipalities to suspend implementation of a decennial revaluation for up two years pending property tax reform in 1995. The court noted that defendant had attached minutes of Board of Alderman meetings to prove it had acted properly under section 12-62h. While section 12-62h was retroactive, defendant's acts were insufficient to prove that it properly postponed decennial revaluation all the way back to 1990. Because there was a genuine issue as to whether defendant's acts between 1990-1994 were proper, its motion for summary judgment was denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant city's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff taxpayer's suit seeking property revaluation was denied. Property tax reform statutes were retroactive, but a genuine issue of material fact remained as to whether defendant's acts properly postponed decennial valuation under the statute.

Sloan v. Tarascio

DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus against respondent warden in connection with attempted murder and assault convictions in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a and 53a-49.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus against respondent warden based on the allegation his convictions for assault and attempted murder were unconstitutional when he was denied effective assistance of trial and appellate counsel. The court noted a habeas petitioner who alleged ineffective assistance was required to demonstrate his counsel's performance was deficient and outside the range of reasonable professional assistance and that the deficient performance prejudiced him such that there was a reasonable probability that but for the deficient performance, the proceeding's result would have been different. The court denied petitioner's habeas corpus request, concluding counsel's performance with respect to cross-examination of a witness to establish petitioner's alleged intoxication during the shooting was not below a level of reasonable representation. The court further found petitioner failed to show the jury charge was legally incorrect such that counsel's failure to object was deficient. The court found petitioner did not show he was prejudiced by appellate counsel's failure to pursue unmeritorious claims on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's habeas corpus request, in respondent warden's favor, because petitioner failed to demonstrate that his trial or appellate counsel's representation fell below a level of reasonable professional assistance or that he suffered prejudice as a result of such alleged deficient performance.

State v. Cutler


CR 9660866


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 787



March 22, 1999, Decided  
March 22, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion for Judgment of Acquittal Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for a judgment of acquittal as to the count charging him with sexual assault in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A), and the count charging him with violating the Connecticut Risk of Injury Statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in a multiple count information, which included a count charging defendant with sexual assault in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A), and a count charging defendant with violating the Connecticut Risk of Injury Statute. Defendant moved for a judgment of acquittal as to these two counts. The court denied defendant's motion. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to have found defendant guilty of these two counts. The court rejected defendant's claims that the section of the Risk of Injury Statute was repealed by implication as the result of amendments to that statute. The section of the statute under which defendant was charged was virtually identical to the former Risk of Injury Statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal, holding there was sufficient evidence for jury to have found defendant guilty, that the sexual assault statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied, and that the section of the Risk of Injury Statute was not repealed by amendments to that statute.

Daniels v. Warden


CV 970573895S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 819



March 18, 1999, Decided  
March 18, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 13, 1999..



DISPOSITION: Petition denied except for relief requested that orders the effective date of the sentence to be June 7, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a motion for habeas corpus relief seeking relief from his sentence to a term of fifteen years execution, suspended after ten years.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's habeas corpus petition seeking relief from his sentence to a term of fifteen years execution, suspended after ten years, was denied. In denying petitioner's habeas petition, the court held that petitioner failed to meet his burden of establishing that he had ineffective assistance of counsel and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a was unconstitutional. According to the court, to succeed on an ineffective assistance of counsel claim a petitioner must show that there was reasonable probability that but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceedings would have been different. The court held that petitioner failed to prove this issue. The court then held that the amendment of § 54-125a was not unconstitutional. The court found that although § 54-125a added a limitation to the Board of Parole's authority it did not give an inmate any right to demand or even apply for parole, nor did it require the Board to actually consider any inmate's eligibility for parole even if he had fulfilled the statute's requirements. Thus, the court held that petitioner did not have an absolute right to be paroled.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's habeas corpus petition seeking relief from the sentence imposed because petitioner failed to establish that but for his trial counsel's unprofessional errors the proceedings would have been different. The court further held that petitioner did not have an absolute right to demand or even apply for parole.

 

1344 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Albahary v. City of Bristol


CV 970482781


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 749



March 16, 1999, Decided  
March 16, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Albahary v. City of Bristol, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 338 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 3, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Albahary v. City & Town of Bristol, 963 F. Supp. 150, 1997 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11535 (D. Conn., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' cross-motion for summary judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city moved for summary judgment, and plaintiff landowners cross-moved for summary judgment, after plaintiffs moved the court to enjoin defendant from obtaining easement rights on plaintiffs' property through a condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city entered into a consent order with the state department of environmental protection, which required defendant to investigate the migration of contaminants from a landfill and to remediate the contamination. The state legislature enacted a special act to allow defendant to acquire by condemnation certain rights in property located outside its corporate limits. Defendant began condemnation proceedings for easement rights on plaintiffs' property, which was adjacent to the landfill. Plaintiffs moved for declaratory and injunctive relief. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. Both the special act and the taking were constitutional because they served a legitimate governmental purpose. Defendant's compliance with the consent order allowed defendant to contain the level of water contamination caused by defendant's landfill. In turn, the special act allowed defendant to comply with the consent order by giving defendant the rights it needed to condemn property outside its borders. Similarly, the taking was a necessary means to achieve the abatement of contamination, and thus the taking was for a public use.


OUTCOME: The court granted a motion by defendant city for summary judgment after plaintiff landowners moved to enjoin defendant from obtaining easement rights on plaintiffs' property. The special act that conferred upon defendant the right to condemn property outside its borders, and the taking of plaintiffs' property, were both constitutional because they served a legitimate governmental purpose of abating contamination from a landfill.

Torres v. Connecticut Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities


CV 950323545S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 675



March 11, 1999, Decided  
March 11, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision, by the Connecticut Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities, dismissing the plaintiff's complaint which alleged that employer committed acts of ethnic and national origin discrimination prohibited by Title VII of the Civil Rights At of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000 et seq. Plaintiff argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-83(a) was unconstitutionally vague and dismissal of the complaint was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Following a decision by the defendant human rights commission, dismissing plaintiff employee's complaint, alleging employer committed acts of ethnic and national origin discrimination in violation of Title VII of Civil Rights At of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000 et seq., plaintiff appealed the decision. The court held Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-83, the statutory provision under which plaintiff's complaint was dismissed because the claim purportedly had no real possibility of succeeding, was not void for vagueness either facially or as applied to plaintiff. The court held Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46-83 used terms of common usage having a plain and ordinary meaning, the "no real possibility" standard was explained to the plaintiff, and the dismissal standard recognized in other legal settings. The court held that the evidence reasonably provided a basis for defendant to believe that no discrimination against plaintiff had taken place. Plaintiff provided no evidence that employer disciplined plaintiff for failing to speak English in certain work settings. Plaintiff appeared to be bilingual and fluent in English. The employer's requirement to speak English was directed at those who spoke Portuguese.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant human rights commission decision to dismiss plaintiff employee's complaint alleging employer acts of ethnic and national origin discrimination in violation of Title VII. Statute under which defendant dismissed plaintiff's claim was not void for vagueness because it employed recognized legal standard which had been explained to the plaintiff. Evidence established that employer did not discriminate against plaintiff.

Wellspeak v. Commissioner


CV 980492611S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 719



March 9, 1999, Decided  
March 9, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed an administrative suspension of his driver's license for refusing to take a blood alcohol test after his arrest in Massachusetts for driving while under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff driver appealed an administrative decision of defendant, the Commissioner of the Department of Motor Vehicles, suspending his driver's license pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. 14-227b for refusing to take a blood alcohol test after his arrest in Massachusetts for driving while under the influence of alcohol. Plaintiff claimed that the suspension violated his rights to due process and constituted double jeopardy because he was not given notice of the Connecticut consequences of his refusal to allow Massachusetts authorities to test his blood alcohol, and he was punished twice for the same offense. The court affirmed defendant commissioner's decision because plaintiff had notice that his driving privileges could be suspended by refusing the test, and an administrative suspension of a criminal defendant's driver's license did not constitute multiple punishment for the same offense.


OUTCOME: The administrative suspension of plaintiff's driver's license was affirmed because plaintiff was notified that suspension could result from refusing the blood alcohol test, and administrative suspension did not constitute multiple punishment for the same offense.

Doe v. Statewide Griev. Comm.


CV 990422129S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 417



February 23, 1999, Decided  
February 23, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Proceed by Fictitious Name denied. Court vacates temporary ex parte order allowing him to do so and directs clerk to unseal affidavit and redenominate file under plaintiff's actual name.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a request that he be allowed to proceed under a fictitious name to avoid alleged embarrassment and stigma attached to the substance of his claim before defendant Statewide Grievance Committee (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: One of plaintiff's former clients filed an attorney misconduct complaint with the Statewide Grievance Committee (Connecticut). The complaint was referred to a local grievance panel, which found probable cause that plaintiff had engaged in misconduct after conducting confidential proceedings. The local panel referred the matter back to the statewide committee for further action. A public hearing was held on the record; plaintiff's actual name was used during these proceedings. After a three year delay, plaintiff filed a motion to enjoin further proceedings, requesting that he be allowed to proceed under a fictitious name on the theory that if the proceedings were enjoined, it was as though probable cause were never found, and he would be entitled to the confidentiality provided to respondents under the Connecticut Practice Book rules. The court denied his request, holding that only where no probable cause was found were such matters kept confidential. The court further held that plaintiff's personal embarrassment at being a respondent in the underlying proceedings did not provide a compelling reason to allow him to proceed anonymously.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff's motion to proceed under a fictitious name, vacating the temporary ex parte order allowing him to do so and directing the clerk to unseal the affidavit and redenominate the file under the plaintiff's actual name. Plaintiff's personal embarrassment at being a respondent in an administrative action involving his conduct as an attorney was not a compelling reason to permit him to proceed anonymously.

State v. Local 387 of Council 4 AFSCME


CV 980579805


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD

February 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: State's application to vacate granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state applied to vacate an order of the arbitrator reinstating grievant, a corrections officer who had been terminated for behavior amounting to second-degree harassment in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-183(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Grievant, a guard with the Department of Corrections, heard that a member of the state Senate referred to correction officers as "criminals." Grievant used a department telephone to call the senator's office and leave a racially charged, vulgar message. The corrections department fired grievant, and the superior court ordered grievant to complete a rehabilitation program. Grievant's union sought his reinstatement. The arbitrator of the state Department of Labor vacated the termination, citing grievant's positive employment record and personal difficulties, and ordered the state to reinstate grievant. The state applied to vacate the arbitrator's award. The court granted the application. The reinstatement was unenforceable as it was against the public policy disallowing the continued employment of individuals who have harassed others using racist, offensive language. The behavior constituted second-degree harassment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-183 and violated several departmental regulations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the application to vacate grievant's reinstatement; the continued employment of the grievant ran counter to the public policy of prevention of such offensive harassment.

Animal Rights Front v. Rocque


CV 970575920


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 343



January 26, 1999, Decided  
January 26, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion for order of notice is denied, except as to the Groton Long Point Association.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Commissioner for the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection (DEP), moved to compel plaintiff, an animal rights organization, to provide proper notice in accordance with Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 17-55 regarding plaintiff's request for declaratory and injunctive relief. Plaintiff claimed that the DEP violated Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-16 and 26-86f when the DEP supervised controlled hunts during which fawn deer were killed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an animal rights group, alleged that the state department of environmental protection (DEP), supervised controlled hunts during which fawn deer were killed in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-16 and 26-86f. Plaintiff filed suit against defendant, DEP's commissioner, requesting declaratory and injunctive relief. Defendant moved to compel plaintiff to provide proper notice, in accordance with Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 17-55, to licensed hunters, private property owners who permitted deer hunting on their land, and a private association on whose land some of the hunting had taken place. The court denied defendant's motion except with respect to the private association. A decision in the case as to whether defendant's activities in certain locations destroyed a natural resource did not affect the rights or interests of private property owners or licensed hunters. However, the private association that owned the land where the hunting took place did have a direct interest in the action and could be affected by a declaration. Thus, plaintiff was required to give proper notice to the private association.


OUTCOME: The court denied, with one exception, a motion by defendant, an environmental protection commissioner, to compel plaintiff, an animal rights organization, to provide proper notice regarding plaintiff's request for declaratory and injunctive relief. The court denied the motion with respect to private landowners and licensed hunters but granted the motion with respect to a private association on whose land allegedly illegal hunting took place.

DeVivo v. DeVivo


CV 980581020S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 158



January 19, 1999, Decided  
January 19, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The court denied the plaintiff's motion to strike the defendants' notice of election and the defendants' supplemental notice of election. The court also granted the defendants' motion pursuant to General Statutes 33-900(d) to stay judicial proceedings and to determine the fair value of the plaintiff's shares.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a motion to strike defendants' notice of election and defendants' supplemental notice of election. Defendants filed a motion pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-900(d) to stay judicial proceedings and to determine the fair value of plaintiff's shares of a corporation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owned stock in defendant corporation and served as one of the two directors. Defendant director owned the remainder of the stock and served as its president. Plaintiff filed a complaint seeking judicial dissolution of corporation. Plaintiff filed an amended complaint seeking dissolution based solely on deadlock of directors in the management of the corporation. Plaintiff's motion to strike defendant's notices of election to purchase in lieu of dissolution was denied. Defendants' motion to stay judicial proceedings pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-900(d) and to determine the fair value of the shares was granted. Plaintiff provided the same set of facts under both complaints. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-900(a) did not clearly state under what section a purchase in lieu of dissolution could be maintained. The amendment between when plaintiff filed the original complaint and the amended complaint attempted to clarify the existing statute. By adopting the technical changes, the legislature made it apparent that the omission of a reference to shareholder or director deadlock was inadvertent. The amendment had a retroactive effect on the statute.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion and denied plaintiff's motion because changes made to the statute were merely technical and only revised the statute as it existed when plaintiff filed the original complaint.

Velez v. Commissioner of Correction


CV 972573S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 42



January 11, 1999, Decided  
January 11, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of December 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3373. As Corrected December 22, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3374.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus following his convictions of burglary, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103; failure to appear; Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172; larceny, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125b; and robbery, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135. Plaintiff claimed his confinement was unlawful because respondent Commissioner of Corrections held him beyond his lawful release date.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of burglary, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103; failure to appear; Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172; larceny, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125b; and robbery, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135. He was sentenced to the custody of respondent Commissioner of Corrections for a period of years. He sought a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that respondent unlawfully held him beyond his lawful release date. The court dismissed his petition and held that subject matter jurisdiction for adjudicating habeas petitions was conferred on the court by Conn. Gen. Stat. §52-466, which gave the court the authority to hear those petitions that alleged illegal confinement or deprivation of liberty. Petitioner alleged sufficient facts for the court's jurisdiction to apply. Petitioner would have been eligible for release at the date he estimated, if he had been eligible for good time credits. The court determined that he had not been eligible.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for a writ of habeas corpus following petitioner's convictions of robbery, burglary, failure to appear and larceny because petitioner's argument, that he was unlawfully held by respondent commissioner of corrections, failed when the court determined that petitioner had not been eligible for good time credits.

Robinson v. Warden


CV 97405187S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 31



January 7, 1999, Decided  
January 7, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent warden moved to dismiss petitioner's habeas corpus petition count wherein petitioner alleged that an increase in minimum time served before parole eligibility from 50 percent of one's sentence to 85 percent constituted retroactively applied increased punishment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a guilty plea at a time when the law allowed the parole board to consider parole for a prisoner convicted of petitioner's crimes after the prisoner served 50 percent of his sentence. The law in place at the time petitioner was sentenced required a prisoner to serve 85 percent of his sentence before he was eligible for parole. Petitioner filed a habeas corpus petition claiming that the increase in the required time to be served constituted a retroactively applied increased punishment. After construing the allegations in petitioner's complaint in their most favorable light, the court found that petitioner alleged facts that supported a claim for violation of the ex post facto clause of the U.S. Const. art. I, § 9. Therefore, the court determined that the violation gave the court subject matter jurisdiction and concluded that the action was properly before the court. Accordingly, the court denied respondent warden's motion to dismiss defendant's claim.


OUTCOME: Respondent warden's claim to dismiss defendant's claim under his habeas corpus petition was denied, because defendant raised a sufficient allegation of a violation of the ex post facto clause of the U.S. Const., which gave the court subject matter jurisdiction over the claim.

In re Sheily C.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183, plaintiff father appealed a decision from the Department of Children and Families (Connecticut), which approved a treatment plan for plaintiff's children that stopped his visitation with the children.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff father was involved in neglect proceedings wherein the trial court committed the care and custody of his children to the Department of Children and Families (DCF). Plaintiff appealed challenging the ruling of a DCF hearing officer, which approved a DCF treatment plan that stopped his visitation with the children. Plaintiff alleged that the hearing officer's findings were inconsistent with the evidence presented and that the officer acted arbitrarily and in abuse of his discretion. Plaintiff also contended that the DCF's final decision violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection. The court found that hearing officer's final decision was consistent with the evidence presented at the hearing and based upon substantial evidence, which supported the conclusion that the DCF treatment plan denying visitation was in the children's best interests. Finally, the court found that plaintiff received a full and fair opportunity to be heard on the issue of visitation and that he was accorded due process with respect to the DCF treatment plan. Accordingly, plaintiff's appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered dismissing plaintiff father's appeal because the decision to deny plaintiff visitation with his children was not illegal, arbitrary, capricious, unconstitutional, or an abuse of the hearing officer's discretion.

ATC Pshp. v. Town of Windham


CV 95248230S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 7



January 4, 1999, Decided  
January 4, 1999, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Governmental defendants' moved to strike plaintiff's third amended revised complaint, which sought damages as a result of defendants' alleged deprivation of plaintiff's right to substantive due process under both the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Prior to governmental defendants' condemnation of real property, plaintiff brought suit for damages alleging that defendants' arbitrary and oppressive conduct in condemning plaintiff's property violated plaintiff's right to substantive due process of law under both the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as well as Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. Defendants filed a motion to strike plaintiff's complaint. With regard to plaintiff's taking without just compensation claim, the court found that claim was not ripe under the Williamson doctrine because plaintiff failed to exhaust its available state remedies. Further, the court found that plaintiff's claim did not rise to a violation of substantive due process, especially in light of the availability of post-deprivation remedies. Finally, the court concluded that the Connecticut constitution did not provide for a direct cause of action for damages resulting from an alleged deprivation of substantive due process. Accordingly, the motion to strike was granted.


OUTCOME: Governmental defendants' motion to strike was granted because plaintiff failed to exhaust its available state remedies with respect to its substantive due process claims, thereby rendering the complaint unripe for adjudication. Further, the court concluded that the state constitution did not provide a direct cause of action for damages as a result of an alleged deprivation of substantive due process.

Seymour v. State Elections Enforcement Comm'n


CV 980579752


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3590



December 16, 1998, Decided  
December 16, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed and the appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut Elections Enforcement Commission found plaintiff candidates in technical violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-333w for failing to indicate "Paid for by" on certain press releases. The candidates appealed, challenging legislative control over the commission's membership, the authorization of disclosure of election law violation complaints, and the alleged selective application of the election laws to their press releases.


OVERVIEW: The candidates claimed: (1) the commission, part of the executive branch, was undermined because four of the five members were appointed by the legislature; (2) complaints to the commission resulted in a disclosure of political associations and unfavorable publicity concerning unsubstantiated charges; and (3) other candidates sent similar press releases which lacked for "Paid for by" attribution but were not prosecuted. The court held: (1) there was no Connecticut precedent suggesting that legislative appointments of commissions which serve executive functions violated the separation of powers provisions, federal law relied on by the candidates was distinguishable on the basis of the appointments clause, and state law rejected a rigid application of the separation of powers doctrine, so the candidates failed to demonstrate the unconstitutional composition of the commission; (2) the disclosure was proper under the Freedom of Information Act (FOIA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-10 et seq.; and (3) the candidates did not identify any other press release or candidate that was treated differently. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-333w(c) was not applicable to candidates.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed and the appeal was dismissed.

Silver Shield Ass'n v. Town of Greenwich


CV 980166321


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3628



December 14, 1998, Decided  
December 15, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town and chief of police filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff association and members' complaint for a declaratory judgment on the grounds that the plaintiffs failed to exhaust the administrative remedies available to them under their collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff association and members filed a complaint that sought declaratory judgment against defendant town and chief of police. Plaintiff association was the exclusive bargaining representative for all of the town's uniformed police personnel. Plaintiff members alleged they were the subjects of formal internal investigations based on internal complaints of employees within the police department. Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment to determine whether the police manual was unconstitutionally void for vagueness, as applied to them, and whether the police regulations deprived them of numerous constitutional rights. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint. The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss, finding that plaintiffs properly sought declaratory judgment regarding the constitutionality of the police manual that was a basis of defendants' actions against plaintiffs. Based upon Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51bb, the court held that administrative exhaustion was not necessary because plaintiffs' allegation for declaratory judgment was that the police manual, which was the basis for the administrative proceedings, violated plaintiffs' constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant town and chief of police's motion to dismiss plaintiff association and members' complaint. The court found that plaintiffs' claim disputed further proceedings because they questioned the constitutionality of the police manual, which was a basis of the proceedings; therefore, plaintiffs were not required to totally exhaust administrative remedies.

Komondy v. Chester Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV 9680207


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3491



December 8, 1998, Decided  
December 8, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b) from the decision of defendant Chester Zoning Board of Appeals (Connecticut), which upheld a cease and desist order issued by the Chester Zoning Compliance Officer. Plaintiffs had been granted a special exception for the use of their premises and a box trailer for administrative offices; warehousing and wholesaling; order fulfillment; and philatelic mail order.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners claimed that defendant zoning board erred in upholding a cease and desist order issued by a zoning compliance officer. Plaintiffs purchased their property after authorities determined that a prior non-conforming use for a light manufacturing business could be continued. A special exception was granted plaintiffs to allow use of the premises for administrative offices; warehousing and wholesaling; order fulfillment; and philatelic mail order. The challenged order required plaintiffs to remove box trailers from the property. The court affirmed defendant's ruling, holding that the zoning permit authorized plaintiffs to place storage trailers on the premises to temporarily store materials and tools incident to the construction and repair of the business at that location. Plaintiffs' trailer, however, contained personal items stored incident to plaintiffs' move into an adjacent residence. Clearly, such use was not in keeping with the usage authorized by the zoning permit. Because the record contained substantial evidence that the actual usage of the trailer varied from that permitted by the zoning permit, the court upheld defendant's decision.


OUTCOME: The court found that defendant zoning board's decision upholding the cease and desist order was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or illegal. Instead, the court found that defendant's decision was supported by substantial evidence in the record, because plaintiff property owners were no longer using the subject trailer for the purposes authorized in their special permit.

 

1358 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Town of Mansfield


CV 9764114S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3432



December 3, 1998, Decided  
December 3, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the decision of the Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Mansfield (Connecticut), which denied his application for a finding of zoning agent error in plaintiff's action to enforce a town ordinance regarding lighting.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner complained to defendant town about a neighbor's lighting system. No enforcement action was taken because the lighting was found to be a private nuisance. Plaintiff appealed to defendant zoning board, which denied the application, based upon absence of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court held that plaintiff satisfied the jurisdictional prerequisites of aggrievement, timeliness, and service of process. The court determined that defendant zoning board had jurisdiction over plaintiff's appeal because the action was an appeal from an enforcement action. The court remanded because defendant zoning board's denial was based upon its erroneous belief that it did not have jurisdiction, and thus, the court could not properly entertain the appeal. Plaintiff's constitutional challenge of the zoning regulation failed because he could not seek relief from a regulation and in the same proceeding challenge its constitutionality. Further, the delegation to defendant zoning board of the right to determine whether a complaint constituted a private nuisance was valid because it was not unconstitutionally vague where it contained intelligible standards upon which to act.


OUTCOME: The court remanded because defendant zoning board did not deny plaintiff property owner's application for a finding of zoning agent error based upon the merits of the claim, but rather on the erroneous assumption that it lacked jurisdiction. The court also held that plaintiff could not challenge the subject zoning regulation as he was seeking to enforce the regulation and further, the regulation was not unconstitutionally vague.

National Loan Investors, L.P. v. Reale


CV 980577024


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3610



December 3, 1998, Decided  
December 3, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike the second special defense denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor filed a motion in its action against defendant debtor to foreclose a judgment lien, to strike defendant's special defenses under the homestead exemption, unclean hands doctrine, and Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUPTA), and on defendant's counterclaims that alleged a violation of CUPTA and negligent infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditor filed an action against defendant debtor seeking to foreclose a judgment lien. Defendant asserted the special defenses of homestead exemption, unclean hands, and the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUPTA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(a). Defendant also asserted counterclaims, alleging violations of CUPTA and negligent infliction of emotional distress. The plaintiff filed a motion to strike defendant's special defenses and counterclaims. The court granted the motion to strike the special defenses of homestead exemption and CUPTA and the counterclaims. The court held that the homestead exemption was inapplicable because the action arose from a contract entered into in 1991. The court held that CUTPA was not available as a special defense and that the counterclaim asserted under CUPTA was without merit. Because defendant's counterclaim alleging negligent infliction of emotional distress contained no allegation of actual injury or causation, it failed to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted. The court denied the motion to strike the special defense of unclean hands because the defense was applicable to a foreclosure action.


OUTCOME: The court granted plaintiff creditor's motion to strike defendant debtor's special defenses under the homestead exemption and the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUPTA) and the counterclaims for a violation of CUPTA and negligent infliction of emotional distress. The court denied plaintiff's motion to strike the special defense under the unclean hands doctrine because it was available in a foreclosure action.

Sherwood v. Danbury Hosp.


CV 960324786S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3406



December 2, 1998, Decided  
December 2, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion for summary judgment as to counts one, two and three of the amended complaint, dated January 22, 1998, granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sued defendant hospital for negligence arising out of a blood transfusion received at the hospital from which patient contracted HIV virus. The hospital filed a motion to strike one count alleging violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, which was granted. The patient amended her complaint. The hospital filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The patient raised three counts in her amended complaint. In count one, she claimed, inter alia, that the hospital was negligent in 15 ways, including providing blood that was contaminated with the HIV virus, and failure to warn the patient of the risks of contamination. In count two, the patient claimed that a special fiduciary relationship existed between the parties. In count three, the patient claimed that the hospital was aware that the patient had a cause of action based upon the contaminated blood, but fraudulently concealed the cause of action from her. The hospital alleged that the claims were barred by the statute of limitations. The superior court held that: (1) whether the action was governed by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-584 or 52-777, the statute was not tolled by the continuous treatment doctrine; (2) the "discovery rule" was not applicable in Connecticut; (3) a fiduciary relationship did not toll the statute of limitations; (4) no evidence of fraudulent conceal was presented; and (5) Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-584 and 52-777 were constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for summary judgment as to the amended complaint was granted.

Porrino v. Town of Madison


CV 970402364


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3418



December 1, 1998, Decided  
December 1, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment may enter in favor of the defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners challenged a decision of defendant town planning and zoning commission (Connecticut), which denied their application for site plan approval to utilize property located in a rural shopping (RS) district as an automobile service station. The owners argued that the commission's action was unreasonable, illegal, arbitrary, capricious, and an abuse of discretion; or that the regulations were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought approval of a site plan to use property located adjacent to a shopping center in an RS zoned area as a gasoline filling station. After a hearing, the commission denied the application. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that: 1) under the Madison regulatory scheme, uses not permitted were excluded; 2) automobile service stations were businesses distinguished from retail stores and were not a permitted use in the RS district, under Madison, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 6.5.1.2; 3) having found an adequate regulatory basis for the commission's decision, the constitutional claims were dismissed; and 4) the owners had failed to establish, by a fair preponderance of the evidence, that the commission planning and zoning commission, in denying the owners' application for site plan approval, acted unreasonably, illegally, arbitrarily, capriciously or in abuse of its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the commission and dismissed the owners' appeal of the commission's denial of its site plan application.
