Peck v. Rattlesnake Ventures


CV 940139352


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335



November 19, 1998, Decided  
November 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court denies defendants' motion to set aside the verdict and for a remittitur as to Counts One and Five, and grants defendants' motion to set aside the verdict, made pursuant to Practice Book 16-35, as to Counts Two, Three, Six and Seven. Jury verdict remains in the amount of $ 225,000 on Count One and Five of the plaintiff's amended complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sued defendants, restaurant, employee, and others, for negligence per se in the operation of a restaurant and bar, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and negligent infliction of emotional distress. After a jury verdict in favor of the injured party, defendants filed several motions, including a motion for remittitur and a motion to set aside the verdict.


OVERVIEW: In their various motions, defendants argued there was insufficient evidence that they violated a local noise ordinance, the ordinance was unconstitutional, there was no basis on which the jury could have awarded economic damages, and the award for non-economic damages was excessive. The court concluded that defendants' claim of insufficient evidence for a finding of negligence per se was baseless. There was extensive testimony by police officers and experts that noise levels taken in the injured party's apartment substantially violated the allowable limits of the ordinance in the zoning district in which the injured party's apartment was located. With respect to the constitutionality of the ordinance, defendants made no serious arguments, presented no facts, and cited no law to substantiate that claim. As to the counts alleging intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress against the restaurant and the employee, the court concluded that they did not relate back to the original complaint, and constituted a new and different cause of action which was time barred.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motions to set aside the verdict and for remittitur were denied as to the counts alleging negligence per se against the restaurant and the employee. Defendants' motion to set aside the verdict was granted as to the counts alleging negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress against the restaurant and the employee.

State v. Philip Morris, Inc.


X02 CV 960148414S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3104



October 27, 1998, Decided  
October 27, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. Philip Morris, Inc., 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2067 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Court hereby denies the State's pending application for a prejudgment remedy without prejudice to its right to resubmit that application, together with a proper statutory notice of rights and all other appropriate documentation required by law, on or before November 10, 1998.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of Connecticut filed an action against defendant tobacco companies and claimed violations of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA) and the Connecticut Antitrust Act (Act). The state sought a prejudgment order to attach the assets of the companies pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278 et seq. in order to secure the state's potential recovery.


OVERVIEW: The state sought entry of a prejudgment order to attach the tobacco companies' assets in the amount of two billion dollars in the state's action for violations of the CUTPA and the Act.. The court held that the remedy of prejudgment attachment under § 52-278 was available to the state because it was a "person" within the meaning of the statute. However, the statute imposed mandatory notice, procedure, and hearing requirements, including documents and an application with specific verbiage as set out in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278c. Because the state failed to comply with the specific requirements of the statute, it was not entitled to the prejudgment attachment that it sought. However, the court ordered that the denial of the motion was without prejudice and noted that if the state reapplied for prejudgment attachment, the court would hold a hearing to determine whether the circumstances warranted such a drastic remedy.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state's application for a prejudgment attachment without prejudice to its right to resubmit that application.

 

1364 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Anson


CV 980579841S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3022



October 26, 1998, Decided  
October 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The defendants' motion to dismiss is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, commissioner of public works and others brought a motion to dismiss plaintiffs, association, subcontractors, and taxpayer's, action for injunctive relief and attorney fees in the association's action that challenged whether a bid package that contained a requirement that each bidder sign a project labor agreement (PLA) with the union and affiliated local unions agreeing to recognize the union as exclusive bargaining representative.


OVERVIEW: The contractors contended that they would have submitted bids if they were not required to enter into the PLA. The court granted the motion to dismiss, finding that the taxpayer had no standing to challenge the bidding process because he did not provide any information on how his pecuniary interests would be harmed. The court held that the subcontractors did not have standing because a diminished possibility of potential work as a subcontractor on a particular project was too attenuated an interest to give them a legal stake in the bidding process. The court found that the association had standing to bring the action on behalf of its members, but had not shown the existence of favoritism, fraud, or corruption in the bidding process. Thus, the association did not have standing to challenge the bidding process. The court determined whether using the PLA was actually an effective method of achieving the state's aims in completing a major public works project within the necessary time and financial constraints was not for the court to decide. Thus, the commissioner's decision to use the PLA was a legitimate exercise of his discretion.


OUTCOME: The court granted the commissioner and other's motion for dismissal of association, subcontractors, and taxpayer's action for injunctive relief that challenged the use of a PLA.

Doe v. State


410586


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2959



October 22, 1998, Decided  
October 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state filed a motion to dismiss an action filed by plaintiff an unsuccessful candidate for a job with the department of public safety.


OVERVIEW: The unsuccessful candidate brought an action against the state alleging that the department of public safety denied him a job because he disclosed that he was homosexual in a pre-employment polygraph test. He further alleged that the test administrator's report included remarks that did not fully and accurately reflect statements he made before and during the polygraph. The unsuccessful candidate argued that the amendment of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142, which listed the claims excepted from the claims commissioner's jurisdiction, waived the application of the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The state filed a motion to dismiss and argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142(2) did not waive sovereign immunity. The court ruled that nothing in the language, legislative history, or common law background of 1996 Conn. Acts 85, which amended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142, suggested that it was intended to diminish sovereign immunity or enlarge the state's waiver of the doctrine and thereby expand the jurisdiction of the court. Therefore, the court did not have jurisdiction over the unsuccessful candidate's claims.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion to dismiss the unsuccessful candidate's action.

McCluskey v. Redding Planning Comm'n


CV 970328626S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2924



October 20, 1998, Decided  
October 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The appeal of the plaintiffs, Malcolm M. McCluskey and Otto Kratzenburg, d/b/a 890 Realty Company, is SUSTAINED, except as to the modified conditions stated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed an application with defendant Redding, Connecticut, Planning Commission (commission) seeking approval of a subdivision. The commission approved the application, subject to six specific conditions, in addition to standard modifications and conditions of approval. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners argued that the conditions imposed by the commission constituted an abuse of discretion. Specifically, the property owners challenged the requirements that: (1) stop signs be provided at an intersection, (2) area be added to a right of way, (3) the side of a road be redesigned, and (4) the design of a turnaround be acceptable to the planning consultants. The parties agreed that the commission had no jurisdiction over the maintenance of roads or placement of stop signs. Thus, the appeal was sustained related to the stop sign requirement. It was also agreed that the commission could require that the right of way be widened. The court held that the commission could not require a developer to improve an existing abutting highway where no intersecting streets were being created. Although the commission could have required the deeding of property to the town as a condition of subdivision approval, no authority existed for the demand that an applicant design or reconfigure an existing public highway. The property owners' obligation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25 was met once land sufficient for road widening purposes was deeded to the town.


OUTCOME: It was agreed that the condition requiring stop signs was improper and that the commission could require the deeding of property for the right of way. The unchallenged conditions for approval remained. The conditions appealed from were modified as follows: (1) area was ordered to be added to a road right-of-way, and (2) the extension of a road and the turnaround was ordered to be deeded to the town.

Maderos v. City of Shelton


CV 970058185S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2813



October 8, 1998, Decided  
October 8, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought to strike each of the special defenses contained in the answer of defendant, the city's central medical emergency dispatcher, as being legally insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Each special defense raised was related to a claim by the dispatcher that it enjoyed a form of immunity from liability for the claims alleged in plaintiff's complaint. The court noted that the motion to strike could not be granted as to those first special defense regarding allegations involving factual issues which were not properly resolved on a motion to strike. Regarding the third special defense to count three, the dispatcher alleged that it was immune from liability pursuant to the common law doctrine of municipal immunity. The court agreed with plaintiff, however, that the common law doctrine of municipal immunity had been wholly supplanted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n. Therefore, the third special defense to count three was stricken. Regarding allegations that the dispatcher's actions were wilful and wanton, the court determined that such allegations also involved factual issues which were not properly resolved on a motion to strike. Although plaintiff claimed that the statutory protection provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-311 did not extend to the dispatcher, this claim also involved factual issues which could not be decided on a motion to strike.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to the third special defense to count three involving the dispatcher's claim that it was immune from liability pursuant to the common law doctrine of municipal immunity, but the motion was denied as to the remaining special defenses.

Shomsky v. City of Shelton Police Dep't


CV 970058215S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD

October 8, 1998, Decided

DISPOSITION: The motion to strike is granted as to the third special defense to count three and the third special defense to count twenty-one, but is denied as to the remaining special defenses.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the executor of decedent's estate, filed a negligence action against defendant police department and the medical emergency dispatcher. The plaintiff filed a motion to strike each of the special defenses contained in the dispatcher's answer.


OVERVIEW: Each special defense related to a claim by the dispatcher that it enjoyed a form of immunity from liability for the claims alleged in the plaintiff's complaint. The defense alleging that it was immune from liability pursuant to the common law doctrine of municipal immunity was stricken, because the common law doctrine of municipal immunity was wholly supplanted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n. Whether the alleged injury was due to the act or omission of someone other than an employee, officer, or agent of the political subdivision was a factual issue and thus could not be decided on the basis of a motion to strike. The special defenses bases on statutory immunity raised factual issues for the finder of fact.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to the third special defense to count 3 and the third special defense to count 21, defenses based on the common law doctrine of municipal immunity. The motion to strike was denied as to all other special defenses.

Marlow v. Norgren


CV 980409958


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2828



October 7, 1998, Decided  
October 7, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state employees, asserting that they were immune from liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, sought to dismiss claims brought against them by plaintiff parents for trespass, infliction of emotional distress, violations of U.S. Const. amend. IV and XIV, and violations under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988. The parents also filed claims against defendants, a police officer and employees of a child care center.


OVERVIEW: The three state employees worked for the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DFC). The parents alleged that when the employees of the child care center reported that the parents abused their minor children, the state employees, acting within their scope of employment, trespassed upon the parents' property which caused the parents extreme emotional distress. They also alleged that the state employees' acts violated their rights guaranteed under U.S. Const. amend. IV and XIV and under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988. The court granted the state employees' motion to dismiss the parents' claim of trespass against them and held that the parents' allegations under their trespass claim regarding malice were conclusory. However, the court denied the motion as to the parents' claims of a violation of their rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and as to the parents' claims that the state employees inflicted emotional distress upon them when they threatened to brand them as abusers. Specifically, the court held that such acts were outside the scope of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 and that malice was properly alleged.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state employees' motion to dismiss the trespass claim, but denied the motion to dismiss as to the parents' remaining claims.

SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2799



September 28, 1998, Decided  
September 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Board's motion for summary judgment granted, and the court declares that the amendments to 3.18 and 14 of the charter were and are invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Board of Education of the Town and Borough of Naugatuck (Connecticut), filed an action for declaratory judgment against defendant Town. Both parties filed for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The voters of the Town of Naugatuck (Connecticut) adopted two amendments to the borough's charter: (1) the manner in which the Board of Education's budget was adopted each year, the budget amendment; and (2) the membership of the Board, the membership amendment. The Board brought an action against the town itself claiming the amendments were illegal and invalid in that they exceeded the town's powers under the Home Rule Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 99. The reviewing court held that the amendment permitting the town mayor to be a member of the board would result in the attempt by one person to faithfully and impartially discharge the duties of both. Under the general rule, a person could not hold two public offices that were incompatible. The mayor's divided loyalties created potential and probable conflicts of interest.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1371 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Town of Griswold


113592


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2706



September 21, 1998, Decided  
September 21, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant Town of Griswold's motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiffs for damages for alleged constitutional violations resulting from defendant town's decision to grant a special exception to construct a water filtration plant, the town filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought damages for alleged constitutional violations resulting from the town's decision to grant a special exception to construct a water filtration plant. The town filed a motion to dismissthe complaint. The court found that this case was brought as an administrative appeal, which was dismissed for failure to exhaust administrative remedies and failure to identify a statutory right to bring an appeal directly to the superior court. The court noted that if an adequate administrative remedy existed, it must be exhausted before the superior court would obtain jurisdiction to act in the matter. The exhaustion doctrine reflected the legislative intent that such issues be handled in the first instance by local administrative officials in order to provide aggrieved persons with full and adequate administrative relief. In this case, the court found that plaintiffs were merely attempting to relitigate their dispute with the town's decision by now claiming constitutional violations. Accordingly, the court granted the town's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: In an action by plaintiffs for damages for alleged constitutional violations resulting from the town's decision to grant a special exception to construct a water filtration plant, the court granted the town's motion to dismiss.

Tunxis Recycling Operating Comm. v. Automated Container Recovery


CV 980486403S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2566



September 11, 1998, Decided  
September 11, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: TROC's application to vacate the arbitration award denied, and ACPI's amended counterclaim seeking affirmation of the arbitration award granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant processor filed a demand for arbitration asserting claims of breach of contract and Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA) violations against plaintiff committee. The arbitrator issued an award in favor of the processor. The committee filed an application to vacate the award. The processor filed a counterclaim seeking confirmation of the award.


OVERVIEW: The committee argued that the award violated public policy by permitting the processor to recover fees during a period on which it lacked a permit and violated state law, the award was contrary to the contract, and the arbitrator failed to reach an award on the subject matter submitted to him. The superior court noted that the only submission to the arbitrator were for breach of contract and CUTPA violations; thus, the effect of the case claimed by the committee was not part of the submission, and not subject to the decision of the arbitrator. Additionally, the evidence demonstrated that the DEP had not taken any serious action against the processor for its alleged violations of the environmental statutes, although it unquestionably had the power to do so and was well aware of the processor's conduct. Thus, the court could not find the award violated a public policy. Finally, the award was not contrary to the contract because the processor did obtain permits; thus, it was reasonable to find the processor was not in breach of contract.


OUTCOME: The application to vacate the arbitration award was denied, and the counterclaim seeking affirmation of the arbitration award was granted.

Ex rel. Tylious T.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) filed petitions for the termination of the parental rights of respondent biological mother to her three children. DCF also sought an adjudication of the rights of respondent fathers.


OVERVIEW: Two of mother's children were placed in foster care after an older sibling died from an unexplained brain injury while he was in the mother's care. The youngest child was born after her sibling's death and was immediately placed in foster care because the mother was incarcerated. DCF initiated neglect proceedings against the mother. The court terminated the mother's rights to the three children. After the commencement of the trial, the court allowed DCF to amend its neglect petition and to withdraw the termination petition in regard to the youngest child's father. This was proper pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super Ct. § 35-1 which allowed a petition to be amended any time prior to a final adjudication. Petition amendments were liberally permitted and the amendment did not cause the surprise, unfairness, occasioned no delay, and did not increase the mother's trial burden. It was proved by clear and convincing evidence that the two older siblings fathers had abandoned their children because neither father had pursued visitation, or displayed affection, love, or concern for the children.


OUTCOME: The court terminated the biological mother's parental rights to the three children. The youngest child was to remain committed with DCF for one year, and the other two children were to be placed for the purpose of securing an adoptive family.

South Cent. Conn. Reg'l Water Auth. v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals

DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal of the defendant's denial of its first variance application dismissed; plaintiff's appeal of the defendant's second variance application sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff water authority sought review of the decision of defendant Zoning Board of Appeals' two decisions to deny plaintiff's requests for a variance from the Milford, Conn., Zoning Regulation § 9, to increase the size of a public utility water distribution tank.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, through it's water tank supplied the area's water for private use and for fire safety. Plaintiff sought to build a larger water tower at a higher elevation in order to better meet the needs of the growing community and requested a variance. The Board denied the first request for a variance and also denied plaintiff's second request, following plaintiff's changes to its plans. The court affirmed the denial of the first request and reversed the denial of the second request. The court found that the grounds espoused by the Board for its first denial were reasonably supported by the record and pertinent to the considerations under the local zoning regulations. The court determined that the Board's reasons for its second denial - namely that plaintiff could have considered other locations for the water tower in no way related to the relevant considerations. The court concluded that plaintiff showed that based on the property's low elevation, enforcement of the zoning regulations would result in unusual hardship and that construction of the new tower would benefit public health and welfare and therefore the variance should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of plaintiff's first request for a variance and reversed the Board's denial of plaintiff's second request for a variance.

Planning & Zoning Comm'n v. Ostrager


537457


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2473



August 25, 1998, Decided  
August 27, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was plaintiff zoning commission's motion for an injunction to be issued against defendant property owners to direct them from ceasing to occupy certain premises located in the Town of Lebanon on a year round basis on the ground that such an occupation was in violation of a zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The property owners had owned certain premises located in the Town of Lebanon. The property owners had received a cease desist order that directed them to discontinue the use of the subject premises on a year round basis because such a use had violated the Town of Lebanon, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 4.4a. When the property owners had refused to comply with this order, the zoning commission had filed a motion for an injunction to compel them from ceasing to occupy the premises at issue on a year round basis. The court issued a judgment that granted the zoning commission's motion for an injunction. The court did not find the zoning regulations at issue were unconstitutional. There was no equal protection violation because the property owners had not shown a pattern of discrimination for establishing an arbitrary discrimination. The zoning regulations had not unconstitutionally taken the property at issue because there was no practical confiscation. Finally, the town had proved its right to an injunction pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-12 where the property owners had knowingly, willingly, and in open defiance had refused to obey the zoning regulations.


OUTCOME: The court issued a judgment that granted the zoning commission's motion for an injunction, and ordered the property owners to cease from occupying the premises located in the Town of Lebanon on a year round basis because such an occupation was in violation of the zoning ordinance.

Davis v. CHRO


CV 970572855


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2371



August 24, 1998, Decided  
August 24, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision by defendant human rights commission that dismissed his complaint of discrimination and sexual harassment against defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a complaint with the human rights commission alleging that he was harassed because of his race and his sex. The employee alleged violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-58(a) and 48a-60(a)(8) and Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e. The commission dismissed the complaint after finding that there was no reasonable possibility that further investigation would result in a finding of reasonable cause against the employer. The employee sought judicial review. The court dismissed the employee's complaint. The court found that the scope of its review of the commission's decision was limited. The court was required to affirm the agency's decision unless it found that substantial rights of the person appealing were prejudiced because the administrative findings were clearly erroneous in light of the substantial evidence. The court found that there was substantial evidence in the record to support the commission's findings and conclusions that the allegations of harassment were either time barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. 46a-82(e), disposed of in an earlier complaint investigated and dismissed by the commission, or insufficient on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the employee's appeal from a decision by the human rights commission that dismissed his discrimination and sexual harassment complaint against the employer.

Beadles v. Department of Children & Families


CV 960564494


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD

DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss the plaintiff's complaint granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother brought suit against defendant Department of Children and Families (Connecticut) in regard to the placement of the mother's daughter in foster care. The Department filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mother's child was placed in foster care. While in foster care the daughter experienced an assault by one of the other children in the foster home. The mother brought suit against the Department and against the foster parent. The Department contended that it and that foster parent were protected by sovereign immunity. The court determined that the Department was protected by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The mother failed to show that the allegations fell into any of three exceptions to the doctrine. The mother failed to prove that she had the permission of the claims commissioner to sue the state. The court found that the foster parent acted within the scope of her employment and that the mother did not allege the foster parent's conduct was wanton, reckless or malicious. The court determined that the mother failed to exhaust her administrative remedies. The court granted the motion to dismiss filed by the Department and the foster parent.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Department's motion for summary judgment in the mother's suit in regard to the placement of her daughter in foster care by the Department.

Planning & Zoning Comm'n v. Karbownik


537443


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2285



August 12, 1998, Decided  
August 13, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town zoning commission sought an injunction directing and ordering defendant property owner to cease occupying certain premises on a year-round basis. The commission also sought a cash bond, attorneys' fees, and a civil penalty.


OVERVIEW: The Lebanon, Conn. Zoning Regulations § 4.4a provided that only a seasonal dwelling could be erected on a lot that was less than two acres. The property owner applied for and was issued a building permit for the construction of a seasonal dwelling on the disputed premises. From the time he received the certificate of occupancy, the property owner occupied the premises as a year-round residence, or allowed others to occupy it year-round. He sought a variance from the Zoning Board of Appeals to permit him to use the premises on a year-round basis, but the Board denied the request. The property owner contended that the zoning regulations were unconstitutional as discriminatory, as an unconstitutional taking, and as nonuniform zoning. The court rejected the property owner's claims and upheld the zoning regulation. The court found that the property owner knowingly, willingly, and in open defiance of a valid zoning regulation refused to obey it. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-12 provided that if the court found that the violation was willful, the court could allow the municipality its costs together with reasonable attorneys' fees to be taxed by the court.


OUTCOME: The court granted a mandatory injunction, attorneys' fees, a cash bond, and a civil penalty on the basis that the property owner willfully violated of the commission's zoning regulations.

 

1379 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Summitwood Assocs. Phase Iv v. Planning Comm'n


391584


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2268



August 7, 1998, Decided  
August 7, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motions to strike and the motion for summary judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant filed an action against defendant planning commission, alleging the invalidity of the planning commission's vote to deny the applicant's site plan application and seeking a writ of mandamus. The planning commission and defendant homeowners file motions to strike the applicant's complaint, alleging that one of the two persons voting to deny the application was a valid member of the planning commission for voting purposes.


OVERVIEW: The applicant filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that, assuming that the dissenter was a valid member of the planning commission, a three-member majority was necessary to deny its application, and mandamus should issue as a matter of right. The court read the allegations of the complaint in the light most favorable to the applicant. When the complaint was so read, it appeared that the dissenter was not an appointed officer at the time of the vote in question. The planning commission's assertion that he was a de facto officer could not be established without evidence. The applicant's first theory of the case survived a motion to strike. The court determined that the 2-1 vote to deny the application did not amount to a rejection of the application. Because the zoning enforcement officer lacked an interest in the outcome of the case and because his participation was unnecessary to grant the relief actually requested in the case, the planning commission's argument that he was a necessary or indispensable party was unpersuasive. In exercising its discretion whether to issue the writ, the court decided to hear evidence about the consequences of the proposed order.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motions to strike and motion for summary judgment.

Connecticut Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Anson


CV 98579841S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2195



July 30, 1998, Decided  
July 30, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Commissioner of the State of Connecticut Department of Public Works, filed a motion to dismiss the complaint filed by plaintiff contractors that sought injunctive relief. The commissioner sought dismissal of the entire complaint on the ground of sovereign immunity and argued that an injunction would interfere with the performance of important government functions.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner invited bids for a construction project that required each bidder to sign a project labor agreement (PLA). The contractors did not submit bids because of the requirement and filed a claim against the commissioner seeking injunctive relief and contending that he acted in excess of his authority under the bidding statutes set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. 4b-91et seq., that certain parts of the bidding statutes were unconstitutionally vague and unlawfully delegated authority, and that the commissioner's actions constituted an unlawful infringement of the constitutional rights to free speech and association. The commissioner filed a motion to dismiss. The court denied the motion finding that the contractors' complaint contained sufficient allegations to overcome the bar of sovereign immunity. The commissioner's decision to require each bidder to sign a PLA supported an inference of favoritism toward union contractors and a conclusion that the commissioner's decision was contrary to the policy underlying the competitive bidding statutes. Further, whether the statute contained standards to promote fairness in the bidding process required a close scrutiny of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1381 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Elm St. Builders v. Austin


CV 980407943S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2190



July 29, 1998, Decided  
July 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff builder sought a writ of mandamus to compel defendant, chairman of the town zoning commission, to refund two bonds required under Wallingford, Conn., Zoning Reg. § 8.4 as a condition of issuing a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The builder claimed that he was entitled to an immediate release of the bonds because a Connecticut municipality was not authorized by state statute to exact performance bonds, except in relation to subdivision applications, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25. All other functions of municipal government were subject to enabling legislation, and without a specific grant of the power to do so, a municipality was not entitled to elect to exact a performance bond for construction work within its borders. The court entered judgment in favor of the chairman. The town was using a modest performance bond to insure that private builders did not create problems, which the town later had to correct. Nothing in the case law or the statutes of Connecticut prohibited the imposition of a performance bond designed to achieve that end. The builder failed to show that he had any right to a release of his bonds until the town was satisfied that it need not draw on the bonds.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the chairman in the builder's action for a writ of mandamus to compel the chairman to refund the bond.

 

1382 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sylvestre v. Sylvestre


0108787


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2140



July 28, 1998, Decided  
July 28, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's Post-Judgment Motion Re: Termination of Alimony, Repayment of Alimony Payments and Attorneys Fees and Costs granted in part and denied in part; and Defendant's Contempt Citation dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband filed a motion seeking, a termination of his alimony obligation to the defendant wife as provided in a decree of dissolution of marriage, the repayment of certain alimony payments, and attorneys fees or costs. By contempt citation, the wife sought a finding that the husband was in contempt by reason of his failure to make certain payments of alimony as required by the decree.


OVERVIEW: The husband sought a termination of his alimony obligation alleging that the wife had commenced "cohabitating" with another man. Soon after he filed the motion for termination, the husband ceased making alimony payments to the wife, which prompted her issuance of a contempt citation. Because the parties did not rely on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-86(b), the court's analysis was limited to the operative effect of the decree of dissolution. The court observed the rule that a judgment, entered pursuant to a stipulation of the parties, which provided for the termination of alimony upon the recipient's cohabitation was entitled to enforcement in accordance with its terms. Proof of cohabitation alone was sufficient to terminate alimony where relief was sought pursuant to a clause in the underlying judgment that alimony was to terminate upon "cohabitation" without reference to any alteration of the cohabiting party's financial needs. Moreover, the court held that the cohabitation clause was self-executing and that it was not unconstitutional. Therefore, upon finding proof of the wife's cohabitation, the court granted the husband's motion and dismissed the contempt citation.


OUTCOME: The court granted the husband's motion for termination of his alimony obligation and ordered the wife to reimburse payments received after she commenced cohabitating with another man. However, the court denied that part of the husband's motion that sought attorneys fees or interest. The court dismissed the wife's contempt citation.

Pomarico's Serv. v. DMV


CV 960380775


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2113



July 27, 1998, Decided  
July 27, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed and the appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee sought review of the decision of defendant, State of Connecticut Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV), which found that the licensee violated the temporary transfer registration requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-61, the certificate of title requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-62(c), and the out of state inspection requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-12(g).


OVERVIEW: The licensee, a used car dealer, was charged with violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-61, 62(c), 12(g). A DMV hearing officer found that the charges were proven, imposed certain penalties, and suspended the licensee's authority to issue new registrations and temporary transfers until the licensee's representatives were retrained. On appeal, the court held that the licensee violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-61 by failing to submit to the DMV the temporary registration papers within seven days of issuance. Further, the hearing officer properly concluded that the licensee unlawfully issued temporary registrations without first obtaining safety inspections, as required by § 14-61 and Conn. Gen. Stat. 14-12(g). Moreover, the DMV's exhibit established that a certain vehicle was transferred to a purchaser before the licensee obtained the vehicle's certificate of title, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-62(c). The licensee could have called the purchaser as a witness to support his claim to the contrary. Finally, the hearing officer's findings of fact were supported by substantial evidence as required by the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that found the licensee violated temporary transfer requirements, certificate of title requirements, and out of state inspection requirements. The court dismissed the licensee's appeal.

 

1384 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Israel


FA 970716665


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2133



July 21, 1998, Decided  
July 22, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of a magistrate in Family Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) denying the state's petition on behalf of plaintiff mother to enforce a Michigan child support order against defendant father, who was a Connecticut resident. The state initiated this action under the Full Faith and Credit for Child Support Orders Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738B.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother filed a paternity action against defendant father in Michigan, where she and the child resided. Defendant's counsel sought to have the case dismissed for lack of in personam jurisdiction. The Michigan court denied defendant's motion and found that it had jurisdiction. The state of Connecticut, on behalf of the mother, sought to enforce the Michigan support order under the Full Faith and Credit for Child Support Orders Act (FFCCSOA), 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738B. The family court denied the petition and refused to enforce the Michigan support orders. On appeal, the court held that, under Michigan law, where defendant appeared specially in the Michigan action to object to the court's jurisdiction, he was precluded after an adverse ruling from collaterally attacking the court's judgment. The court found that the FFCCSOA was constitutional under both the Commerce Clause and the Tenth Amendment and held that, to the extent it conflicted with Connecticut laws on the reciprocity of child support orders, the Act preempted such laws. The court reversed the decision of the magistrate and remanded the case to the family court for a determination as to the amount of the arrearage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the family court magistrate and held that the Michigan child support orders were entitled to full faith and credit in Connecticut. Because the parties had not submitted financial information to the court, the case was remanded for a determination of the amount of the arrearage and the amount defendant should have been required to pay based on his financial status.

 

1385 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Birnberg v. ER Dev.


356495, 388506


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2045



July 15, 1998, Decided  
July 15, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: GF's motion for summary judgment (no. 106) in the GF case is denied. North American's motion for summary judgment (no. 113) in the GF case is granted. North American's motion for summary judgment (no. 132) in the Birnberg case is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgage assignors filed a foreclosure action against defendants, mortgagor and tax sale purchaser. In a second, consolidated case, plaintiff mortgage assignee sought declaratory relief and damages against defendants, town, tax collector, and tax sale purchaser. The assignee and the purchaser filed separate motions for summary judgment in the second case; the purchaser also filed a motion for summary judgment in the first case.


OVERVIEW: The cases were consolidated because they involved the same parcel of mortgaged real estate. In December 1993 the assignors assigned the mortgage to the assignee. In January 1994 the assignors filed their foreclosure action. In June 1994, the tax collector sold the property at issue to the purchaser at a tax sale. The court followed an appellate case that had rejected a due process challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-157, similar to that raised by the assignee. To successfully challenge the sale, the assignee had to show (1) lack of prior notice of the sale to it or its predecessors under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-157, and (2) that it did not learn of the sale within one year after it was made. Though the assignee lacked prior notice of the tax sale, the assignees had such notice, albeit after they had already assigned the mortgage. Further, the assignee's vice president learned of the tax sale shortly after it took place. That the vice president did not understand the legal consequences of the sale was immaterial for purposes of § 12-157. As the prima facie evidence of the purchaser's unencumbered title could not be overcome, it was entitled to summary judgment in both cases.


OUTCOME: The assignee's motion for summary judgment in the second case was denied. The purchaser's motions for summary judgment in both cases were granted.

Santini v. Connecticut Hazardous Waste Mgmt. Serv.


CV 940538646S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2029



July 13, 1998, Decided  
July 13, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed suit against defendant Connecticut Hazardous Waste Management Service and alleged that the Service's notice announcement that the landowner's property was under consideration for a low level radioactive nuclear waste facility was an unconstitutional taking of the landowner's property under Conn. Const. Art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased land, which the landowners wanted to develop into a residential community. The Connecticut Hazardous Waste Management Service announced that part of the property was one of three candidate sites for the construction of a disposal facility for low-level radioactive nuclear waste. The landowners were unable to continue with the residential development and obtain funds from sales to pay down debt. The funding for the site was never appropriated and the landowners filed suit against the Service and alleged that the designation of part of the property as one of the three finalists for acquisition as a low-level radioactive waste disposal facility was a taking of the landowners' property. The court found that there was no taking and held that because no land was physically taken and no interest in the land was extinguished or affected, the prohibition against taking of property without just compensation in Conn. Const. Art. I, § 11 did not apply to the landowners.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was no unconstitutional taking of the landowners' property.

Henderson v. Hoban


391352


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1927



July 7, 1998, Decided  
July 7, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: motion to dismiss of the defendant Hoban is granted. The motion for summary judgment of the defendant Miele is also granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sued defendants, supervisor and co-worker, alleging that they intentionally inflicted emotional distress on her. Defendants each filed a motion to dismiss and a motion for summary judgment. Defendant's asserted the claims were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The injured party sued both defendants in their individual capacities only.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was employed as an assistant clerk in the bail commission office. The injured party claimed she suffered from two traumatic brain injuries, which caused high distractibility and a decrease in her short term memory. She asserted defendants were aware of her condition and wantonly, willfully, and maliciously undertook a continual course of harassment that was both extreme and outrageous. Consequently, she suffered severe emotional distress. She did not file any affidavits in response to the supervisor's motion to dismiss. Thus, the evidence submitted in support of the supervisor's motion to dismiss was unrefuted and required dismissal of the claim. As the injured party alleged the co-worker's actions were wanton, willful, malicious, extreme, and outrageous, sovereign immunity did not bar her claims. However, the episodes related in the injured party's complaint neither individually nor collectively rose to the unusual degree necessary to maintain an action for intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OUTCOME: The supervisor's motion to dismiss was granted. The co-worker's motion for summary judgment was granted.

State v. Webb


HHDCR 50492


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1911



July 1, 1998, Decided  
July 7, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Webb, 252 Conn. 128, 750 A.2d 448, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 19 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Webb, 238 Conn. 389, 680 A.2d 147, 1996 Conn. LEXIS 301 (1996)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's challenge to the state's method of execution under the state constitution denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the state supreme court, the trial court considered defendant's challenge to his execution by lethal injection after defendant contended it constituted cruel and unusual punishment under the Connecticut Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court remanded defendant's case to allow him to challenge his execution by lethal injection as cruel and unusual punishment under the state constitution. At a hearing, the State called as a witness an anesthesiologist who attested to the lack of pain associated with the proper implementation of the written procedure, the procedural safeguards involved, and the minimal skill and training actually necessary to carry out the procedure. The defense called as witnesses persons who either participated in a task force to establish a procedure for carrying out death by lethal injection, or were anticipated participants in the procedure. Additionally, the defense offered a transcript of the testimony of a doctor from a prior hearing on the same issue. That doctor attested to the risks attendant to a procedure for implementing an execution by lethal injection, the potential for pain associated with those risks, and the failure of an administrative directive to address those risks. After the hearing, the trial court found defendant had not met his burden of showing the procedure violated the state constitution, and thus concluded his challenge should be denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant's constitutional challenge to the State's method of execution was denied.

Bilco Co. v. Carey Precast Concrete Co.


0405960

1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1751

June 19, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff domestic corporation brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant foreign corporation, seeking a declaration of the domestic corporation's rights concerning a license agreement between the two corporations. The foreign corporation filed a motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the domestic corporation licensed to the foreign corporation the non-exclusive right to use all of the domestic corporation's knowledge pertaining to the sale, manufacture, and installation of certain basement entrances. The court noted that a dispute arose concerning the foreign corporation's ability to service its exclusive area. The domestic corporation brought the instant action, seeking to clarify its rights under the licensing agreement. The foreign corporation asserted that the court did not have personal jurisdiction. The court granted the foreign corporation's motion to dismiss, holding that while the foreign corporation had constitutionally sufficient minimum contacts with Connecticut, the assertion of personal jurisdiction over the foreign corporation would not have comported with the constitutional principles of due process. The court said that asserting personal jurisdiction over the foreign corporation would not have comported with traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice because virtually all of the critical factors necessary for the adjudication of the action were connected to Ohio.


OUTCOME: The court granted the foreign corporation's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction.

Smith v. Deep River Planning & Zoning Comm'n

June 17, 1998, Decided

DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed from a decision of defendant zoning board which granted defendant applicant's petition for a special permit and a subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The applicant owned land and he filed an application with the zoning board for a special permit and to subdivide his land into residential building lots. The zoning board granted the application and the citizens appealed, arguing that by issuing the special permit and approving the subdivision application the zoning board acted arbitrarily, unreasonably, capriciously, illegally, and in abuse of its discretion. The zoning board argued that the citizens failed to exhaust their administrative remedies by appealing the granting of the special permit directly to the court. The court ruled that if an adequate administrative remedy existed, it must be exhausted before the court obtained jurisdiction to act in the matter, and that exhaustion was required even in cases where the agency's jurisdiction over the proposed activity was challenged. The court dismissed the appeal, concluding that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal from the decision granting the special permit and subdivision was dismissed.

Ross v. Ross


FA 970162587S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2248



June 17, 1998, Decided  
August 10, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Annulment requested in first Count of plaintiff's complaint denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband filed a complaint in two counts. The first count sought a decree annulling the marriage and the second count sought a dissolution of the marriage. Defendant wife then filed a one-count cross complaint, also seeking a decree annulling the marriage. The parties both requested an annulment on the first count of the husband's complaint.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married in a ceremony that took place at the husband's home in Connecticut. The home was totally within the boundaries of Connecticut. A priest of the Episcopal Church, who was known to the parties, performed the marriage ceremony. The priest was rector of a church in New York. Both parties claimed that there was a deficiency in obtaining the necessary ecclesiastical permission for the priest to perform the marriage ceremony in Connecticut. The court concluded that civil law, not canon law, determined the solemnization of the marriage ceremony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-22. There was no statutory requirement that the clergyman performing the marriage ceremony had to be working in the ministry in Connecticut. Therefore, the priest was an authorized person to perform marriages in Connecticut. In addition, there was no evidence that the ceremony he performed was deficient according to the traditions of the Episcopal Church. The court concluded that the case was a request to examine the internal workings of Episcopal Church canon law, and the court would not apply canon law.


OUTCOME: The annulment requested in the first count of the husband's complaint was denied.

 

1392 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibbs


CR 9389935


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1775



June 15, 1998, Decided  
June 17, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The defendant's third amended challenge to the jury array is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information with capital felony. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 842, defendant challenged the jury array. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of capital felony and two counts of murder. The State thereafter elected to withdraw its claim for the death penalty and no penalty phase hearing took place. The court sentenced defendant to life in prison without the possibility of release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the jury array violated the jury summoning statutes, federal and state constitutional rights, and the right to heightened procedural protection including the right to reliable sentencing proceedings. The court stated that in Connecticut, the jury administrator prepared a master list from a larger pool of names called the source list annually for each judicial district. The voter list and motor vehicle list comprised the source list. The master list was generated from town voter's registries and the state motor vehicle list of licensed drivers, minus the duplicates. Defendant focused on three factors relating to the representation of Hispanics: (1) English ability requirement; (2) undeliverables; and (3) no-shows. The court found that defendant failed to state a prima facie case of violation of the U.S. Const. amend. VI, equal protection, or due process. In addition, defendant's arguments with regard to heightened protection, jury summoning statutes, and independent state constitutional protection were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's challenge to the jury array.

 

1393 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Kucej v. Zoning Comm'n


CV 950322558


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT FAIRFIELD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1673



June 12, 1998, Decided  
June 12, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the decision of the Stratford Zoning Commission dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner appealed from a decision of appellee Zoning Commission of the Town of Stratford (Connecticut), which denied the owner's application for a special use for his property.


OVERVIEW: After acquiring title to the property, which contained two rental units, the owner undertook to have installed on the third floor a new kitchen and bathroom, where none had previously existed. The town ordered the property owner to cease and desist from installing the kitchen and bathroom. The order was the subject of a civil action, which ended with a stipulated judgment whereby it was agreed that the property owner was to apply for a special use and that he would be bound by the outcome of that application. The zoning commission denied the property owner's application. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the commission did not act arbitrarily in failing to grant the property owner's application for a special use, in that its decision in the matter was not predetermined. The court further held that the commission's denial did not amount to an unconstitutional confiscation of the owner's property. The owner was not losing any of the rental income that was available to the owner of that house at the time he acquired it. He was merely being limited, as a consequence of the commission's action, from increasing the revenue he hoped to receive.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's appeal from the decision of the zoning commission.

 

1394 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Boudreau v. City of Middletown


CV 970083396S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1645



June 9, 1998, Decided  
June 9, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike granted as to second count. Motion to strike denied as to the fifth count and as to the claims set forth in the fourth count at paragraphs 19(a) and (b).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor child and her mother filed an action against defendant police officers and town that alleged negligent interference with the custodial rights of the mother, deprivation of the minor child's constitutional rights to security in her person and in her house as well as her right to liberty and equal protection of the laws, and negligent supervision of the police officers. The police officers and the town filed a motion to strike.


OVERVIEW: The complaint was filed after the minor child was taken by the police officers after the father of the minor child went to the police department and stated that he had been given temporary custody of the minor child. The minor child and her mother's complaint alleged only negligence and neither an absence of custodial rights nor knowledge that the father of the minor child did not have custodial rights and the court determined that the mother failed to state a cognizable cause of action for interference with custodial rights. The court further determined that both the minor child and her mother asserted that they were deprived of their right to equal protection of the law but they did not explain any way in which they suffered a deprivation distinct from the claimed seizure. Finally, the court denied the motion to strike as to the minor child and her mother's indemnification claim against the town. The determination of the minor child and her mother's compliance with the notice requirement provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-465 must await factual development.


OUTCOME: The court granted the police officers and town's motion to strike as to all counts requested except the count that related to indemnification and a portion of the count that relied upon the state constitution.

 

1395 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Champagne v. Lewis


CV 960565267


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD - NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1658



June 9, 1998, Decided  
June 9, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual filed an action under the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166 et seq., seeking review of a decision of defendant, the State of Connecticut Psychiatric Security Review Board (PSRB), which ordered that the individual remain confined at a hospital for care, custody, and treatment under maximum security conditions.


OVERVIEW: The individual was charged with murder. He was found not guilty by reason of a mental disease or defect and was committed to the custody of the Commissioner of Mental Health. The PSRB held a hearing to review the individual's status and ordered that he remain confined at a hospital for care, custody, and treatment under maximum security conditions. The individual sought review of the portion of the PSRB's order requiring that he be confined under maximum security conditions. The court dismissed the appeal, concluding that it lacked jurisdiction to review the PSRB's decision. The court noted that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-597, it had jurisdiction to review PSRB decisions as to conditional release or confinement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-584 and temporary leave decisions under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-587. The court found that the decision to confine the individual under maximum security conditions was not a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-584 or Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-587 decision and, therefore, that it did not have jurisdiction to review that portion of the PSRB's order. Further, the court found that the individual was not entitled to review under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-186(f).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the individual's appeal.

J&N Enters. v. Shelton Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV 970058771S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1598



June 4, 1998, Decided  
June 4, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subdivision developer sought review of a decision of appellee Shelton Planning and Zoning Commission (Connecticut), which unilaterally modified the parties' agreement concerning the subdivision developer's proposed subdivision plan. The subdivision developer had filed an application with the commission for approval of the plan.


OVERVIEW: The subdivision developer filed an application with the commission for approval of a subdivision plan of a tract of land. The representatives of the subdivision developer and the commission reached a tentative agreement regarding the plan, subject to submission of the agreement to the commission as a whole for its approval. Thereafter, the commission unilaterally modified the agreement. The subdivision developer appealed the commission's decision. The court sustained the appeal and remanded the matter to the commission. The court held that commission's approval of the plan as modified was not proper because the modifications constituted a major revision of the plan as submitted.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the subdivision developer's appeal of the commission's unilateral modification of the agreement between the parties related to the proposed subdivision plan. The court also remanded the matter to the commission.
