FDIC v. Crystal


CV 910502615


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD-NEW BRITAIN, AT HARTFORD


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1449



May 20, 1998, Decided  
May 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC), as receiver for a bank, appealed the decision of defendant, Commissioner of Revenue Services of the State of Connecticut, seeking a refund of taxes and interest paid pursuant to the Connecticut Corporation Business Tax (CCBT), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-213 through 12-242.


OVERVIEW: The CCBT required corporate taxpayers to include interest income received from federal, state, and local bonds as part of their gross income. Based on the CCBT, the Commissioner assessed a deficiency against the bank, and the bank paid the taxes and interest due thereunder. As receiver for the bank, the FDIC sought a refund of the taxes paid, but the Commissioner denied the refund. In its appeal, the FDIC contended that the CCBT discriminated against the FDIC as a holder of federal obligations and that the Commissioner failed to issue timely notice of the deficiency assessment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-233. The court dismissed the FDIC's appeal. The FDIC failed to raise its discrimination claim at the audit and thereby deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction. The court then held that the Commissioner's notice of deficiency to the bank fell within the applicable three-year statute of limitation as evidenced by computer records and supporting testimony.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the FDIC's appeal.

 

1398 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


ATC Pshp. v. Town of Windham


CV 950248230S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1490



May 20, 1998, Decided  
May 19, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion to strike granted by ATC Pshp. v. Town of Windham, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 7 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 4, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Northeast Econ. Alliance v. ATC Pshp., 1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1057 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 16, 1998)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a motion to strike plaintiff's second amended revised complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed new complaints in an attempt to distinguish the action from one that would fall under a decision on a previous motion to strike, which was stayed. The basis for plaintiff's claim was that the trial court did not address substantive due process claims. The court found that the prior decision was applicable to the second amended revised complaint. The essential action was unaltered: it claimed an unconstitutional "taking" of property without just compensation. The stay was terminated as to the original decision, and the decision was applied to the Second Amended Revised Complaint. Defendants alleged that plaintiff had not been deprived of its property without due process because the property was taken after a judicial condemnation action. Also, they claimed that due process was met by plaintiff's pending lawsuits, one for replevin and the other an appeal of the taking. The court held that the fact that defendants went through a process did not mean that the value was "just compensation." The plaintiff stated a claim for deprivation of just compensation. However, plaintiff had not yet exhausted its remedies, and defendants were entitled to have the complaint stricken.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the second amended revised complaint was granted.

 

1399 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cummings


CR 939390935


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1560



May 7, 1998, Decided  
May 7, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion to Resentence denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of stalking, harassment, disorderly conduct, and criminal violation of a protective order. Defendant was sentenced to seven years, three months, suspended after four years. The sentence on the disorderly conduct was three months. Defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct was reversed, but the other convictions were affirmed. Defendant filed a motion for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of stalking in the first degree, stalking in the second degree, two counts of harassment in the second degree, disorderly conduct, and criminal violation of a protective order. Defendant was sentenced to seven years, three months, suspended after four years. The sentence on the disorderly conduct was three months. After serving several months of incarceration defendant was release on an appellate bond. On appeal, defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct was reversed. Defendant's convictions were affirmed in all other respects. Defendant filed a motion for resentencing, which was opposed by the State who sought to have the original sentence imposed less the three months for the vacated disorderly conduct count. The court conducted a post-sentencing hearing and defendant showed that he had married and was successfully employed. The court held that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-39(a), it did not have authority to reduce defendant's sentence because the original sentence was longer that three years. The court held that it was bound by the appellate mandate that affirmed the other convictions in all respects.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to resentence and held it was bound by the remand. Because the sentence was longer than three years, the court did not have authority to reduce the sentence that was originally imposed.

 

1400 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lepri


CR 97258439


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1257



May 4, 1998, Decided  
May 5, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to suppress denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury case, defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence obtained in a search of his home on the ground that the magistrate issuing the search warrant relied upon an affidavit that contained stale information and to suppress the evidence found at his neighbor's home on the ground that the warrantless seizures there violated his constitutionally protected expectation of privacy.


OVERVIEW: Based on an affidavit indicating that minors complained of defendant's sexual involvement with them, a search warrant was issued for pornographic video tapes and sexually explicit materials. Numerous items were seized from defendant's home. The police received information that defendant was seen removing items from his neighbor's home. After the neighbor consented to a search of her home and yard, the police seized garbage bags, a box, and briefcases and searched those containers. Defendant sought to suppress the evidence seized from his home on the ground of staleness, as the warrant authorized a search for videos which were "easily transferable," but was based on activity which took place weeks earlier. The court held that the issuing judge could reasonably have determined there was probable cause to believe that defendant was engaged in on-going pedophilia and that associated materials would be found at his home. Defendant did not have standing to challenge the search of the garbage bag, the briefcases, and the open box of videos obtained from the neighbor's home, as defendant abandoned any reasonable expectation of privacy in them by telling the neighbor to say they were hers.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to suppress.
